Salah — Prayer

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Hand Placement in the Qawmah
Expanding ruling of hand placement with manner, time, and intra-Hanafi dispute on qawmah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion of 'qiyam lahu qarar' to evaluate whether hand placement is sunnah in the qawmah and explain the evidence for both sides of the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
The qawmah is excluded from hand placement because it lacks stability and prescribed dhikr, despite the Sahibayn's view that it contains dhikr.

While the previous lesson established the general rule that hand placement is sunnah in stable standings with prescribed dhikr, the qawmah (standing after ruku' before sujud) became a point of contention among the early Hanafi masters. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani held that placement is only during recitation, not during the qawmah. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argued that placement is sunnah in the qawmah because it contains prescribed dhikr (tasmi' and tahmid). In this lesson, we will dissect this intra-Hanafi dispute, examine the evidence, and understand why the later school favored the view of Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the contested issue
Is it sunnah to place hands in the qawmah? Identify that this is a dispute within the Hanafi school.
Imam Muhammad says no; Sahibayn say yes.
2
Identify the two positions
Imam Muhammad: placement is not sunnah in qawmah. Sahibayn: placement is sunnah in qawmah.
Both are early authorities within the school.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's dalil
They rely on the general command from the hadith of Ibn Abbas that placement is sunnah in all standings, and they argue that the qawmah contains prescribed dhikr (tasmi' or tahmid).
Their view is also supported by some later authorities like al-Multaqat.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response (Imam Muhammad's view)
The dominant view particularizes the general command: the qawmah lacks stability (qarar) and the dhikr is part of the transition, not the standing. Evidence from al-Qunyah shows that tasmi' is not repeated if missed until standing straight.
The wisdom of placement (preventing blood gathering) only applies to prolonged standings.
5
Determine the tarjih
The later school (e.g., al-Hadadi, al-Qunyah) favors no placement in qawmah, unless it is prolonged (tawil).
The mufta bihi is to not place, but the Sahibayn's view is also considered valid.

And he places his right hand on his left under his navel, opening (with du'a) and seeking refuge silently for recitation, so the one who is preceded (masbuq) does not perform it. And the apparent statement of the commentator is to prefer it, and in Sharh al-Munyah it is the more appropriate, and it is preferable to give weight to permissibility because it is pure remembrance, as evidence by the basmalah on the slaughtered animal with the condition of pure remembrance therein due to His saying 'So mention the name of Allah upon them when lined up' [22:36] meaning purely. His statement (and he places his right on his left under his navel as we have previously mentioned, and he did not mention the manner of placement because it was not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah. And there is a difference of opinion on it, and the chosen view is that he takes the wrist with the little finger and thumb because taking necessitates placement and not vice versa, and this is because reports differed: some mention placement and some mention taking, so combining them acting on both evidences is better. And the author also did not mention the time of placement; so in Zahir al-Riwayah its time is when he finishes the takbir, and it is a sunnah of a standing that has stability (qiyam lahu qarar) in which there is prescribed dhikr, so he places during the praise (thana'), and in qunut, and the takbirs of the funeral prayer, and it was said it is sunnah only during recitation, so he does not place in these places. And they all agree that it is not sunnah for the one who prays sitting. Fatawa al-Marghinani that it is the correct one, then he said: so the preponderant regarding basmalah is non-acceptance, and the more preponderant i.e., in al-Bahr is acceptance. The author's statement 'and he places his right on his left' – said in al-Nahr: meaning palm on palm, and it is said on the wrist. Al-Ayni said it, and his statement admits both possibilities, and in it is an indication of explaining the manner; so what is in al-Bahr that he did not explain it due to its absence in Zahir al-Riwayah is subject to consideration. And from the second he grasps the left wrist with the right hand, and al-Hindawani chose it. And Muhammad said: he places them such that the wrist is in the middle of the palm. Al-Sarakhsi said: many scholars considered it good to take the wrist with the thumb and little finger and place the rest so that it combines between the two reported (narrations) of taking and placing in the sunnah, and it is the chosen view. End quote. In Mi'raj al-Dirayah after attributing this statement to al-Mujtaba, al-Zahirah, and al-Mabsut with the addition 'so as to act upon both hadiths and schools out of precaution', he said: and it was said this is outside the schools and hadiths, so acting upon it is not precaution. End quote. His statement: 'so it is a sunnah of a standing that has stability' – al-Ramli said: it is explicit that it is not sunnah for the one who prays sitting, and I have not seen anyone draw attention to this, and people are heedless of it. And if it is not sunnah for him, how should he place? Apparently he places his hands on his thighs and spreads his fingers as he does in the first and second sitting. Then I saw in Sharh al-Wiqayah called Tawfiq al-Inayah in explaining his statement 'and he places his right' etc., the picture of the issue: the praying person places his right palm on his left palm and forms a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist in the state of standing. End quote. So his statement 'in the state of standing' implies that he does not do that in the state of sitting – consider. And I saw in the books of the Shafi'is that he does in sitting as he does in standing. End quote. I said: his student Sheikh Alauddin al-Haskafi mentioned something similar and said: I have not seen it. Then he said: then I saw in Majma' al-Anhur that what is meant by 'standing' is more general because the sitting person does likewise. His statement: 'and they all agree' etc. – said in al-Nahr: there is consideration regarding the consensus. It was mentioned in al-Siraj from al-Nasafi, al-Hakim, al-Jurjani, and al-Fadli that he leans in the qawmah (standing after ruku'), the funeral prayer, and the extra takbirs of the Eid; it is appropriate for what the commentator narrated from some that it is sunnah for every standing. And Shaykh al-Islam narrated in one place that according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he holds (i.e., places hands) in the qawmah that is between ruku' and sujud because in that standing there is prescribed dhikr, i.e., tasmi' (sami'a Allahu liman hamidah) or tahmid. And he singled out the two's statement because according to Muhammad it is sunnah during recitation, and according to the two it is Zahir al-Riwayah as in al-Siraj. And this reasoning with regard to the person led by the imam and the imam himself is precluded because it is not sunnah to place in the standing that intervenes between ruku' and sujud because it has no stability and no recitation in it. By this, what is in Fath al-Qadir is refuted: that the letting go in the qawmah according to the mentioned criterion requires that there is no prescribed dhikr in it; but this is only complete if it is said that tahmid and tasmi' are not sunnah in it but rather in the very transition to it, but this is contrary to the apparent texts, and the reality is that rarely does tasmi' occur except in the standing while combining between them. End quote. Because you know that their statement is only about qiyam that has stability. And in al-Qunyah: if he leaves tasmi' until he stands up straight, he does not do it, just as if he did not say the takbir while bending until he ruku' or sujud, he abandons it. And one should memorize this and observe each thing in its place. End quote. And it is explicit that the qawmah has no prescribed dhikr. And it is mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in Sharh Kitab al-Salah that he lets go (i.e., does not place hands) in the qawmah between ruku' and sujud according to the two's statement just as is the view of Muhammad. And in another place he mentioned that according to the two's statement one should hold (place hands) because in this standing there is prescribed dhikr, i.e., tasmi' or tahmid; and upon this the author of al-Multaqat relied. End quote. And it supports what the researcher examined earlier. And upon this, that tasmi' or tahmid is only sunnah in the state of transition; yes, for the one praying alone it is based on that he combines them (tasmi' and tahmid), as he says 'Rabbana laka al-hamd' when he stands upright, according to the apparent answer which is correct as in al-Qunyah. And we do not admit that this standing has absolutely no stability because of their statement that the one praying a supererogatory prayer, even if it is sunnah, it is sunnah for him to perform supplications like 'Fill the heavens and the earth...' after tahmid, and 'Allahumma ighfir li warhamni' between the two prostrations. And know that al-Hadadi restricted the letting go (of hands) in what has no prescribed dhikr to when the standing is not prolonged; but if it is prolonged he holds (places hands). And in al-Khulasa: likewise he lets go in Zahir al-Riwayah in every standing that has no dhikr and is not long; and this implies that the previous criterion should be increased with 'or is long' – and Allah is the granter of success. End quote. Sheikh Isma'il said after that: the commentary of Miskin narrated the restriction with 'long'. Al-Birjandi said: placement of the hand in the mentioned manner is sunnah in every standing in which dhikr is prescribed, whether the dhikr is obligatory, obligatory (wajib), or sunnah; and what is meant by 'prescribed' is legislated. And in Sharh Ibn Malik: so he places in the mentioned states according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because what is narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) regarding the sunnah of placement is general in the states of standing, but the qawmah from ruku' is particularized from those states due to its lack of extension, so what remains besides it remains on the original. And similar is in Ghurar al-Adhkar and al-Manba'. And in the first two also in explaining the statement of Muhammad: because the legislation of placement is to prevent the blood from gathering in the fingertips, and that only occurs in the state where prolongation is sunnah, i.e., the state of recitation. End quote. And apparently this extension and prolongation is what is meant by the statement of al-Bahr 'has stability (luhu qarar)' – end of his words. Then he objected to al-Nahr regarding its transmission from al-Fadli about leaning that it is not correct; rather, what is in al-Siraj from him is that he lets go in the mentioned (situations). So the correct is not to mention him together with al-Nasafi and those after him. End quote. This is his objection to the reasoning in the statement of Shaykh al-Islam 'because in this standing there is prescribed dhikr' etc., and his interpretation of it for the one praying alone is not apparent because tasmi' and tahmid are remembrance with 'or' which denotes one of two things, and the one praying alone performs them both according to what he mentioned, so his submission (i.e., that it is only for the mufrid) is not correct even for the mufrid. Rather, the apparent is that it agrees with what was discussed in Fath al-Qadir as the author of al-Bahr said. So the statement of Shaykh al-Islam 'i.e., tasmi'' – meaning if it were

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the ruling of placing hands during prayer. It opens by clarifying the manner of placement: the right hand is placed on the left under the navel. The author notes that the manner (kayfiyyah) is not specified in Zahir al-Riwayah, and there is a difference of opinion. The preferred view among later scholars is to grasp the left wrist with the thumb and little finger, while placing the remaining fingers on the forearm. This combines the two narrations (some mention 'placement', some mention 'grasping') and is chosen by al-Sarakhsi and many others. As for the time of placement, the passage explains that in Zahir al-Riwayah it is sunnah to place hands immediately after the takbir, and continues until the end of the standing position in which prescribed dhikr occurs. Thus, placement is done during the opening supplication (thana'), during qunut, and during the takbirs of the funeral prayer. However, there is a view that it is only sunnah during recitation (qira'ah), so one would not place in those other positions. The passage then extensively discusses the specific case of the qawmah (standing after ruku' before sujud). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Imam Muhammad, placement in the qawmah is not sunnah because it is a brief standing without recitation and without prescribed dhikr (since tasmi' and tahmid are part of the transition, not the standing itself). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions, Sahibayn), placement is sunnah in the qawmah because there is prescribed dhikr (tasmi' or tahmid). The passage weighs the evidence, quoting from various later authorities such as Shaykh al-Islam and al-Multaqat, and concludes that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the qawmah is a standing without stability (qarar) and without prescribed dhikr, so hands are not placed. The passage also clarifies that one who prays sitting does not place hands at all, as the sunnah is only for qiyam that has stability. Finally, there is a discussion of whether the qawmah can be considered prolonged (tawil) – if it is prolonged, placement becomes sunnah even according to the hesitant views. The overall ruling: the sunnah of placing hands applies in every standing position that has prescribed dhikr and is extended; brief stances like the qawmah are excluded.

Key Terms
وضع (wad'): Placement of the right hand on the left during prayer; a sunnah act with differing opinions on manner and timing.
قومة (qawmah): The brief standing after rising from ruku' before going into sujud; a position where hand placement is disputed.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani; the most authoritative transmission of Hanafi rulings.
سنة قيام له قرار (sunnatu qiyamin lahu qarar): A sunnah that applies to a standing position that has stability (i.e., is not a brief transition) and contains prescribed dhikr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the primary reason the dominant Hanafi view excludes the qawmah from hand placement?
A) The qawmah has no prescribed dhikr at all.
B) The qawmah is not a standing (qiyam) but a bowing position.
C) The qawmah lacks stability (qarar) and the dhikr in it is part of transition.
D) The Sahibayn agreed with Imam Muhammad on this point.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is not to place hands in the qawmah because it lacks stability and its dhikr is transitional; this differs from the Sahibayn's view and from other schools.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Placing Hands in the Standing Between Ruku' and Sujud: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the ruling on wad' in the qawma and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wad' in the qawma and explain the basis of the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The qawma lacks qarar, so wad' is not sunnah – unless the standing is prolonged.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: should you place your hands (wad') during the brief standing between ruku' and sujud? The majority holds that it is not sunnah because this standing has no settled recitation (qarar). However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it sunnah if the standing is prolonged or if the tasmii' and tahmid are recited in it. Let's explore the reasoning and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act in question is wad' (placing right hand over left) in the qawma (standing between ruku' and sujud). The dispute is whether it is sunnah or not.
The qawma is typically brief, unlike other standings in prayer.
2
Understand the Hanafi position and its dalil
The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that wad' is not sunnah because the qawma lacks qarar (settled posture) and has no prescribed recitation. The tasmii' and tahmid are part of the transition, not the standing itself.
Al-Qunyah states that if one delays tasmii' until fully upright, he does not repeat it, confirming no sunnah dhikr in the qawma.
3
Examine the opposing view of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that wad' becomes sunnah if the standing is prolonged or if one recites tasmii' or tahmid in it. Some later scholars (e.g., author of al-Multaqat) rely on their view.
Their argument: Since tasmii' and tahmid are sunnah in that position, the standing has a sunnah dhikr, so wad' is also sunnah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that tasmii' and tahmid are part of the rising (intiqal), not the settled standing. The early masters (Abu Hanifa and his two disciples) agreed that wad' is not sunnah in the qawma, as evidenced by the statement 'Ajmalu anna la yusanna al-wad' fi al-qiyam al-mutakhalil'.
The passage cites al-Haddadi who qualifies: if the standing is not prolonged, one lets hands hang; if prolonged, one places.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the condition of prolongation
The mufta bihi (relied-upon view) is that wad' is not sunnah in the qawma based on zahir al-riwayah. However, if the standing is prolonged (e.g., for a long supplication), some scholars adopt wad'. The practical ruling: leave hands hanging, unless you follow the Sahibayn or prolong the standing.
The tarjih is by the majority of early Hanafi imams, and the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq supports this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنه لا يسن الوضع في القيام المتخلل بين الركوع والسجود لأنه لا قرار له ولا قراءة فيه، وبهذا اندفع ما في فتح القدير من أن الإرسال في القومة بناء على الضابط المذكور يقتضي . ليس فيها ذكر مسنون وإنما يتم إذا قيل بأن التحميد والتسميع ليس سنة فيها بل في نفس الانتقال إليها لكنه خلاف ظاهر النصوص والواقع أنه قل ما يقع التسميع إلا في القيام حالة الجمع بينهما اهـ . لما علمت أن كلامهم إنما هو في قيام له قرار. وفي القنية: ولو ترك التسميع حتى استوى قائماً لا يأتي به كما لو لم يكبر حالة الانحطاط حتى ركع أو سجد تركه، ويجب أن يحفظ هذا ويراعى كل شيء في محله اهـ. وهو صريح في أن القومة ليس فيها ذكر مسنون. وذكر في شرح منية المصلي أن شيخ الإسلام ذكر في شرح كتاب الصلاة أنه يرسل في القومة التي تكون بين الركوع والسجود على قولهما كما هو قول محمد. وذكر موضع آخر أن على قولهما يعتمد فإن في هذا القيام ذكراً مسنوناً وهو التسميع أو. التحميد، وعلى هذا مشى صاحب الملتقط .اهـ. وهو مساعد لما بحثه المحقق آنفاً. وعلى هذا في عن أن التسميع أو التحميد إنما هو سنة خالة الانتقال نعم هو في حق المنفرد بناء على أنه يجمع بينهما مسلم لما أنه يقول ربنا لك الحمد» إذا استوى قائماً في الجواب الظاهر وهو الصحيح كما في القنية، ولا نسلم أن هذا قيام لا قرار له مطلقاً لقولهم : إن مصلي النافلة ولو سنة يسن له أن يأتي بالأدعية الواردة نحو «ملء السموات والأرض إلى آخره بعد التحميد واللهم اغفر لي وارحمني بين السجدتين. واعلم أن الحدادي قيد الإرسال فيما ليس فيه ذكر مسنون بما إذا لم يطل القيام، أما إذا أطاله فيعتمد. وفي الخلاصة : وكذا يرسل في ظاهر الرواية في كل قيام لا ذكر فيه ولا يطول، وهذا يقتضي أن يزاد في الضابط السابق أو يطول والله تعالى الموفق .اهـ.
That it is not sunnah to place the hands in the standing that intervenes between bowing and prostrating, because there is no settled position (qarar) for it and no recitation in it. And by this is repelled what is in Fath al-Qadir, that the letting go (irsal) in the qawma, based on the mentioned principle, implies... It does not have a sunnah dhikr, but that is only established if it is said that the tahmid and tasmii' are not sunnah in it, but rather in the transition itself, but that contradicts the apparent texts and the reality is that tasmii' rarely occurs except in the standing while combining between them. Since you know that their speech is only about a standing that has qarar. In al-Qunyah: If one leaves the tasmii' until he is fully upright, he does not come with it, just as if he did not say the takbir while going down until he bowed or prostrated, he leaves it, and it is necessary to memorize this and observe everything in its place. It is explicit that the qawma does not have a sunnah dhikr. In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in Sharh Kitab al-Salah that he lets the hands hang (yursil) in the qawma between bowing and prostrating according to the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as is the view of Muhammad. He mentioned elsewhere that reliance is on their view, because in this standing there is a sunnah dhikr, which is tasmii' or tahmid, and the author of al-Multaqat followed this. This supports what the muhaqqiq investigated earlier. And upon this... that tasmii' or tahmid is only sunnah in the state of transition. Yes, regarding the one praying alone (munfarid), based on his combining both, it is granted that he says 'Rabbana laka al-hamd' when he is upright in the apparent answer, and that is correct as in al-Qunyah. And we do not concede that this standing absolutely has no qarar, because of their statement that the one performing a supererogatory prayer, even if it is a sunnah prayer, it is sunnah for him to come with the reported supplications like 'Mil' al-samawati wa al-ard' etc. after the tahmid, and 'Allahumma ighfir li wa arhamni' between the two prostrations. Know that al-Haddadi restricted the letting go (irsal) in what has no sunnah dhikr to when the standing is not prolonged; if he prolongs it, he adopts (the placing). In al-Khulasah: Similarly, he lets go (yursil) in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) in every standing that has no dhikr and is not prolonged. This necessitates adding 'or is prolonged' to the previous principle. And Allah is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage discusses whether it is sunnah to place the right hand over the left during the standing between ruku' and sujud (qawma). The author states that the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that it is not sunnah because this standing is brief and has no settled recitation (qarar). However, there is a dispute within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that if the standing is prolonged, or if one considers the tasmii' and tahmid as part of the standing itself, then placing hands becomes sunnah. The text cites al-Haddadi who qualifies that the non-placing applies only when the standing is not prolonged; if prolonged, one should place. The author also mentions that the munfarid (person praying alone) combines tasmii' and tahmid, but the tasmii' is part of the rising, not the settled standing. The passage reconciles the various positions by noting that the general principle is that placing hands is sunnah in any standing that contains sunnah dhikr and is prolonged, but the qawma is typically brief, so it is excepted.

Key Terms
القيام المتخلل / القومة (al-qiyam al-mutakhalil / al-qawma): The standing position between ruku' and sujud after rising from bowing
الوضع (al-wad'): Placing the right hand over the left during standing in prayer
القرار (al-qarar): Settled state or stability in a position, especially with regard to recitation

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, why is placing hands not sunnah in the standing between ruku' and sujud?
A) Because it is a brief standing with no settled position and no recitation
B) Because the Prophet never did it
C) Because it invalidates the prayer
D) Because it is forbidden by ijma

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, wad' in the qawma is not sunnah because the standing lacks qarar, unless the standing is prolonged.

Condition for Placing Hands: Prolonged Standing with Dhikr
Refines the ruling on wad' by adding the condition of prolongation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when placing hands is sunnah in prayer and identify the condition of prolongation that exempts the qawma.

Core Idea
Placing hands is sunnah only in prolonged standings with dhikr; the qawma is exempted due to brevity.

The general ruling states that placing hands is sunnah in any standing position where dhikr is recited. However, this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq introduces a crucial refinement: the standing must be prolonged. This narrows the scope and explains why the qawma (standing after ruku') is excluded. We will trace the reasoning from the primary texts and the intra-Hanafi debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline ruling
Recall that the sunnah of placing hands (wad') generally applies to all standings during prayer based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas. This is the starting point before any refinement.
2
Recognize the refinement: condition of prolongation
The text introduces the condition that the standing must be prolonged (tawil). This is derived from the purpose of wad': to prevent blood from pooling in the fingertips, which only occurs during prolonged standing.
Al-Barjandi says wad' is sunnah in every standing with dhikr, but others restrict it to prolonged standings.
3
Locate the exemption of the qawma
The qawma (brief standing after ruku') is excluded because it is not prolonged. The hadith's generality is thus specified by this practical reasoning.
Ibn Malik's commentary explains that the qawma lacks extension (imtidad).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Some later scholars (like al-Barjandi) hold that wad' is sunnah in any standing with dhikr regardless of length, but the majority condition prolongation. The text resolves that the mufta bihi is the latter view.
The ijma' of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that wad' is not sunnah in the qawma, but the ikhtilaf among later mashayikh is about other standings.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative position is that wad' is sunnah in prolonged standings (e.g., qiyam al-qira'ah) and in any standing where the dhikr is prolonged, but not in the brief qawma unless the imam deliberately prolongs it.
The text favors the view that wad' is restricted to tawil, as per the reasoning in Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ اسمعيل بعد : نقله شرح مسكين التقييد بالطويل، قال البرجندي: وضع اليد على الوجه المذكور سنة في كل قيام شرع فيه ذكر، فرضاً كان الذكر أو واجباً أو سنة، والمراد بالمسنون المشروع. وفي شرح ابن ملك : فيضع في الأحوال المذكورة عندهما لأن ما روي عن ابن عباس رضي الله تعالى عنهما في سنة الوضع عام في أحوال القيام لكن خصت القومة من الركوع من تلك الأحوال لعدم امتدادها فبقي ما عداها على الأصل، ومثله في غرر الأذكار والمنبع، وفي الأولين أيضاً في تعليل قول محمد لأن شرع الوضع للصيانة عن اجتماع الدم في رؤوس الأصابع وذلك إنما يكون في الحالة التي السنة فيها التطويل وهي حالة القراءة .اهـ. والظاهر أن هذا الامتداد والتطويل هو المراد من قول البحر له قرار اهـ. كلامه . ثم اعترض على النهر في نقله عن الفضلي الاعتماد أنه ليس بصحيح بل الذي في السراج عنه أنه يرسل في المذكورات، فالصواب عدم ذكره مع النسفي ومن بعده .اهـ. هذا واعتراضه على التعليل في قول شيخ الإسلام لأن في . هذا القيام ذكراً مسنوناً الخ . وحمله له على المنفرد غير ظاهر لأن التسميع والتحميد ذكراً بـ«أو» التي لأحد الشيئين والمنفرد يأتي بهما على ما ذكره فلا يصح تسليمه في المنفرد أيضاً، بل الظاهر موافقته لما بحثه في فتح القدير كما قاله صاحب البحر، فقول شيخ الإسلام «وهو التسميع» أي لو كان المصلي إماماً، وقوله أو التحميد لو كان مؤتماً أو منفرداً كما يأتي في المتن. قوله: (وعلى هذا فالمراد من الإجماع المتقدم الخ) أي قوله وأجمعوا أنه لا يسن الوضع في القيام الخ» وبهذا سقط اعتراض النهر السابق كما لا يخفى والحاصل أن الإجماع بين أئمة المذهب والاختلاف المذكور إنما هو بين مشايخ المذهب ولكن قد يقال : لو صح الإجماع كيف يسوغ للمشايخ النزاع تأمل.
Shaykh Isma'il said after transmitting from Sharh Miskin: The restriction to the prolonged type. Al-Barjandi said: Placing the hand in the described manner is sunnah in every standing in which dhikr is prescribed, whether the dhikr is fard, wajib, or sunnah, and what is meant by 'musannun' is 'mashru'' (legislated). In Sharh Ibn Malik: He places in the mentioned cases according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because what is narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) regarding the sunnah of placing is general for all standings, but the qawma from bowing is exempted due to its lack of extension, so all other standings remain on the original generality. And similar is in Ghurar al-Adhkar and al-Manba'. And in the first two (the two disciples) also, in the ta'lil of Muhammad's statement: Because the legislation of placing is for the preservation from the accumulation of blood in the fingertips, and that is only in the situation where prolongation is sunnah, i.e., the situation of recitation. It is apparent that this extension and prolongation is what is meant by the statement of al-Bahr: 'it has qarar.' Then he objected to al-Nahr regarding his transmission from al-Fadli about reliance (i'timad) that it is not correct; rather, the position in al-Siraj from him is that he lets hang (yursil) in the mentioned things. So the correct view is not to mention it with al-Nasafi and those after him. Now, his objection to the ta'lil in the statement of Shaykh al-Islam: 'Because in this standing there is a sunnah dhikr etc.' and his interpretation of it for the munfarid is not apparent, because tasmii' and tahmid are dhikr with 'aw' (or) which is for one of two things, and the munfarid comes with both as mentioned, so his concession does not apply to the munfarid either. Rather, it is apparent that it agrees with what was investigated in Fath al-Qadir, as said by the author of al-Bahr. So the statement of Shaykh al-Islam 'and it is tasmii'' means if the person praying is an imam, and his statement 'or tahmid' if he is a follower or munfarid, as will come in the matn. His statement: 'And upon this, what is meant by the aforementioned ijma' is the agreement of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples on the correct view, and it was declared correct in al-Bada'i' as the answer of the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), using as evidence his statement: 'We, the prophets, have been commanded to place our right hands over our left in prayer' without distinguishing between any situation, so it is general except what is excluded by evidence. And the commentator (al-Sharh) mentioned that he places in the takbirs of Eid, and according to some, it is sunnah in all standings absolutely, so he places in all. And al-Bada'i' reported the difference among the mashayikh regarding placing between the takbirs.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage refines the earlier ruling by introducing the condition of prolongation (tawil) for the sunnah of placing hands in standings with dhikr. Shaykh Isma'il and al-Barjandi state that placing hands is sunnah in every standing where dhikr is prescribed (whether fard, wajib, or sunnah), and the term 'musannun' here means 'mashru'' (legislated). The exemption of the qawma from ruku' is due to its lack of extension (imtidad). Ibn Malik's commentary explains that the hadith of Ibn Abbas (general command for all standings) is the basis, but the qawma is excluded because it is not prolonged. The reason for placing hands is to prevent blood from pooling in the fingertips, which occurs during prolonged recitation. Therefore, the condition for sunnah wad' is that the standing be prolonged and contain dhikr. The passage also addresses an objection to al-Nahr's transmission from al-Fadli, clarifying that the correct view is to let hang in the mentioned standings (qawma) unless prolonged. Finally, it reiterates that the ijma' of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that wad' is not sunnah in the qawma, but the later disagreement among mashayikh is about exceptions. The text reconciles this by stating that the ijma' refers to the original position, and the later ikhtilaf is about rulings when conditions change.

Key Terms
التطويل / الامتداد (al-tatwil / al-imtidad): The quality of being prolonged or extended; a condition for wad' to be sunnah in a standing
المسنون / المشروع (al-musannun / al-mashru'): Legally prescribed or legislated; in this context, al-Barjandi uses it to mean any standing that has dhikr prescribed by the Law

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be met for placing hands to be sunnah in a standing position according to the refined ruling in this passage?
A) The standing must contain any dhikr
B) The standing must be prolonged and contain dhikr
C) The standing must be after ruku'
D) The standing must be in a fard prayer

Key Takeaway
Placing hands is sunnah in prolonged standings with dhikr; the qawma is excluded due to brevity.

Ruling on the Opening Supplication (Thana') for Different Followers
Ruling on thana' for imam, ma'mum, and masbuq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for thana' for imam, ma'mum, munfarid, and masbuq, and identify when the masbuq omits it.

Core Idea
The opening supplication (thana') is sunnah for all, but the masbuq omits it when the imam recites aloud.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the opening supplication (thana') is a confirmed sunnah for every person praying — whether imam, follower (ma'mum), or one praying alone (munfarid). However, there is a critical exception for the masbuq (latecomer): when the imam recites aloud, the masbuq must listen and therefore omits the thana'. This lesson will help you internalize this rule and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its basic ruling
First note that thana' is the opening supplication said at the start of prayer. The text states it is sunnah for everyone based on the Prophet's practice.
Sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Recognize the exception for the masbuq
When the imam recites aloud (jahr), the masbuq must listen to the Quranic recitation, so he omits the thana'. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
Listening to the imam's recitation takes priority.
3
Differentiate the three roles
Memorize that imam, ma'mum, and munfarid all recite thana'. Only the masbuq leaves it out under the specific condition of audible recitation.
Ma'mum who arrives on time also recites thana', even in audible prayers? Actually, the text says 'every person praying' includes ma'mum, but later masbuq exception. The ma'mum who is not masbuq also recites thana' silently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (مستفتحاً) . هو حال من الوضع أي يضع قائلاً سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك وتبارك اسمك وتعالى جدك ولا إله غيرك. وقد تقدم أنه سنة لرواية الجماعة أنه كان صلى الله عليه وسلم يقوله إذا افتتح الصلاة أطلقه فأفاد أنه يأتي به كل مصل، إماماً كان أو مأموماً أو منفرداً لكن قالوا : المسبوق لا يأتي به إذا كان الإمام يجهر بالقراءة للاستماع وصححه في الذخيرة. ثم سبحان في الأصل مصدر كغفران وهو لا يكاد يستعمل إلا مضافاً منصوباً بإضمار فعله وجواباً، فمعنى سبحانك أسبحك تسبيحاً أي أنزهك تنزيهاً . وقيل اعتقد نزاهتك عن كل صفة لا تليق بك. وبحمدك أي نحمدك بحمدك فهو في المعنى عطف الجملة على الجملة فحذفت الثانية كالأولى، وأبقى حرف العطف داخلاً على متعلقها مراداً به الدلالة على الحالية من الفاعل فهو في موضع نصب على الحال منه فكأنه إنما أبقى ليشعر بأنه قد كان هنا حملة طوي ذكرها إيجازاً على أنه لو قيل بحمدك بلا حرف العطف كان جائزاً صواباً كما روي عن أبي حنيفة لأنه لا يخل بالمعنى المقصود والحاصل أنه نفى بقوله : «سبحانك صفات النقص، وأثبت بقوله بحمدك» صفات الكمال لأن الحمد إظهار الصفات الكمالية . ومن هنا يظهر وجه تقديم التسبيح على التحميد وتبارك لا يتصرف فيه ولا يستعمل إلا الله تعالى. ذكره القاضي البيضاوي . المصلي إماماً، وقوله أو التحميد لو كان مؤتماً أو منفرداً كما يأتي في المتن. قوله: (وعلى هذا فالمراد من الإجماع المتقدم الخ) أي قوله وأجمعوا أنه لا يسن الوضع في القيام الخ» وبهذا سقط اعتراض النهر السابق كما لا يخفى والحاصل أن الإجماع بين أئمة المذهب والاختلاف المذكور إنما هو بين مشايخ المذهب ولكن قد يقال : لو صح الإجماع كيف يسوغ للمشايخ النزاع تأمل.
His statement: '(mustaftihan)' is a hal (adverbial) from wad', i.e., he places while saying: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabaraka ismuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruk.' It has preceded that it is sunnah due to the narration of the group (al-Jama'ah) that he would say it when opening the prayer; he (the narrator) released it, so it indicates that every person praying says it, whether imam, follower, or one praying alone. But they said: The masbuq (latecomer) does not come with it if the imam is reciting loudly (jahr), because of listening, and it was declared correct in al-Dhakhirah. Then 'subhan' originally is a masdar like 'ghufran', and it is hardly ever used except in an annexed form, accusative with its verb implied and in answer. So the meaning of 'subhanaka' is 'I glorify You with tasbih', i.e., 'I declare Your transcendence.' It is said: believe in Your transcendence from every attribute that does not befit You. 'Wa bihamdika' means 'we praise You with Your praise', so in meaning it is the conjunction of a sentence to a sentence; the second was deleted like the first, and the conjunction particle was kept entering on its dependent, intended to indicate the adverbial state (hal) from the subject, so it is in the accusative case as a hal from it. It is as if it was kept to indicate that there was a sentence that was removed, mentioned briefly, so that if it were said 'bihamdika' without the conjunction, it would be permissible and correct, as narrated from Abu Hanifa, because it does not miss the intended meaning. The conclusion is that he denied attributes of deficiency with 'Subhanaka' and affirmed attributes of perfection with 'wa bihamdika', because hamd is the manifestation of perfect attributes. From here, the reason for presenting tasbih before tahmid becomes apparent. 'Tabaraka' is not conjugated and is not used except for Allah, as mentioned by al-Qadi al-Baydawi. The person praying as imam, and his statement 'or tahmid' if he is a follower or munfarid, as will come in the matn. His statement: 'And upon this, what is meant by the aforementioned ijma' is the agreement of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples on the correct view, and it was declared correct in al-Bada'i' as the answer of the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), using as evidence his statement: 'We, the prophets, have been commanded to place our right hands over our left in prayer' without distinguishing between any situation, so it is general except what is excluded by evidence. And the commentator (al-Sharh) mentioned that he places in the takbirs of Eid, and according to some, it is sunnah in all standings absolutely, so he places in all. And al-Bada'i' reported the difference among the mashayikh regarding placing between the takbirs.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on the opening supplication (thana') in prayer. It states that the thana' (Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...) is sunnah for every person praying—imam, follower (ma'mum), and one praying alone (munfarid)—based on the hadith that the Prophet would say it when opening the prayer. However, there is an exception: a masbuq (a latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has begun) should not recite the thana' if the imam is reciting audibly (jahr), because the masbuq must listen to the imam's recitation. This ruling is confirmed in al-Dhakhirah. The passage then provides a linguistic and theological explanation of the thana', noting that 'subhan' is a verbal noun expressing glorification, and it is always annexed (mudaf) and accusative. The phrase 'wa bihamdika' is interpreted as a sentence meaning 'and I praise You with Your praise', with the conjunction indicating a state (hal). The purpose is to negate attributes of deficiency and affirm attributes of perfection. Finally, the passage returns to the earlier discussion of wad' (placing hands) and clarifies that the ijma' referred to earlier is the agreement of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) on the principle, while later disagreements among mashayikh are about applications, not the core ruling.

Key Terms
المستفتح / الثناء (al-mustaftih / al-thana'): The opening supplication said at the beginning of prayer: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...'
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has started and misses a rak'ah or more
التسبيح (al-tasbih): The verbal noun 'subhan' meaning declaration of Allah's transcendence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In what situation does the masbuq omit the opening supplication (thana')?
A) When he joins the prayer late
B) When the imam is reciting audibly (jahr)
C) When he is praying behind an imam in a silent prayer
D) Always, because he is late

Key Takeaway
Thana' is sunnah for all, but the masbuq omits it when the imam recites aloud.

Hand Placement in Prayer: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
Clarifying consensus, dalil, and scope of hand placement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand placement in prayer, identify the primary dalil, and explain its general applicability across all standing positions.

Core Idea
The command to place hands in prayer is general for all standing positions unless specified otherwise.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on placing the right hand on the left during prayer. The text clarifies that the consensus of the three founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) affirms it as sunnah, based on a prophetic hadith. We will see how the hadith's generality is maintained and how later differences among scholars are resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the consensus and ruling
The text states that the consensus (ijma) of Abu Hanifa and his two companions is that the correct ruling is sunnah. Confirm that the three agreed on this.
This is the foundation of the mufta bihi position.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith cited: 'Indeed we, the company of prophets, were commanded to place our right hands on our left hands in prayer.' Identify the source and wording.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but widely accepted.
3
Analyze the dalil's import (wajh al-dalalah)
The imperative 'amrna' (we were commanded) indicates a command. In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) yields wujub only if a qarina (indicator) for obligation is present. Here, no such qarina exists, so it indicates sunnah.
This distinguishes Hanafi from Shafi'i, who take the imperative as obligation (fard) unless evidence suggests otherwise.
4
Apply the generality of the text
The hadith is general – 'without distinction between any situation and another.' Therefore, the sunnah applies to all standing positions in prayer, including the extra takbirs of 'Eid, unless a specific proof restricts it.
The default is 'umum (generality); any takhsis (specification) requires a separate dalil.
5
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf and resolve
Later mashayikh differed on placement between the takbirs of 'Eid. However, the mufta bihi position is the general one, as upheld by al-Marghinani and others. The consensus of the three imams and the generality of the hadith override the later ikhtilaf.
This illustrates the hierarchy: Zahir al-Riwayah > later opinions unless a clear exception is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالمراد من الإجماع المتقدم اتفاق أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه على الصحيح وصحح في البدائع جواب ظاهر الرواية مستدلاً بقوله إنا معاشر الأنبياء أمرنا أن نضع أيماننا على شمائلنا في الصلاة» من غير فصل بين حال وحال فهو على العموم إلا ما خص بدليل. وذكر الشارح أنه يضع في تكبيرات العيد وعند بعضهم أنه سنة القيام مطلقاً حتى يضع في الكل. وحكى في البدائع اختلاف المشايخ في الوضع فيما بين التكبيرات .
The intended meaning of the preceding consensus is the agreement of Abu Hanifa and his two companions on the correct view, and it was corrected in al-Bada'i' that the answer of the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) is that they use as proof his saying: 'Indeed we, the company of prophets, were commanded to place our right hands on our left hands in prayer' without distinction between any situation and another, so it is general unless it is specified by a proof. And the commentator mentioned that one places (hands) in the takbirs of 'Eid, and according to some it is sunnah of standing absolutely, so that one places in all. And in al-Bada'i' the difference of the mashayikh regarding placement between the takbirs is narrated.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the text's ruling about hand placement in prayer. The author explains that the consensus mentioned earlier refers to the agreement of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the correct position that placing the right hand on the left is sunnah. The hadith cited (from the Prophet ﷺ) is general, covering all types of prayer unless specified otherwise. The commentator also notes that according to some, the hand is placed during the takbirs of 'Eid, while others hold it is sunnah of standing absolutely. Al-Bada'i' records differences among later scholars (mashayikh) regarding placement between the takbirs. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent/well-known transmission from the founding imams, specifically from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
البدائع (al-Bada'i'): A Hanafi legal work (Badai' al-Sanai' by al-Kasani), often cited for resolving intra-madhhab differences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on placing the right hand on the left in prayer according to the consensus of Abu Hanifa and his two companions?
A) Fard
B) Sunnah
C) Wajib
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms that placing the right hand on the left is sunnah in all standing positions of prayer, based on the general command of the Prophet ﷺ.

Follower's Recitation of Thana' in Loud and Silent Prayers
Legal analysis of follower's thana' based on jahr and mukhafatah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower's recitation of thana' in loud and silent prayers and explain the rationale using the concepts of intended sunnah and obligatory listening.

Core Idea
The follower recites thana' in silent prayers but not in loud ones, as thana' is an intended sunnah that outweighs subsidiary listening.

When you pray behind an imam, are you supposed to recite the opening supplication (thana') or remain silent? The answer depends on whether the imam recites aloud or silently. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling and the legal reasoning behind it, based on the distinction between an intended sunnah (sunnah maqsudah) and a subsidiary sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
Identify what thana' is (the opening supplication) and note that it is classified as a sunnah maqsudah (intended sunnah) in the Hanafi school.
It is not wajib or fard, but an encouraged sunnah.
2
Determine the ruling for loud recitation
Read the passage to see the clear ruling: when the imam recites aloud (jahr), the follower does not recite thana'. This applies to both mudrik (one who caught the whole prayer) and masbuq (latecomer).
The source states there is no dispute on this, though later it notes a minority view.
3
Determine the ruling for silent recitation
In silent prayers (mukhafatah), the follower does recite thana'. The passage relies on the principle that thana' is an intended sunnah and listening (insat) is only obligatory during the state of listening.
Listening is not an obligation in silent prayers, so no conflict arises.
4
Analyse the objection and response
Consider the objection: if listening is obligatory even in loud prayers, why doesn't that obligation alone drop the follower's own recitation of Qur'an? The response: the follower's Qur'an recitation is dropped because the imam's recitation suffices, not because of listening. The imam's thana' does not suffice for the follower, so the follower must recite thana' when there is no listening obligation.
This highlights that the absence of the listening obligation in silent prayers allows the follower to perform the intended sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الجهر فإنه يمنع من الثناء بلا خلاف لكن مقتضى قوله وصححه في الذخيرة أن فيه خلافاً أيضاً وكذا في التتارخانية عن الخلاصة : ويسكت المؤتم عن الثناء إذا جهر الإمام هو الصحيح اهـ؛ وهو بإطلاقه يشمل المدرك والمسبوق، وقد رأيت في الذخيرة التصريح بالخلاف في الجهرية، وصحح أنه لا يثني بعد ما نقل عن شيخ الإسلام أنه في المخافتة يثني لأن الثناء سنة مقصودة والإنصات إنما يجب حالة الاستماع، أما في غير حالة الاستماع فيسن تعظيماً للقرآن فكان سنة تبعاً لا مقصوداً بنفسه بخلاف الثناء فمراعاة السنة المقصودة أهم فإن قيل : الإنصات فرض وإن كان لا يستمع حتى سقطت التلاوة عن المقتدي قلنا : إنما سقطت لأن قراءة الإمام له قراءة لا للإنصات وليس ثناء الإمام ثناء للمقتدي فإذا لم يأتي به يفوته اهـ ملخصاو ظاهره اعتماد أنه يأتي به في المخافتة وعليه مشى في الدرر
He said: The loud [recitation] prevents the [recitation of] thana' without dispute, but the implication of his statement — and al-Dhakhirah authenticated it — is that there is also a dispute about it. Similarly, in al-Tatar Khaniyyah from al-Khulasa: 'The follower remains silent from thana' when the imam recites aloud; this is the correct [view], end quote. And its generality includes one who caught the prayer from the beginning and the latecomer. And I saw in al-Dhakhirah explicit mention of dispute regarding loud [prayers], and it is authenticated that he does not recite thana'. It is transmitted from Shaykh al-Islam that in silent [prayers] he recites thana', because thana' is an intended sunnah, while listening is only obligatory during the state of listening. As for other than the state of listening, it is recommended out of reverence for the Qur'an, so it is a subsidiary sunnah, not intended in itself, unlike thana'. So observing the intended sunnah is more important. If it is said: Listening is obligatory even if he does not listen, so much so that the recitation [of Qur'an] has fallen from the follower [as a duty], we say: It only fell because the imam's recitation is his recitation, not because of listening. And the imam's thana' is not thana' for the follower; if he does not come with it, he misses it. End of summary. And its apparent meaning is reliance that he recites it in silent [prayers], and upon this is the reliance in al-Durar.
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the follower's (muqtadi) recitation of the opening supplication (thana') when the imam recites aloud (jahr) or silently (mukhafatah). The author first states that there is no dispute that jahr prevents the follower from reciting thana'. However, he notes that al-Dhakhirah indicates there is also a dispute about it. The correct view from al-Khulasa and al-Dhakhirah is that the follower remains silent when the imam recites aloud, and this applies to both one who caught the entire prayer (mudrik) and the latecomer (masbuq). The reasoning is that thana' is an intended sunnah (sunnah maqsudah), while listening (insat) is only obligatory during the state of listening. When not listening, it is recommended (sunnah) out of reverence for the Qur'an, but that is a subsidiary sunnah. Since thana' is an intended sunnah, it takes precedence over the subsidiary sunnah of listening. The passage also addresses an objection: if listening is obligatory (even if one does not hear), then the follower's own recitation of Qur'an is dropped. The response is that the follower's recitation is dropped because the imam's recitation suffices, not because of the obligation of listening. The imam's thana' does not suffice for the follower, so the follower must recite thana' in silent prayers. Thus, the relied-upon position is that in silent prayers, the follower does recite thana'.

Key Terms
الثناء (al-thana'): The opening supplication (subhanaka allahumma) recited after takbirat al-ihram.
الإنصات (al-insat): Listening attentively to the imam's recitation; obligatory during the recitation.
المؤتم (al-mu'tamm): The follower (muqtadi) who prays behind an imam.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joined the prayer late (after the imam has started).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only in loud prayers (jahr).
B) Only in silent prayers (mukhafatah).
C) In all prayers, regardless of imam's recitation.
D) Never, unless the imam pauses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling differentiates between loud and silent prayers: the follower recites thana' only when the imam recites silently.

Rulings on Ta'awwudh (Seeking Refuge) in Prayer: Wording, Silence, and Consequences
Detailed analysis of ta'awwudh in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'awwudh, identify its preferred wording, explain why it is sunnah, and apply the intra-madhhab dispute to determine when a follower and latecomer recite it.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is a sunnah of recitation, recited silently, and its wording is 'a'udhu billah'; the follower recites it only when the imam is silent.

The act of seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) before reciting the Qur'an in prayer is a well-established practice. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq not only clarifies its preferred wording and silent recitation but also delves into a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about whether it is attached to recitation or the opening supplication, which has direct practical implications for followers and latecomers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is ta'awwudh and what is its hukm level? The passage states it is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 16:98: 'fa-sta'idh bi-llahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'. Why is it not wajib?
The imperative indicates obligation, but it is diverted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the imperative indicate sunnah due to ijma' diverting it? The consensus of the salaf diverts the imperative from wajib to sunnah.
The principle: al-amr yafidu al-wujub illa li-sarf.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding whether ta'awwudh is sunnat al-qira'ah or sunnat al-thana'.
This affects who recites it.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical differences for the follower, latecomer, and timing relative to 'Id takbirat.
The mufta bihi: follower recites only when imam is silent; masbuq always recites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتعوذ سراً) أي قال المصلي أعوذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم وهو اختيار أبي . وعاصم وابن كثير وهو المختار عندنا وهو قول الأكثر من أصحابنا لأنه المنقول من استعادته ، وبهذا يضعف ما اختاره في الهداية من أن الأولى أن يقول أستعيذ بالله ليوافق يعني لأن المذكور فيه فاستعذ بصيغة الأمر من الاستعاذة وأستعيذ مضارعها فيتوافقان بخلاف «أعوذ ) فإنه من العوذ لا من الاستعاذة، وجوابه كما في فتح القدير أن لفظ «استعذ» طلب العوذ، وقوله «أعوذ » مثال مطابق لمقتضاه أما قربه من لفظه فمهدر. وفي البدائع : ولا ينبغي أن يزيد عليه أن الله هو السميع العليم يعني كما هو اختيار نافع وابن عامر والكسائي لأن هذه الزيادة من باب الثناء وما بعد التعوّذ محل القراءة لا محل الثناء، وقد قدم المصنف أنه سنة لقوله تعالى فإذا قرأت القرآن فاستعذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم [النحل : ٩٨] أي إذا أردت قراءة القرآن فأطلق المسبب على السبب. وإنما لم يكن واجباً لظاهر الأمر لأن السلف أجمعوا على سنيته كما نقله المصنف في الكافي ولم يعين سند الإجماع الذي هو الصارف للأمر عن ظاهره وعلى القول بأنه لا يحتاج إلى سند بل يجوز أن يخلق الله لهم ضرورياً يستفيدون به الحكم فلا إشكال. وروى ابن أبي شيبة عن إبراهيم النخعي عن ابن مسعود أربع يخفيهن الإمام : التعوّذ والتسمية وآمين وربنا لك الحمد. فقوله «سراً» عائد إلى الاستفتاح والتعوّذ قوله (للقراءة فيأتي به المسبوق لا المقتدي ويؤخر عن تكبيرات العيدين) أن التعوّذ سنة القراءة فيأتي به كل قارىء للقرآن لأنه شرع لها صيانة عن وساوس الشيطان فكان تبعاً لها وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وعند أبي يوسف هو تبع للثناء. وفائدة الخلاف في ثلاث مسائل : إحداها أنه لا يأتي به المقتدي عندهما لأنه لا قراءة عليه، ويأتي به أيضاً، وكذا في متن التنوير، وكذا في الخانية حيث قال : وينبغي التفصيل إن كان الإمام يجهر لا يأتي به وإن كان يسر . يأتي به اهـ ومشى عليه في المنية أيضاً. قوله : (وهو قول الأكثر من أصحابنا) قال في النهر : وجعله الشارح ظاهر المذهب، وادعى بعضهم إجماع القراء عليه من حيث الرواية(۱) وهذا لأن السين إنما دخلت في الأمر دلالة على طلب الاستعاذة، فالقائل «أعوذ ) ممتثل لا أستعيذ لأنه طلب للاستعاذة لا متعوذ، ولذا كان (أعوذ هو المنقول من استعادته عليه الصلاة والسلام. وقول الجوهري عذت بفلان واستعذت به التجأت إليه مردود عليه عند أهل اللسان كذا في النشر لابن الجزري . . قوله : (لأن السلف أجمعوا على سنيته قال في النهر : في دعوى الإجماع نزاع، فقد روي الوجوب عن عطاء والثوري وإن كان جمهور السلف على خلافه كما في الفتح. قوله : ( فقوله سراً عائد الخ) قال في (۱) قوله (الرواية) لعله الدراية تأمل اهـ منه .
His statement [of the author]: 'And [recite] ta'awwudh silently' means the prayer says 'a'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim.' And this is the choice of Abu 'Asim and Ibn Kathir, and it is the chosen [view] with us, and it is the saying of the majority of our companions, because it is what is transmitted from his [the Prophet's] seeking refuge. And by this is weakened what was chosen in al-Hidayah that it is better to say 'asta'idhu billah' to conform, because what is mentioned [in the verse] is 'fa-sta'idh' in the imperative form from isti'adhah, and 'asta'idhu' is its imperfect verb, so they correspond, unlike 'a'udhu,' for it is from 'awdh' not from isti'adhah. Its answer, as in Fath al-Qadir, is that the word 'ista'idh' is a request for refuge, and his saying 'a'udhu' is an example conforming to its requirement; as for its closeness to the wording, it is disregarded. In al-Bada'i': 'It is not appropriate to add to it "innallaha huwa al-sami' al-'alim," meaning as is the choice of Nafi', Ibn 'Amir, and al-Kisa'i, because this addition is from the category of thana', and after ta'awwudh is the place for recitation, not for thana'. And the author has stated that it is sunnah due to His statement: 'So when you recite the Qur'an, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed shaytan' (al-Nahl 16:98), meaning when you intend to recite the Qur'an; thus the result is used for the cause. And it is not wajib because of the apparent imperative, because the salaf (early generations) have consensus on its being sunnah, as the author transmitted in al-Kafi, and he did not specify the chain of consensus which diverts the imperative from its apparent meaning. And on the view that [the source of consensus] does not need a chain, rather Allah can create for them a necessary knowledge by which they derive the ruling, there is no problem. Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i from Ibn Mas'ud: 'Four things the imam conceals: ta'awwudh, tasmiyah (basmalah), amin, and rabbana laka al-hamd.' So his statement 'silently' refers back to the opening [supplication] and ta'awwudh. His statement: 'For recitation; so the latecomer (masbuq) recites it, not the follower (muqtadi), and it is delayed after the takbirat of the two 'Ids' means that ta'awwudh is a sunnah of recitation, so every reciter of the Qur'an recites it because it was prescribed for it as a protection from the whisperings of shaytan, so it is subsidiary to it. And this is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. According to Abu Yusuf, it is subsidiary to thana'. The benefit of the dispute is in three issues: first, that the follower does not recite it according to both of them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) because he has no recitation on him; and he recites it also... likewise in the text of al-Tanwir and likewise in al-Khaniyyah where he said: 'It should be differentiated: if the imam recites aloud, he does not recite it; if he recites silently, he recites it.' And upon this the author of al-Munya relied. His statement: 'And it is the saying of the majority of our companions.' He said in al-Nahr: 'And the commentator considers it the apparent [teaching] of the madhhab, and some claimed consensus of the reciters upon it from the perspective of transmission (or perhaps 'diraya) ...' And this is because the 'sin' in the imperative only indicates the request for isti'adhah, so the one who says 'a'udhu' is compliant, not 'asta'idhu', because it is a request for refuge, not a person seeking refuge. Therefore, 'a'udhu' is what is transmitted from his [the Prophet's] seeking refuge. The statement of Jawhari that 'udhtu bi-fulan and ista'dhtu bihi' both mean 'I sought refuge with him' is rejected by linguists, as in al-Nashr of Ibn al-Jazari. His statement: 'Because the salaf are united on its being sunnah.' He said in al-Nahr: 'There is dispute about the claim of consensus, because obligation has been narrated from 'Ata' and al-Thawri, even though the majority of salaf are contrary, as in al-Fath.' His statement: 'So his saying "silently" refers back...' He said... end.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof regarding ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) in prayer. It begins by stating that ta'awwudh is recited silently (sirran). The preferred wording is 'a'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' (not 'asta'idhu'), as this is the transmitted wording from the Prophet's practice. Although the verse uses 'fa-sta'idh', the response is that 'a'udhu' is an exact fulfillment of the request for refuge. It is also not appropriate to add 'innallaha huwa al-sami' al-‘alim' after it, as that would be thana' (praise) in a place designated for recitation. The ruling that ta'awwudh is sunnah (not wajib) is supported by the consensus (ijma') of the salaf, though some early scholars like 'Ata' and al-Thawri held it as wajib. The author then clarifies that ta'awwudh is a sunnah of recitation (sunnat al-qira'ah), meaning it is tied to the act of reciting the Qur'an. This leads to two positions: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, ta'awwudh is subsidiary to recitation; according to Abu Yusuf, it is subsidiary to the opening supplication (thana'). The practical consequences of this difference (thamarah al-khilaf) are in three issues: (1) The follower (muqtadi): according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the follower does not recite ta'awwudh because he does not recite Qur'an behind the imam; but according to Abu Yusuf, he does recite it because he recites thana'. However, later Hanafi scholars like the authors of al-Tanwir and al-Khaniyyah differentiate: if the imam recites aloud, the follower leaves ta'awwudh; if silently, he recites it. (2) The latecomer (masbuq): he recites ta'awwudh because he will recite Qur'an in his own remaining prayer. (3) Ta'awwudh is delayed until after the takbirat of the two 'Id prayers. The passage ends with a defense of the wording 'a'udhu' against linguistic objections, and a note that the claim of consensus on sunniyyah is disputed.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): The act of seeking refuge in Allah from the accursed shaytan before reciting the Qur'an.
الاستعاذة (al-isti'adhah): The verbal form of seeking refuge, synonymous with ta'awwudh. The verse uses 'fa-sta'idh' which is a request for refuge.
سنة القراءة (sunnat al-qira'ah): A sunnah that is attached to the act of reciting the Qur'an; it is performed by every reciter.
سنة الثناء (sunnat al-thana'): The sunnah of praising Allah in prayer (the opening supplication).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, what is the preferred wording for seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) in prayer?
A) 'A-sta'idhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'
B) 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'
C) 'A'udhu billahi al-sami' al-'alim min al-shaytan al-rajim'
D) 'Innallaha huwa al-sami' al-'alim' followed by 'a'udhu billah'

Key Takeaway
Ta'awwudh is a sunnah recited silently; its wording is 'a'udhu billah'; the follower recites it only when the imam is silent; the masbuq always recites it.

Ruling on Ta'awwudh: Sunnah Status, Wording, and Silent Recitation
Explains the ruling, wording, and volume of ta'awwudh in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'awwudh, explain why it is sunnah not wajib, and identify the correct wording and volume.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah, not wajib — the Quranic command is overridden by Salafi ijma'.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the status and form of ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) in prayer. It addresses three core questions: what wording is used, whether it is recited aloud or silently, and why it is considered sunnah despite a clear Quranic imperative. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correct practice and for appreciating how Hanafi usul operates when a general command is qualified by consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Ta'awwudh is the act of seeking refuge with Allah from Satan before Quran recitation in prayer. The author states it is sunnah, i.e., recommended but not obligatory.
2
Locate the primary evidence (dalil)
The Quranic verse from Surah al-Nahl (16:98) is cited: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan.'
The verse contains an imperative command.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the dalil proves the ruling)
The imperative form prima facie indicates obligation (wujub). However, the Hanafi school argues that the Salaf (early Muslims) unanimously considered ta'awwudh sunnah, and this ijma' overrides the apparent meaning of the command.
The diversion of the command from obligation to recommendation is a key Hanafi usul principle.
4
Determine the wording and volume
The commentator prefers the wording 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' over alternatives like 'Asta'idhu billah'. He also states it is recited silently (sirran), based on a narration from Ibn Mas'ud listing four things the imam conceals.
The addition of 'inna Allaha huwa al-sami' al-aleem' is not recommended.
5
Synthesize the practical ruling
Thus, the Hanafi mufta bihi is: ta'awwudh is sunnah muakkadah, recited silently, with the wording 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim', before Quran recitation in prayer.
If omitted, the prayer remains valid but the sunnah is lost.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتعوذ سراً) أي قال المصلي أعوذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم وهو اختيار أبي . وعاصم وابن كثير وهو المختار عندنا وهو قول الأكثر من أصحابنا لأنه المنقول من استعادته ، وبهذا يضعف ما اختاره في الهداية من أن الأولى أن يقول أستعيذ بالله ليوافق يعني لأن المذكور فيه فاستعذ بصيغة الأمر من الاستعاذة وأستعيذ مضارعها فيتوافقان بخلاف «أعوذ ) فإنه من العوذ لا من الاستعاذة، وجوابه كما في فتح القدير أن لفظ «استعذ» طلب العوذ، وقوله «أعوذ » مثال مطابق لمقتضاه أما قربه من لفظه فمهدر. وفي البدائع : ولا ينبغي أن يزيد عليه أن الله هو السميع العليم يعني كما هو اختيار نافع وابن عامر والكسائي لأن هذه الزيادة من باب الثناء وما بعد التعوّذ محل القراءة لا محل الثناء، وقد قدم المصنف أنه سنة لقوله تعالى فإذا قرأت القرآن فاستعذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم [النحل : ٩٨] أي إذا أردت قراءة القرآن فأطلق المسبب على السبب. وإنما لم يكن واجباً لظاهر الأمر لأن السلف أجمعوا على سنيته كما نقله المصنف في الكافي ولم يعين سند الإجماع الذي هو الصارف للأمر عن ظاهره وعلى القول بأنه لا يحتاج إلى سند بل يجوز أن يخلق الله لهم ضرورياً يستفيدون به الحكم فلا إشكال. وروى ابن أبي شيبة عن إبراهيم النخعي عن ابن مسعود أربع يخفيهن الإمام : التعوّذ والتسمية وآمين وربنا لك الحمد. فقوله «سراً» عائد إلى الاستفتاح والتعوّذ.
His statement: (And he seeks refuge silently) meaning the worshiper says: I seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan. This is the choice of Abu [Amr?] and Asim and Ibn Kathir, and it is the chosen [view] according to us, and it is the saying of the majority of our companions because it is what is transmitted from his seeking refuge. And by this is weakened what was chosen in al-Hidayah that the first is to say 'I seek refuge with Allah' to correspond, because what is mentioned therein is 'fa-ista'idh' in the imperative form from seeking refuge, and 'asta'idh' is its imperfect, so they correspond, unlike 'a'udhu' for it is from 'al-'awdh' not from seeking refuge. The answer, as in Fath al-Qadir, is that the word 'ista'idh' is a request for refuge, and his saying 'a'udhu' is an example matching its requirement; as for its closeness to its wording, it is disregarded. And in al-Bada'i': It is not proper to add 'indeed Allah is the All-Hearing, All-Knowing', as is the choice of Nafi', Ibn Amir, and al-Kisa'i, because this addition is from the category of praise, and after seeking refuge is the place of recitation, not the place of praise. And the author has presented that it is sunnah based on His saying, the Exalted: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan' [al-Nahl 16:98], meaning when you intend to recite the Quran, so the caused was applied to the cause. And it was not wajib because of the apparent command, because the Salaf agreed upon its being sunnah, as the author transmitted in al-Kafi, and he did not specify the chain of ijma' which is the diversion of the command from its apparent meaning; and on the view that it does not need a chain, rather Allah can create for them a necessity by which they derive the ruling, there is no problem. And Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i from Ibn Mas'ud: Four things the imam conceals: seeking refuge, the basmala, amin, and 'Rabbana laka al-hamd'. So his statement 'silently' refers to the opening supplication and seeking refuge.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) in prayer. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that it is said silently. The commentator expands: the worshiper says 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'. This wording is the choice of Abu Amr, Asim, and Ibn Kathir among the qira'at imams, and it is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school because it is the wording transmitted from the Prophet's own seeking refuge. The commentator argues against the view in al-Hidayah that one should say 'Asta'idhu billah' to match the Quranic imperative 'fa-ista'idh', pointing out that 'a'udhu' is from a different root but still fulfills the command. Adding 'inna Allaha huwa al-sami' al-aleem' is not recommended because it is praise, and the place after ta'awwudh is for recitation, not praise. The ruling level: ta'awwudh is sunnah, not wajib, based on the Quranic verse (al-Nahl 16:98). The verse uses an imperative which prima facie indicates obligation, but the Salaf (early Muslims) unanimously considered it sunnah, and this ijma' diverts the command from its apparent meaning of obligation. A hadith from Ibn Mas'ud (through a mursal chain) lists four things the imam says silently: ta'awwudh, basmala, amin, and 'Rabbana laka al-hamd'. Thus, 'silently' applies to both the opening supplication (istiftah) and ta'awwudh.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): The act of seeking refuge with Allah from Satan, recited before Quran recitation in prayer.
سراً (sirran): Silently, in a low voice such that only the worshiper hears himself.
استعاذة (isti'adha): The verbal noun meaning seeking refuge; synonymous with ta'awwudh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because the Prophet never said it in prayer.
D) Because it is only recommended for the imam.

Key Takeaway
Ta'awwudh is a sunnah act in prayer, recited silently before Quran recitation, with the wording 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim', and its status as sunnah (not wajib) is due to the consensus of the Salaf overriding the apparent command.
