Ta'awwudh: Sunnah of Qira'ah or Thana'? An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'awwudh's attachment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on ta'awwudh, explain the three practical differences between them, and apply the ruling to the muqtadi, masbuq, and imam in Eid prayer.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah, but its placement determines who recites it and when.

The passage presents an internal Hanafi dispute concerning the nature of ta'awwudh (seeking refuge): is it a sunnah accompanying Quran recitation (qira'ah) or the opening supplication (thana')? The answer produces three practical consequences in prayer. Understanding this dispute clarifies rulings for followers, latecomers, and the imam, especially in Eid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, recognise that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold ta'awwudh is a sunnah of qira'ah, while Abu Yusuf holds it is a sunnah of thana'.
Both agree it is sunnah; the dispute is about its attachment.
2
Analyse the first practical difference: muqtadi
Under Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, the muqtadi (follower who joined from the beginning) does not say ta'awwudh because he does not recite Quran behind the imam. Under Abu Yusuf, he does say it because he does say thana'.
Muqtadi always says thana' in Hanafi school.
3
Analyse the second difference: imam's timing in Eid prayer
According to Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, the imam says ta'awwudh after the additional takbirs in the first rak'ah. According to Abu Yusuf, both imam and muqtadi say it after thana', before the additional takbirs.
This affects the order of the Eid prayer opening.
4
Analyse the third difference: masbuq's repetition
Under Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, the masbuq (latecomer) says ta'awwudh only when he stands to complete missed rak'ahs. Under Abu Yusuf, he says it twice: once at the beginning and again after recitation in the qada'.
This arises because thana' is said at the beginning and after Fatiha in the makeup.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preponderance)
The author of al-Khulasa preferred Abu Yusuf's view, but the majority of early texts (al-Mabsut, al-Manzumah) record the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, with some narrations from Muhammad agreeing with Abu Yusuf. The commentator leaves the matter with 'Wallahu a'lam'.
The mufta bihi is not definitively settled; later fatwa practice may vary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (للقراءة فيأتي به المسبوق لا المقتدي ويؤخر عن تكبيرات العيدين) أن التعوّذ سنة القراءة فيأتي به كل قارىء للقرآن لأنه شرع لها صيانة عن وساوس الشيطان فكان تبعاً لها وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وعند أبي يوسف هو تبع للثناء. وفائدة الخلاف في ثلاث مسائل : إحداها أنه لا يأتي به المقتدي عندهما لأنه لا قراءة عليه، ويأتي به عنده لأنه يأتي بالثناء ثانيها أن الإمام يأتي بالتعوّذ بعد تكبيرات الزوائد في الركعة الأولى عندهما، ويأتي به الإمام والمقتدي بعد الثناء قبل التكبيرات عنده ثالثها أن المسبوق لا يأتي به الثناء للحال ويأتي به إذا قام إلى القضاء عندهما وعنده يأتي به مرتين عن الدخول بعد القراءة، وقد ذكر صاحب الهداية وجماعة الخلاف بين الصاحبين وأبي يوسف وفي عامة النسخ كالمبسوط والمنظومة وشروحها بين أبي يوسف ومحمد، ولم يذكر قول أبي حنيفة بل وذكر أبو اليسر رواية عن محمد كما عن أبي يوسف، فلذا والله أعلم صحح صاحب الخلاصة قول أبي يوسف أنه تبع للثناء. وأشار المصنف إلى أن محل التعوّذ بعد الثناء ومقتضاه أنه لو تعوّذ قبل الثناء أعاده بعده لعدم وقوعه في محله وإلى أنه لو نسي التعوّذ فقرأ الفاتحة لا يتعوّذ لفوات المحل. وقيدنا بقراءة القرآن للإشارة إلى أن التلميذ لا يتعوّذ إذا قرأ على أستاذه كما نقله في الذخيرة، وظاهره أن الاستعاذة لم تشرع إلا عند قراءة القرآن أو في الصلاة وفيه نظر ظاهر، وقد قدمنا أن المسبوق يأتي بالثناء إلا إذا كان إمامه يجهر بالقراءة، ويأتي به أيضاً إذا قام إلى قضاء ما سبق .به. وإذا أدرك الإمام في الركوع يتجرى إن كان أكبر رأيه أنه لو أتى به أدرك الإمام في شيء من الركوع يأتي به قائماً وإلا يتابع الإمام ولا يأتي بالثناء في الركوع لفوات محله فإنه محل التسبيحات وإنما يأتي بتكبيرات العيد فيه دون تسبيحاته لأنها واجبة دونها، وكذا لو أدرك المسبوق الإمام في السجدة فهو كالركوع، وإذا لم يدرك الإمام في الركوع والسجود لا يأتي بهما لأنه انفرد عن الإمام بعد الاقتداء بزيادة لم يعتد بها وإن كانت غير مفسدة لما أن زيادة ما دون الركعة غير مفسد وإن أدرك إمامه في القعدة فإنه لا يأتي بالثناء بل يكبر للافتتاح ثم للانحطاط ثم يقعد وقيل يأتي بالثناء وينبغي أن يفصل كما في الركوع والسجود وأن لا فرق بين القعدة الأولى والثانية. وقد أجاب عنه في النهر بأن ما في الذخيرة ليس في المشروعية وعدمها بل في الاستنان وعدمه .اهـ. أي فتسن للقراءة ولا
His statement: (For recitation, so the masbuq says it, not the muqtadi, and it is delayed from the takbirs of the two Eids) that ta'awwudh is a sunnah of recitation, so every reciter of the Quran says it because it was legislated for it as a safeguard from the whisperings of Satan, so it is a follower of it. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. According to Abu Yusuf, it is a follower of thana'. The benefit of the difference lies in three issues: First, the muqtadi does not say it according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) because he has no recitation, but he says it according to him (Abu Yusuf) because he says thana'. Second, the imam says ta'awwudh after the additional takbirs in the first rak'ah according to them, but according to him, the imam and muqtadi say it after thana' before the takbirs. Third, the masbuq does not say thana' for the current state but says it when he stands to make up what he missed according to them, while according to him, he says it twice: at the beginning after the opening takbir and after recitation. And the author of al-Hidayah and a group mentioned the difference between the two companions (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf, and in most copies like al-Mabsut, al-Manzumah and its commentaries, it is between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and they did not mention the saying of Abu Hanifa; rather, Abu al-Yusr mentioned a narration from Muhammad the same as from Abu Yusuf. Therefore, and Allah knows best, the author of al-Khulasa declared Abu Yusuf's view correct that it is a follower of thana'. And the author indicated that the place of ta'awwudh is after thana', and its implication is that if he sought refuge before thana', he repeats it after because it did not occur in its place, and that if he forgets ta'awwudh and recites al-Fatiha, he does not seek refuge because the place has passed. And we restricted it to recitation of the Quran to indicate that the student does not seek refuge when reciting to his teacher, as transmitted in al-Dhakhira. Its apparent meaning is that seeking refuge is only legislated when reciting the Quran or in prayer, and there is an apparent objection to this. And we have mentioned that the masbuq says thana' unless his imam is reciting aloud, and he also says it when he stands to make up what he missed. If he catches the imam in ruku', he waits; if he thinks that if he says it he will catch the imam in something of ruku', he says it standing; otherwise, he follows the imam and does not say thana' in ruku' because its place has passed, for it is the place of tasbihat. He only says the takbirs of Eid in it without its tasbihat because they are obligatory unlike them. Similarly, if the masbuq catches the imam in sujud, it is like ruku'. If he does not catch the imam in ruku' or sujud, he does not say them (thana' and ta'awwudh) because he has separated from the imam after following with an addition that is not counted, even if it does not invalidate, because an addition of less than a rak'ah does not invalidate. If he catches his imam in the sitting, he does not say thana', but rather says the opening takbir, then the takbir for bowing, then sits. And it is said he says thana', and it is appropriate to differentiate as in ruku' and sujud, and that there is no difference between the first and second sitting. And it was answered about it in al-Nahr that what is in al-Dhakhira is not about legislation or absence thereof, but about sunnah and its absence. So it is sunnah for recitation and not...
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the nature of ta'awwudh: is it a sunnah of qira'ah (recitation) or of thana' (the opening supplication)? Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that ta'awwudh is a sunnah attached to Quran recitation, as it was legislated to protect against Satanic whispers during recitation. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that it is a sunnah attached to thana'. The practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf) are three: (1) The muqtadi (follower) does not recite ta'awwudh according to the first view because he does not recite Quran behind the imam, but according to Abu Yusuf, he does recite it because he says thana'. (2) The imam recites ta'awwudh after the additional takbirs in the first rak'ah of Eid prayer according to the first view, but according to Abu Yusuf, the imam and muqtadi recite it after thana' and before the takbirs. (3) The masbuq (latecomer) does not recite thana' immediately but only when he stands to make up missed rak'ahs according to the first view, but according to Abu Yusuf, he recites thana' twice: once after the opening takbir and again after recitation in the qada'. The author of al-Hidayah and others mention this dispute, but many sources frame it as between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, not including Abu Hanifa. Abu al-Yusr transmitted a narration from Muhammad agreeing with Abu Yusuf, leading the author of al-Khulasa to prefer Abu Yusuf's view. The commentator then discusses related rulings: if one recites ta'awwudh before thana', it must be repeated in its proper place; if one forgets and starts Fatiha, the place is lost and ta'awwudh is not repeated. Ta'awwudh is only for Quran recitation, not for when a student recites to a teacher, as in al-Dhakhira. The masbuq's actions are detailed: when catching the imam in ruku', sujud, or sitting, specific rules apply to thana' and ta'awwudh, with the general principle that the place for thana' is before Fatiha, so if missed, it is not made up in later positions.

Key Terms
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer who joined from the beginning.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joins the prayer late and misses one or more rak'ahs.
الثناء (al-thana'): The opening supplication (du'a al-istiftah) recited after the takbirat al-ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why does the muqtadi (follower) not recite ta'awwudh?
A) Because the muqtadi has no Quran recitation behind the imam.
B) Because ta'awwudh is only for the imam.
C) Because the muqtadi says thana' instead.
D) Because the muqtadi is not required to seek refuge.

Key Takeaway
Ta'awwudh is sunnah in Hanafi prayer, but its attachment to qira'ah or thana' produces three practical differences among the three founding imams, with no definitive tarjih.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Rulings on Ta'awwudh in Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Positions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'awwudh timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on when ta'awwudh is recited in prayer and apply the mufta bihi ruling to the imam and masbuq scenarios.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah; its correct place is after thana', but the three Hanafi masters differ on timing for imam and masbuq.

This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute recorded in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq concerning the placement of ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) in prayer. The three pillars of the school—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—hold different views on when the imam and the latecomer (masbuq) should recite it. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the relied-upon practice and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three issues in dispute
The passage presents three points of intra-Hanafi difference: (1) when the imam says ta'awwudh in the first rak'ah, (2) when the masbuq says ta'awwudh, and (3) the general rule that ta'awwudh follows thana'.
2
Map each master's position
For each issue, state the view of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Note that the text reports a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in many copies, while Abu Hanifa's view is derived from other sources.
Use the intruction in the passage to distinguish the sources.
3
Identify the mufta bihi
The author of al-Khulasa preferred Abu Yusuf's position that ta'awwudh follows thana'. This becomes the relied-upon ruling.
4
Work through the masbuq scenarios
Apply the rulings to a masbuq who catches the imam in ruku', sajdah, or qa'dah. Decide whether he says thana' and ta'awwudh, and where.
Use the passage's guidelines.
5
Reflect on the grammatical note
The commentary discusses whether the word 'ta'awwadha' indicates order. Understand that the author's placement, not the conjunction, establishes the sequence.
Optional but enriches comprehension.

Source Text

وظاهره أن الاستعاذة لم تشرع إلا عند قراءة القرآن أو في الصلاة وفيه نظر ظاهر، وقد قدمنا أن المسبوق يأتي بالثناء إلا إذا كان إمامه يجهر بالقراءة، ويأتي به أيضاً إذا قام إلى قضاء ما سبق .به. وإذا أدرك الإمام في الركوع يتجرى إن كان أكبر رأيه أنه لو أتى به أدرك الإمام في شيء من الركوع يأتي به قائماً وإلا يتابع الإمام ولا يأتي بالثناء في الركوع لفوات محله فإنه محل التسبيحات وإنما يأتي بتكبيرات العيد فيه دون تسبيحاته لأنها واجبة دونها، وكذا لو أدرك المسبوق الإمام في السجدة فهو كالركوع، وإذا لم يدرك الإمام في الركوع والسجود لا يأتي بهما لأنه انفرد عن الإمام بعد الاقتداء بزيادة لم يعتد بها وإن كانت غير مفسدة لما أن زيادة ما دون الركعة غير مفسد وإن أدرك إمامه في القعدة فإنه لا يأتي بالثناء بل يكبر للافتتاح ثم للانحطاط ثم يقعد وقيل يأتي بالثناء وينبغي أن يفصل كما في الركوع والسجود وأن لا فرق بين .اهـ. قال الرملي أقول : الترتيب مستفاد من صنيعه لا من الواو فانظر إلى قوله وسمى وقرأ الخ» تأمل قوله : ( وفيه نظر ظاهر وجهه كما قال بعض الفضلاء أن الأمر بالاستعاذة معلول بدفع الوسوسة فيجوز الإتيان به في جميع ما يخشى فيه الوسوسة .اهـ. وقد أجاب عنه في النهر بأن ما في الذخيرة ليس في المشروعية وعدمها بل في الاستنان وعدمه .اهـ. أي فتسن للقراءة ولا
And according to him, because he comes with the thana'. Second: that the Imam comes with ta'awwudh after the additional takbirs in the first rak'ah according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the Imam and follower come with it after thana' before the takbirs according to him (Abu Hanifa). Third: that the masbuq does not come with thana' for the current state, and he comes with it when he stands to make up (qada') according to them, and according to him he comes with it twice: upon entering after recitation. Al-Hidayah and a group mentioned the dispute between the two companions and Abu Yusuf, and in most copies like al-Mabsut and al-Manzuma and their commentaries, it is between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and he did not mention the statement of Abu Hanifa; rather Abu al-Yusr mentioned a narration from Muhammad similar to Abu Yusuf, so, and Allah knows best, the author of al-Khulasa declared Abu Yusuf's statement correct: that it follows thana'. The author pointed out that the place of ta'awwudh is after thana', and its implication is that if one says ta'awwudh before thana', he repeats it after because it did not occur in its place; and that if he forgets ta'awwudh and recites al-Fatiha, he does not say ta'awwudh because the time has passed. We have restricted by recitation of Quran to indicate that a student does not say ta'awwudh when reciting to his teacher, as quoted in al-Dhakhira. Its apparent meaning is that ta'awwudh is only prescribed when reciting Quran or during prayer, but there is an obvious issue. We have stated earlier that the masbuq says thana' unless his Imam recites aloud; he also says it when he stands to make up what he missed. If he catches the Imam in ruku', he deliberates: if he thinks he can say it and still catch the Imam in part of ruku', he says it standing; otherwise he follows the Imam and does not say thana' in ruku' because its place is lost; ruku' is the place for tasbihat, and he says the Eid takbirs in it without its tasbihat because they (takbirs) are wajib and tasbihat are not. Similarly, if the masbuq catches the Imam in sajdah, it is like ruku'. If he does not catch the Imam in ruku' or sajdah, he does not say them (thana' and ta'awwudh) because he separated from the Imam after following with an increase not deemed significant, even if not invalidating—since an increase less than a rak'ah does not invalidate. If he catches his Imam in the qa'dah, he does not say thana' but says takbir for iftitah, then for lowering, then sits; it is said he says thana', and one should differentiate as in ruku' and sajdah, and there is no difference between the first and second qa'dah. al-Nahr: Its being a qualification in istiftah is also unlikely; therefore it is from tanaazu', but it is a hal from the subject of 'ta'awwadha', and it is permissible to be a description of an omitted verbal noun—that is better because the use of an indefinite verbal noun as hal, though frequent, is samaa'i (based on heard usage). There is consideration in his statement that it is from tanaazu' due to what some scholars said from Ham' al-Hawami' that tanaazu' occurs in every object except for the purpose and distinction, and similarly hal, contrary to Ibn Mu'ti. Hence Shaykh Ala' al-Din al-Haskafi said: it is like tanaazu'—that is similar to tanaazu' which is the attachment of two or more verbal operators or their derivatives to one or more nouns. He said: (And the author pointed out that the place of ta'awwudh is after thana'). al-Nahr said: The implication of this reference is not hidden because the waw does not indicate order. He said: al-Ramli says: I say: order is understood from his action, not from the waw. So look at his saying 'and he named and recited' etc. Consider his saying: (and in it is an apparent consideration). Its aspect, as some scholars said, is that the command for ta'awwudh is conditioned to repel waswasa, so it is permissible to do it in everything where waswasa is feared. And he answered him in al-Nahr that what is in al-Dhakhira is not about prescription or its lack, but about being sunnah or not. That is, it is sunnah for recitation but not.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the rulings of ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) in prayer. It opens by presenting three issues: (1) The masbuq recites thana' according to all, but there is ikhtilaf among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding when the Imam says ta'awwudh: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the Imam says it after the additional takbirs in the first rak'ah, while Abu Hanifa holds it is after thana' before takbirs. (2) The masbuq does not say ta'awwudh immediately but says it when he stands for qada' according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, while according to Abu Hanifa he says it twice: upon entering and after recitation. The text notes that in most sources the ikhtilaf is between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, with the author of al-Khulasa preferring Abu Yusuf's view that ta'awwudh follows thana'. The author then states that the proper place for ta'awwudh is after thana', so if one says it earlier, he should repeat it. If one forgets and recites al-Fatiha, he does not go back to ta'awwudh. The restriction 'at reading Quran' indicates that a student reciting to his teacher does not say ta'awwudh, as reported in al-Dhakhira. The text addresses the masbuq in various scenarios: if he catches the Imam in ruku', he should weigh whether to say thana' while standing or follow the Imam; in sajdah it is similar; if he catches the Imam in the sitting, he says takbir and sits without thana'. The river commentary (al-Nahr) discusses a grammatical point about the word 'ta'awwadha' and then addresses a criticism about the indicative nature of the waw, concluding that order is derived from the author's style. Another point about ta'awwudh being prescribed only to repel waswasa is answered by distinguishing between prescription and sunnah. All explanations are within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): The act of saying 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' to seek refuge from Satan when beginning Quran recitation in prayer.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the Imam has started, missing one or more rak'ahs.
الثناء (al-thana'): The opening supplication of prayer, typically 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, where does the Imam say ta'awwudh in the first rak'ah?
A) Before the additional takbirs
B) After the additional takbirs
C) After thana' and before the additional takbirs
D) After reciting al-Fatiha

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position on ta'awwudh is: the Imam says it after thana' before the additional takbirs, and the masbuq says it only when standing for qada'.

The Ruling on Tasmiyah in Prayer: Sunnah or Wajib?
Disputes obligation of tasmiyah with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over tasmiyah and evaluate the evidence for the sunnah position.

Core Idea
The famous Hanafi ruling is that tasmiyah is sunnah, not wajib, despite some later scholars arguing for wujub.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the legal status of saying Bismillah in each rak'ah. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq counts it among the sunan, but some later Hanafi scholars considered it wajib. Let's trace the evidence and the response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling in the passage
The passage discusses tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim') in prayer. The author states that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq counted it among the sunan, which is the famous position.
Note the term 'sunan' indicates recommended, not obligatory.
2
Locate the disagreement
Some later Hanafi scholars like al-Zahidi and Ibn Wahban consider it wajib, requiring sajdah al-sahw if omitted. This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is the focus.
The wajib position is based on a narration from Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa.
3
Analyze the proof for wujub
The proof for wujub is that even if tasmiyah is not part of al-Fatiha definitively due to khabar al-wahid, the khabar al-wahid still necessitates action, so it becomes effectively part of al-Fatiha in practice.
This reasoning uses the principle that khabar al-wahid requires action (wujub al-'amal).
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The author refutes the wujub claim by citing the hadith of Anas in Sahih Muslim, where Anas did not hear the Prophet or the caliphs recite the basmala aloud. The Hanafi response is that they recited it silently, not that they omitted it.
Thus the hadith does not negate recitation; it only proves silence, which is the Hanafi practice.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage concludes that the famous and relied-upon position is sunnah mu'akkadah, as the author of Kanz counted it among the sunan and the majority of early Hanafis held this view.
The later wajib opinion is considered weak (da'if) by the author.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وسمی سراً في كل ركعة أي ثم يسمي المصلي بأن يقول بسم هذا الرحيم . هو المراد بالتسمية هنا، وأما في الوضوء والذبيحة فالمراد منها ذكر الله تعالى. والمراد بالمصلي هنا الإمام أو المنفرد، أما المقتدي فلا دخل له فيها فإنه لا يقرأ بدليل أنه قدم أنه لا يتعوّذ، وقد عدها المصنف فيما سبق من السنن وهو المشهور عن أهل المذهب. وقد صحح الزاهدي في شرحه وفي القنية وجوبها في كل ركعة وصرح في باب سجود السهو بأنه يلزمه السهو بتركها وتبعه على ذلك ابن وهبان في منظومته قال : وإن الوجوب قول الأكثر. والشارح الزيلعي في باب سجود السهو وعلل في البدائع بما يفيده فإنه قال : وروى أبي يوسف عن أبي حنيفة أنه يأتي بها في كل ركعة هو قول أبي يوسف ومحمد، لأن التسمية إن لم تجعل من الفاتحة قطعاً لخبر الواحد لكن خبر الواحد يوجب العمل فصارت من الفاتحة عملاً فمتى لزمه قراءة الفاتحة يلزمه قراءة التسمية احتياطاً .اهـ. وهذا كله ضعيف والمواظبة لم تثبت لما في صحيح مسلم عن أنس: صليت خلف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبي بكر وعمر وعثمان فلم أسمع أحداً . يقرأ بسم . الله الرحمن الرحيم وإن كان قد أجاب عنه أئمتنا بأنه لم يرد نفي القراءة بل السماع للإخفاء بدليل ما رواه أحمد عنه فكانوا لا يجهرون الرحمن الرحيم وهو دليلنا على الإخفاء بها، ولولا التصريح بلزوم السهو بتركها لقلت إن
His saying: (and he says the tasmiyah silently in every rak'ah) i.e., then the worshiper says tasmiyah by saying 'Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim'. That is what is meant by tasmiyah here; as for wudu and slaughter, what is meant is the mention of Allah. The worshiper here means the Imam or the individual; as for the follower, he has no part in it because he does not recite, as evidenced by the fact that he stated earlier that he does not say ta'awwudh. The author counted it among the sunan earlier, and that is the famous [position] among the people of the madhhab. However, al-Zahidi in his commentary and in al-Qunyah declared it wajib in every rak'ah, and he stated in the chapter of sahw that sahw becomes necessary by leaving it, and Ibn Wahban followed him in his poem, saying: 'Indeed wujub is the statement of the majority.' The commentator al-Zayla'i in the chapter of sajdat al-sahw and he explained in al-Bada'i' what implies it: he said: 'Abu Yusuf narrated from Abu Hanifa that he says it in every rak'ah; that is the statement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, because tasmiyah, even if it is not made part of al-Fatiha categorically due to the khabar al-wahid, but the khabar al-wahid necessitates action, so it becomes part of al-Fatiha in practice; so when one is obligated to recite al-Fatiha, he is obligated to recite tasmiyah as a precaution.' All of this is weak, and constancy was not proven because of what is in Sahih Muslim from Anas: 'I prayed behind the Prophet (peace be upon him), Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and I did not hear any of them recite Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim.' And indeed our imams answered it by saying that he did not deny the recitation, only the hearing, due to concealment, as evidenced by what Ahmad narrated from him that they did not recite aloud 'ir-Rahman ir-Rahim', and that is our evidence for concealment of it. Were it not for the explicit statement [in some sources] that leaving it necessitates sahw, I would say that
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage deals with the legal status of tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim') in prayer. It begins by clarifying that tasmiyah here refers to the basmala in prayer, distinct from its use in wudu and slaughter. The text states that the author (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) considers it among the sunan, which is the famous position in the Hanafi school. However, some late Hanafi scholars like al-Zahidi and Ibn Wahban consider it wajib, requiring sajdah al-sahw if omitted. The passage then presents the evidence for wujub from the transmission of Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa and the reasoning of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: that even if tasmiyah is not part of al-Fatiha definitively due to khabar al-wahid, the khabar al-wahid still necessitates action, so it becomes effectively part of al-Fatiha in practice. The author refutes this by citing the hadith of Anas in Sahih Muslim, where Anas did not hear the Prophet or the Rightly Guided Caliphs recite the basmala aloud. The Hanafi response to this hadith is that the basmala was recited silently, not that it was omitted; thus it does not negate its recitation. The passage concludes by noting that without the explicit statement that leaving it requires sahw, one would say it is not wajib. The implication is that the majority Hanafi position is that tasmiyah is sunnah, not wajib.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): The act of saying 'Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim' (In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful) in prayer, often at the beginning of each rak'ah before reciting al-Fatiha.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur; it is zanni al-thubut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the famous Hanafi position, what is the ruling on saying 'Bismillah' in each rak'ah of prayer?
A) Wajib, neglecting it requires sajdah al-sahw
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Fard, like reciting al-Fatiha
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that tasmiyah is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, despite a minority opinion arguing for wujub.

The Basmalah in Prayer: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the basmalah in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the basmalah in prayer, distinguish the sunnah view from the wajib view, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The basmalah is a sunnah recited silently; the view of obligation is weak within the Hanafi school.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the ruling of saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' (the basmalah) during prayer. While the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states it is a sunnah, some later Hanafi scholars argued for obligation, creating an intra-school dispute. We will navigate the evidence, including the hadith of Anas, and settle on the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling in the matn
The base text says the musalli says the basmalah silently in every rak'ah. This is the sunnah view.
The author counts it among the sunan.
2
Locate the minority wajib view
Al-Zahidi and al-Qunyah hold it wajib, requiring sajdah al-sahw if omitted. This is based on a narration from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad as a precaution.
Their evidence: the solitary hadith necessitates action, so the basmalah becomes effectively part of the Fatiha.
3
Examine the primary proof for the sunnah view
The hadith in Sahih Muslim from Anas: he did not hear the Prophet or the caliphs recite it aloud. The Hanafi response is that they recited it silently.
This proves silent recitation, not omission.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preponderance)
The author declares the wajib view weak due to lack of consistency (muwazabah). Al-Nahr states both views are preponderant but the texts follow the sunnah view.
The mufta bihi is sunnah mu'akkadah.
5
Apply the practical ruling
The basmalah is said silently at the start of each rak'ah. If forgotten until after the Fatiha, it is not repeated. There is no issue if said between the Fatiha and surah.
This summarizes the practical implications of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٥٤٤
كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة
.
الله الرحمن

His statement (and he says it silently in every rak'ah) meaning then the pray-er says the basmalah by saying "Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim". That is what is meant by tasmiyah here. As for wudu and slaughter, it means remembrance of Allah. The pray-er here means the imam or the one praying alone. As for the follower, he has no part in it because he does not recite, as evidenced by the earlier statement that he does not seek refuge. The author counts it among the sunan previously, and this is the well-known view of the school. Al-Zahidi in his commentary and in al-Qunyah affirmed its obligation in every rak'ah, and he stated in the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw that neglecting it necessitates sujud al-sahw, and Ibn Wahban followed him in his poem saying: Obligation is the view of the majority. The commentator al-Zayla'i in the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw and he reasoned in al-Bada'i' in a way that benefits: he said: Abu Yusuf narrated from Abu Hanifa that he says it in every rak'ah. This is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, because if the tasmiyah is not made part of the Fatiha definitively due to the solitary hadith, yet the solitary hadith necessitates action, so it becomes part of the Fatiha in practice. So whenever recitation of the Fatiha is obligatory, recitation of the tasmiyah is obligatory as a precaution. End quote. All this is weak, and consistency has not been established because of what is in Sahih Muslim from Anas: I prayed behind the Prophet (peace be upon him), Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and I did not hear any of them recite "Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim". Although our imams responded that it does not negate recitation; rather, it negates hearing due to quietness, as evidenced by what Ahmad narrated from him: they did not recite aloud "al-Rahman al-Rahim". That is our evidence for saying it quietly. Were it not for the explicit statement about the necessity of sujud for leaving it, I would say that

it is sunnah for other than it, and negating sunnah does not negate legitimacy. The text of al-Dhakhirah is as follows: When a man says "Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim", if he intends by it recitation of the Quran, he seeks refuge before it, because Allah says: "So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah" (An-Nahl 98). If he intends opening speech, as a student recites to the teacher, he does not seek refuge before it, because he does not intend by it Quran recitation. Do you not see that if a man intends to give thanks and says "Alhamdulillah Rabb al-Alamin", he does not need to seek refuge before it? Therefore, a person in janabah, if he says "Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim" intending Quran recitation, it is not permissible; if he intends opening speech or tasmiyah, there is no harm. End quote. The summary: if he intends to say "Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim", he does not say the ta'awwudh before it unless he intends recitation. But if he intends opening speech, as a student says it at the beginning of his lesson for knowledge, he does not seek refuge, because the basmalah leaves its Quranic nature by the intention of dhikr, to the extent that it is permissible for a person in janabah to say it if he does not intend it as Quran. In short, if one says something of the Quran, ta'awwudh is not recommended before it unless he intends tilawah. But if he says the basmalah to open speech or says al-hamdalah intending thanks, not intending it as Quran, then ta'awwudh is not recommended. Similarly, if he speaks something that is not Quran, it is more priority. Yes, seeking refuge is recommended when entering the restroom and the like, which is not speech. As for speech that is not Quran, ta'awwudh is not recommended for it. Contemplate his statement: (All this is weak). He said in al-Nahr: The truth is they are two preponderant views, except that the texts are on the first. The second is supported by what passed from al-Bada'i'. Then he said: I say: in obligating sujud for leaving it there is contradiction with the fact that it is not obligatory to leave the minimum of the Fatiha. So ponder. End quote. I say: the contradiction is repelled by what has passed for us in the obligations from al-Haskafi from al-Mujtaba of the obligation of sujud for leaving an ayah of it.

So what is in Munyat al-Musalli that the imam does not say it when praying aloud and says it when praying silently is a gross error, contradicting all narrations. And his statement: "in every rak'ah" means at the beginning of every rak'ah. So the tasmiyah is not recommended between the Fatiha and the surah absolutely according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad said: it is recommended if reciting silently, not if aloud. In al-Bada'i', it is declared the correct view is that of the two. The disagreement is about recommendation; as for not being disliked, it is agreed upon. Hence, it is stated in al-Dhakhirah and al-Mujtaba that if one says the basmalah between the Fatiha and the surah, it is good according to Abu Hanifa, whether that surah is recited silently or aloud. And the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam and his student al-Halabi gave preponderance to this, due to the doubt arising from the difference of opinion on whether it is an ayah of every surah, although that doubt is less than the doubt arising from the difference of opinion on whether it is an ayah of the Fatiha. And what is in al-Qunyah that sujud al-sahw is necessary for leaving it between the Fatiha and the surah is very far-fetched. Similarly, the statement of one who said "he does not say the basmalah except in the first rak'ah" is an incorrect statement. Rather, al-Zahidi said: it is a gross error against our companions. In mentioning the tasmiyah after ta'awwudh, there is an indication of its place. So if one says the basmalah before ta'awwudh, he repeats it after, because it did not occur in its proper place. His statement: (It is an ayah of the Quran revealed as a separator between surahs. It is not from the Fatiha nor from any surah) is an elucidation of the most correct of the opinions, as in al-Muhit and others, and a refutation of the other two opinions: one is that it is not Quran, which is the view of some of our scholars, due to the difference of scholars and reports about it causing doubt. The second is that it is from the Fatiha and from every surah, attributed to al-Shafi'i. The justification for the most correct view is their consensus on writing it with the command to strip the Mushaf, and it is mutawatir in it, which is evidence of its being Quran mutawatir. Thus the doubt from the disagreement is repelled. The reason the denier of it is not judged as a disbeliever is that denying a qat'i matter does not necessitate disbelief unless there is no

He said in al-Nahr: In al-Khulasa, it is made a narration from the Imam. In al-Mustasfa, the fatwa is on it. In al-Bada'i', the correct is the view of the two. In al-Atabiyyah and al-Muhit, the view of Muhammad is the chosen one. Ibn al-Diya' in his commentary on al-Ghaznawiyyah from the commentary of 'Umdat al-Musalli reported that the view of Abu Yusuf was chosen because the word fatwa is more emphatic and stronger than the word chosen. His statement: (not... because its place is lost) the wording of Sharh al-Munyah by Ibn Amir Haj: he does not say it because its place is lost. His statement: (And the reason he did not judge etc.) his wording in his commentary on al-Manar is clearer than this. Its text: There is a difference of opinion on the basmalah. The truth is that it is from the Quran, but the one who denies it is not deemed a disbeliever, despite his denial of a qat'i matter, due to the strong doubt that removes its being from the Quran from the realm of clarity to the realm of ambiguity. So it is Quran due to its tawatur in its place, but no disbelief because of the lack of tawatur that it is in the beginnings of surahs as Quran. The conclusion: al-Bahr al-Raiq vol. 1 p. 35

Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the basmalah (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) in the prayer. The author, al-Marghinani, comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq which states that the musalli (the one praying) says the basmalah silently in every rak'ah. The commentary first clarifies the terminology: 'tasmiyah' here means the specific basmalah, whereas in wudu or slaughter it means general dhikr of Allah. The person addressed is the imam or the munfarid (one praying alone); the muqtadi (follower) does not recite it, as he does not recite the Fatiha itself (as established earlier that he does not say ta'awwudh). The author counts it among the sunan, which is the well-known view. However, some later scholars like al-Zahidi and the author of al-Qunyah consider it wajib, such that leaving it necessitates sajdah al-sahw. Ibn Wahban followed this in his poem. The commentator al-Zayla'i in his commentary on al-Hidayah cites a narration from Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa that he says it in every rak'ah, which is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Their reasoning: although the basmalah is not definitively part of the Fatiha because of the solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid), such a hadith requires action, so in practice it becomes part of the Fatiha. Therefore, whenever recitation of the Fatiha is obligatory, recitation of the basmalah is also obligatory as a precaution. The author dismisses this as weak because consistency (muwazabah) is not established; the hadith in Sahih Muslim from Anas states that he did not hear the Prophet or the caliphs recite the basmalah aloud. The Hanafi response is that this does not negate recitation, only hearing it aloud, as another narration indicates they did not say it aloud. Thus it is said silently. The passage then discusses when the basmalah is said without the intention of Quran recitation, such as opening speech, in which case ta'awwudh is not required. It also notes that a person in janabah may say it if not intending Quran. The author then states that the view of obligation is weak, and the truth is that it is a sunnah. The text of al-Nahr mentions that both views are preponderant but the texts follow the first (sunnah). A contradiction is noted: if leaving the basmalah requires sajdah, then it would seem like a wajib, but this is resolved by noting that leaving even a single ayah of the Fatiha also requires sajdah. The passage then refutes the view in Munyat al-Musalli that the imam says it only when reciting silently, calling it a gross error. It clarifies that the basmalah is said at the beginning of each rak'ah, not between the Fatiha and the surah (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad says it is sunnah only in silent prayer. The disagreement is about recommendation, not about it being disliked; Abu Hanifa considers it good between the Fatiha and surah. The passage also addresses the issue of forgetting the basmalah until after finishing the Fatiha: it is not repeated because its place is lost. Finally, it discusses the Qur'anic status of the basmalah: it is an ayah revealed as a separator between surahs, not part of the Fatiha or any surah (this is the most correct view). Some said it is not Quran at all, others said it is part of the Fatiha and every surah (Shafi'i view). The most correct view is supported by consensus on writing it in the Mushaf with tawatur, though the denier is not declared a disbeliever due to strong doubt. The conclusion is that the basmalah is Quran but its placement in the beginnings of surahs is not mutawatir, hence no takfir for denial.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): The act of saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' in prayer; specifically, the basmalah.
الفاتحة (al-Fatiha): The opening surah of the Quran, recited in every rak'ah of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the well-known Hanafi view, what is the ruling on reciting the basmalah (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) in prayer?
A) It is wajib and must be recited aloud.
B) It is sunnah and recited silently in every rak'ah.
C) It is mustahab but only in the first rak'ah.
D) It is makruh to recite it at all.

Key Takeaway
The basmalah in prayer is a sunnah recited silently; the intra-Hanafi dispute over obligation is settled by the majority view that it is not wajib.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Basmalah: Status and Rulings in Prayer
Commentary on basmalah as Quranic verse and its recitation between Fatihah and surah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the basmalah as a Quranic verse for separation, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on its recitation between Fatihah and surah, and apply the concept of shubhah to the issue of takfir.

Core Idea
Basmalah is Quranic verse for separation, not part of surahs; its recitation in prayer is hasan, not sunnah.

The basmalah is universally recognized as a verse of the Quran, but its precise status and placement in prayer have been matters of scholarly debate. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi school's position that the basmalah is an independent verse sent down to separate surahs, and we explore the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding its recitation between al-Fatihah and a subsequent surah. Understanding this dispute requires careful attention to the concepts of tawatur, shubhah, and the different levels of obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine whether the basmalah is part of the Fatihah and each surah, or an independent verse for separation.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school relies on the tawatur of the basmalah in the mushaf to prove its qur'aniyyah, but not its inclusion in the surahs. The hadith of divided prayer and the verse count of Surat al-Mulk serve as additional evidence.
3
Understand the shubhah
The strong doubt (shubhah) about whether the basmalah is part of every surah prevents the ruling of kufr for its denier, even though its qur'aniyyah is qat'i.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation
Abu Hanifa considers reciting basmalah between Fatihah and surah as hasan in all prayers; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it is not sunnah in loud prayers, with Muhammad adding it is sunnah in silent prayers. Al-Bada'i and later authorities prefer the Sahibayn's view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf (and Muhammad in silent prayers): it is not sunnah to recite basmalah aloud between Fatihah and surah in loud prayers, and in silent prayers it is hasan but not sunnah.

وإذا خافت يأتي بها غلط فاحش مخالف لكل الروايات. وقوله في كل ركعة أي في ابتداء كل ركعة فلا تسن التسمية بين والسورة مطلقاً عندهما. وقال محمد تسن إذا خافت لا إن جهر. وصحح في البدائع قولهما. والخلاف في محلها، ولو نسيها حتى فرغ من الفاتحة لا لأجل فوات محلها. يسمي قوله (وهي آية من القرآن أنزلت للفصل بين السور ليست من الفاتحة ولا من كل سورة) بيان للأصح من الأقوال كما في المحيط وغيره ورد للقولين الآخرين: أحدهما أنها ليست قرآناً وهو قول بعض مشايخنا لاختلاف العلماء والأخبار فيها فأورث شبهة. ثانيهما أنها . من ومن كل سورة ونسب إلى الشافعي ووجه الأصح إجماعهم على كتابتها مع الأمر بتجريد المصحف وقد تواترت فيه، وهو دليل تواتر كونها قرآناً، وبه اندفعت الشبهة للاختلاف، وإنما لم يحكم بكفر منكرها لأن إنكار القطعي لا يوجب الكفر إلا إذا لم يثبت فيه الفاتحة عليكم أيضاً فإنه يدل على عدم السنية أيضاً وأنتم لا تقولون بذلك قوله : (فما في منية المصلي الخ) قال الرملي : أولها شارحها الحلبي بقوله أي لا يأتي بها جهراً بل يأتي بها سراً» اهـ. ولا يختفى بعده. قوله : (وقال محمد تسن إن خافت أي تسن في السرية. قال في النهر : وجعله في الخلاصة رواية الثاني عن الإمام. وفي المستصفى وعليه الفتوى وفي البدائع الصحيح قولهما، وفي العتابية والمحيط قول محمد هو المختار، ونقل ابن الضياء في شرح الغزنوية عن شرح عمدة المصلي أنه إنما اختير قول أبي يوسف هذا لأن لفظة الفتوى آكد وأبلغ من لفظة المختار قوله : (لا . لأجل فوات محلها) عبارة شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج لا يسمي لأجلها لفوات محلها قوله : (وإنما لم يحكم الخ) عبارته في شرحه على المنار أوضح مما هنا ونصها. وقد اختلف في البسملة والحق أنها من القرآن لكن لم يكفر جاحدها مع إنكاره القطعي للشبهة القوية بحيث يخرج بها كونها من القرآن من حيز الوضوح إلى حيز الإشكال، فهي قرآن لتواترها في محلها ولا كفر لعدم تواتر كونها في الأوائل قرآناً. والحاصل أن البحر الرائق ج ١ م ٣٥ يسمي ثلاث آيات وأمن الإمام والمأموم سراً وكبر بلا مد وركع ووضع يديه على ركبتيه وفرج شبهة قوية، فإن ثبتت فلا كما في البسملة. فالموجب لتكفير من أنكر القرآن إنكار ما تواتر كونه قرآناً، وأما البسملة فلما تواترت في المصحف ثبتت قرآنيتها، وبتواتر كونها قرآناً في الأوائل لم يكفر جاحدها، فالتواتر المعتبر في القرآن تواتره في محله والمعتبر في التكفير تواتر كونه قرآناً، وبهذا اندفع ما قيل من الإشكال في التسمية وهو أنها إن كانت متواترة لزم تكفير منكرها ولم يتكافروا فيها، وإن لم تكن متواترة فليست قرآناً . وأشار بقوله آية إلى أنها في القرآن آية واحدة يفتتح بها كل سورة، وعند الشافعي آيات في السور. والخلاف في غير البسملة التي في سورة النمل، أما هي فبعض آية اتفاقاً. ومما استدل به لمذهبنا حديث قسمت الصلاة بيني وبين عبدي فإذا قال الحمد الله إلى آخره (١) فإنه لم يذكر البسملة فدل أنها ليست من الفاتحة. وحديث عد سورة الملك ثلاثين آية وهي ثلاثون دونها، والكلام في البسملة طويل بين الأئمة واستفيد من كلام المصنف أنه يحرم قراءتها على الجنب والحائض. وقيده في المحيط وغيره بأن يقرأ على قصد القرآن ومقتضى كونها قرآناً أن تحرم على الجنب إلا إذا قصد الذكر أو التيمن. وفي المجتبى : الأصح أنها آية في حق حرمتها على الجنب لا في حق جواز الصلاة بها فإن فرض القراءة ثابت بيقين فلا يسقط بما فيه شبهة، وكذا في المحيط.
Sent down for separation between surahs, not from Fatihah nor from any surah. And he recited Fatihah and a surah or Fatihah (the obligation in their speech meaning affirmation) it is general and includes loud and silent prayers. So what is in Munyat al-Musalli that the Imam does not come with it when loud and comes with it when silent is a gross error contradicting all narrations. And his saying in every rak'ah meaning at the beginning of every rak'ah, so the tasmiyah is not sunnah between Fatihah and surah absolutely according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said it is sunnah if silent, not if loud. And in al-Bada'i the correct is their saying. The dispute is about sunniyyah; as for absence of karahah it is agreed upon. Hence it is stated in al-Dhakhirah and al-Mujtaba that if he says the tasmiyah between Fatihah and surah it is good (hasan) according to Abu Hanifah, whether that surah is recited silently or loudly. And al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam and his student al-Halabi preferred it due to the shubhah of difference in it being an ayah from every surah, although the shubhah therein is less than the shubhah arising from difference in it being an ayah from Fatihah. And what is in al-Qunyah that he must perform sajdah al-sahw for leaving it between Fatihah and surah is very far. Likewise the saying of one who says he does not say it except in the first rak'ah is incorrect. Rather al-Zahidi said it is a gross error against our companions. And mentioning the tasmiyah after ta'awwudh indicates its place. So if he says it before ta'awwudh he repeats it after because it did not occur in its place. And if he forgets it until he finishes Fatihah, he does not say it because its place is lost. His saying (And it is an ayah from the Qur'an sent down for separation between surahs, not from Fatihah nor from any surah) is a clarification of the most correct of the opinions as in al-Muhit and others, and a refutation of the other two opinions: one: that it is not Qur'an, which is the saying of some of our mashayikh due to differing scholars and reports causing shubhah. Second: that it is from every surah, attributed to al-Shafi'i. And the aspect of correctness is their consensus on writing it with the command to purify the mushaf, and it is mutawatir therein, which is evidence of its tawatur as Qur'an, and thereby the shubhah due to difference is repelled. And he did not rule kufr for its denier because denial of the qat'i does not necessitate kufr except when there is no strong shubhah. Also the hadith 'I divided the prayer between Me and My servant...' does not mention the basmalah, indicating it is not from Fatihah. And the hadith counting Surat al-Mulk as thirty verses, and it is thirty without it. And the discussion on basmalah is lengthy among the imams. It is understood from the author's speech that it is haram for a junub or menstruating woman to recite it. And it is restricted in al-Muhit to reciting with intent of Qur'an; the requirement of it being Qur'an is that it is haram for the junub unless he intends dhikr or tabarruk. And in al-Mujtaba: the correct is that it is an ayah in respect of its prohibition on the junub, not in respect of the validity of prayer with it, because the obligation of recitation is established with certainty and is not dropped by what involves shubhah. Similarly in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute over the basmalah in prayer, with additional discussion on its status as Qur'an. It begins by citing the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'It is an ayah of the Qur'an sent down to separate between surahs, not part of the Fatihah nor any surah.' The commentary clarifies that this is the most correct view (asahh), rejecting two other opinions: (1) that it is not Qur'an at all (attributed to some Hanafi mashayikh due to conflicting reports), and (2) that it is part of every surah (attributed to al-Shafi'i). The Hanafi proof for its qur'aniyyah is that the entire Ummah agreed to write it in the mushaf, and its tawatur (widespread transmission) in the mushaf establishes it as Qur'an. However, its denier is not declared a kafir because there is a strong shubhah (doubt) regarding its being part of the surahs, which prevents the ruling of kufr. The passage then delves into the dispute between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the sunniyyah of reciting it between Fatihah and surah. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), it is not sunnah in loud prayers, but Muhammad says it is sunnah in silent prayers. The author notes that al-Bada'i affirms the Sahibayn's view. However, Abu Hanifa considers it hasan (good) without karahah. It also addresses the ruling for a junub or menstruating woman: it is haram to recite basmalah if intended as Qur'an, but permissible if intended as dhikr or tabarruk.

Key Terms
البسملة (al-basmalah): The phrase bismillah al-rahman al-rahim, considered a Quranic verse used to separate surahs but not part of any surah (except Surat al-Naml).
التواتر (al-tawatur): Widespread transmission and acceptance of the mushaf text, used as proof of basmalah's Qur'anic status.
الشبهة (al-shubhah): A legal doubt that prevents the application of a certain ruling (e.g., takfir) even when the qat'i is denied.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting basmalah between Fatihah and surah in a loud prayer?
A) It is sunnah to recite it aloud.
B) It is not sunnah (according to the Sahibayn).
C) It is wajib.
D) It is makruh tahrimi.

Key Takeaway
Basmalah is a Quranic verse for separation, not part of surahs; in Hanafi prayer practice, it is hasan to recite it between Fatihah and surah in silent prayers, but not sunnah, and not reciting it does not invalidate the prayer.

Obligation of Reciting Fatihah and Surah: Both Require Repetition if Omitted
Commentary on the wajib recitations in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of reciting Fatihah and a surah for imam and munfarid, and explain why omission of either requires i'adah.

Core Idea
Both Fatihah and a surah are wajib in prayer; omission of either necessitates repetition due to karahah tahrimiyyah.

In this passage, the commentator refines a common view within the Hanafi school. While the base text (sharh) holds that only omitting Fatihah requires i'adah, the commentator demonstrates that omitting the surah equally triggers karahah tahrimiyyah and thus i'adah. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and establishes the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting Surat al-Fatihah and a surah (or three verses) after it during prayer for the imam and munfarid. State the hukm level: wajib.
The ma'mum does not recite; he listens.
2
Understand the matn's distinction
The matn (and sharh) claim that Fatihah is more emphatically wajib; leaving it requires i'adah, but leaving the surah does not. Identify this as the view being critiqued.
This is an intra-Hanafi position, not the final mufta bihi.
3
Analyse the commentator's critique
The commentator argues that both are wajib by agreement (ittifaq). Since leaving any wajib in prayer establishes karahah tahrimiyyah, and every prayer with karahah tahrimiyyah must be repeated, leaving the surah also necessitates i'adah.
The key principle: "Kullu salatin uiddiyat ma'a karahatin tahrimiyyah yajibu i'adatuha."
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that both Fatihah and surah are wajib, and omission of either requires i'adah. This is supported by later Hanafi authorities.
Fatihah is more emphasized in terms of being a rukn in other schools, but in practice both are equally wajib for i'adah.

قوله (وقرأ الفاتحة وسورة أو ثلاث آيات أي وقرأ المصلي إذا كان إماماً أو منفرداً على وجه الوجوب ما ذكر وهما واجبتان للمواظبة لكن الفاتحة أوجب حتى يؤمر بالإعادة بتركها دون السورة. كذا ذكره الشارح، وقد تبع فيه الفقيه وفيه نظر ظاهر لأن كلا منهما واجب اتفاقاً وبترك الواجب تثبت كراهة التحريم وقد قالوا كل صلاة أديت مع كراهة التحريم يجب إعادتها، فتعين القول بوجوب الإعادة عند ترك السورة وما يقوم مقامها كترك الفاتحة. الفاتحة أكد في الوجوب من السورة للاختلاف في ركنيتها دون السورة، والأكدية لا نعم الموجب لتكفير جاحده إنكار ما تواتر في محله وما تواتر كونه ،قرآناً والمعتبر في إثبات القرآنية الأوّل فقط انتهت. وقد ظهر أن قوله هنا وبتواتر كونها (قرآناً صوابه وبعدم تواتر الخ» كما لا يخفى. وقد رأيته ملحقاً في بعض النسخ هذا واعلم أن في كلامه في البحر اضطراباً وذلك أنه ذكر أولاً في وجه الأصح أن تواترها في المصحف دليل تواتر قرآنيتها وأن بذلك اندفعت الشبهة في قرآنيتها، ومعلوم أن تواترها في أوائل السور وقد حكم بأن ذلك دليل تواتر قرآنيتها واللازم من كونها قرآناً في الأوائل، ثم حكم بأن فيها شبهة فناقض صدر كلامه وكذلك قوله فالموجب لتكفير من أنكر القرآن إنكار ما تواتر كونه قرآناً مناقض لما قبله من إثبات تواتر كونها قرآناً، وكذا قوله ذلك تواتر (١) رواه مسلم في كتاب الصلاة حديث ٣٨ ٤٠. أبو داود في كتاب الصلاة باب ١٣٢. الترمذي في كتاب تفسير سورة الفاتحة باب .١ النسائي في كتاب الافتتاح باب ٢٣ أحمد في مسنده (٢٤١/١، .(٢٨٥
His saying (And he recited the Fatihah and a surah or three verses) meaning the worshiper, if he is imam or alone, recites what was mentioned in the manner of obligation, and both are obligatory due to constancy, but the Fatihah is more obligatory such that he is ordered to repeat (i'adah) by leaving it, unlike the surah. Thus the commentator stated, and the faqih followed him, but there is an apparent flaw because both are wajib by agreement, and by leaving a wajib there is karahah tahrimiyyah established, and they said every prayer performed with karahah tahrimiyyah must be repeated. So the ruling of obligation of i'adah upon leaving the surah and what substitutes for it is established, like leaving the Fatihah. The Fatihah is more emphasized in obligation than the surah due to the difference regarding its being a rukn, unlike the surah, and the emphasis is not... Yes, the cause for takfir of its denier is denial of what is mutawatir in its place and what is mutawatir as Qur'an, and the consideration in proving qur'aniyyah is the first only. It has become clear that his statement here 'and by tawatur of it being Qur'an' is correct as 'and by lack of tawatur' etc. as is not hidden. And I have seen an appendix in some copies. Know that in his speech in al-Bahr there is contradiction, because he first mentioned in the aspect of the most correct that its tawatur in the mushaf is evidence of tawatur of its qur'aniyyah, and that the shubhah in its qur'aniyyah is thereby repelled, and it is known that its tawatur is in the beginnings of surahs, and he ruled that it is evidence of tawatur of its qur'aniyyah, and the necessary consequence is that it is Qur'an in the beginnings, then he ruled that there is shubhah in it, contradicting his earlier words. Likewise his statement: the cause for takfir of the denier of the Qur'an is denial of what is mutawatir as Qur'an, contradicting his earlier proof of tawatur of it being Qur'an. And likewise his statement 'that tawatur' (reported by Muslim in kitab al-salat hadith 38-40, etc.)
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligation (wujub) of reciting Surat al-Fatihah and a surah (or three verses) for the imam and the munfarid (one praying alone). The matn states that both recitations are wajib, but Fatihah is more emphatically wajib such that leaving it necessitates repetition (i'adah) of the prayer, whereas leaving the surah does not. The commentator (al-Haskafi) critiques this view, arguing that both are wajib by agreement, and leaving any wajib results in karahah tahrimiyyah (disliked to the degree of prohibition). It is a well-known principle in the Hanafi school that any prayer performed with karahah tahrimiyyah must be repeated. Therefore, leaving the surah also requires i'adah, just like leaving the Fatihah. The Fatihah is indeed more emphasized because of differences among scholars regarding its being a rukn (essential pillar), while the surah is not considered a rukn. However, in terms of actual practice, both are wajib and their omission necessitates repetition. The passage then digresses into a criticism of al-Bahr al-Raiq regarding basmalah's tawatur, pointing out a contradiction: al-Bahr first states that tawatur of basmalah in the mushaf proves its qur'aniyyah and removes shubhah, but later says there is shubhah preventing takfir. The author corrects this by explaining that tawatur in the mushaf proves qur'aniyyah, but tawatur of it being in the beginnings of surahs as part of them is not established, hence no takfir. This serves as a hashiya-like refinement.

Key Terms
الوجوب (al-wujub): Legal obligation; here it refers to the obligation of reciting Fatihah and a surah in prayer for imam and munfarid.
الإعادة (al-i'adah): Repeating the prayer due to an omission of a wajib element, which causes karahah tahrimiyyah.
كراهة التحريم (karahah tahrimiyyah): Disliked to the level of prohibition; an act that is sinful to leave but not as severe as haram. In prayer, it necessitates i'adah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator in this passage, what is the consequence of omitting the surah after Fatihah in the first two rak'ahs for an imam?
A) No consequence; the surah is recommended but not obligatory.
B) The prayer is valid but must be repeated due to karahah tahrimiyyah.
C) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
D) The imam should perform sajdah sahw.

Key Takeaway
Both Fatihah and a surah are wajib for imam and munfarid, and omission of either necessitates i'adah.

The Basmalah: Tawatur, Takfir, and Recitation by Junub
Inter-madhhab dispute on the basmalah's Qur'anicity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not deem denial of the basmalah as kufr and state the ruling on its recitation by a junub.

Core Idea
Denial of the basmalah does not entail takfir because its being Quran is not established by independent tawatur.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq tackles a nuanced issue: the basmalah is undeniably in the mushaf, but does that make its denial kufr? The Hanafi school distinguishes between tawatur of occurrence and tawatur of being Quran, leading to a shubha that prevents takfir. This dispute also affects how a person in a state of major impurity (junub) may recite the basmalah. Let's unpack the legal reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Start by identifying what the Hanafi school holds regarding the basmalah: it is a single verse that opens each surah, but its being a verse is not mutawatir in the sense required for takfir.
The passage uses 'شبهة' to explain why denial is not kufr.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opposing school is al-Shafi'i, who considers the basmalah as multiple verses forming part of each surah.
This difference has practical consequences for prayer recitation.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i likely relies on other evidence (not fully cited here) for considering the basmalah as separate verses.
The passage focuses on Hanafi evidence.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is based on two hadiths: the hadith of dividing the prayer (no basmalah mentioned) and the count of Surah al-Mulk (30 verses excluding basmalah). These indicate the basmalah is not part of the surah for recitation.
This is a dalil naqli argument.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis do not recite the basmalah aloud in prayer or count it as a verse of al-Fatihah; Shafi'is do. Additionally, the basmalah's special status creates a shubha affecting the ruling on junub recitation.
The thamarah also affects takfir.

شبهة قوية، فإن ثبتت فلا كما في البسملة. فالموجب لتكفير من أنكر القرآن إنكار ما تواتر كونه قرآناً، وأما البسملة فلما تواترت في المصحف ثبتت قرآنيتها، وبتواتر كونها قرآناً في الأوائل لم يكفر جاحدها، فالتواتر المعتبر في القرآن تواتره في محله والمعتبر في التكفير تواتر كونه قرآناً، وبهذا اندفع ما قيل من الإشكال في التسمية وهو أنها إن كانت متواترة لزم تكفير منكرها ولم يتكافروا فيها، وإن لم تكن متواترة فليست قرآناً . وأشار بقوله آية إلى أنها في القرآن آية واحدة يفتتح بها كل سورة، وعند الشافعي آيات في السور. والخلاف في غير البسملة التي في سورة النمل، أما هي فبعض آية اتفاقاً. ومما استدل به لمذهبنا حديث قسمت الصلاة بيني وبين عبدي فإذا قال الحمد الله إلى آخره (۱) فإنه لم يذكر البسملة فدل أنها ليست من الفاتحة. وحديث عد سورة الملك ثلاثين آية وهي ثلاثون دونها، والكلام في البسملة طويل بين الأئمة واستفيد من كلام المصنف أنه يحرم قراءتها على الجنب والحائض. وقيده في المحيط وغيره بأن يقرأ على قصد القرآن ومقتضى كونها قرآناً أن تحرم على الجنب إلا إذا قصد الذكر أو التيمن. وفي المجتبى : الأصح أنها آية في حق حرمتها على الجنب لا في حق جواز الصلاة بها فإن فرض القراءة ثابت بيقين فلا يسقط بما فيه شبهة، وكذا في المحيط.
A strong doubt; if it is established then no, as in the basmalah. The cause for takfir of one who denies the Quran is the denial of what is mutawatir in being Quran. As for the basmalah, since it is mutawatir in the mushaf, its Qur'anicity is established, but due to the lack of tawatur of its being Quran in the openings [of surahs], the one who denies it is not deemed a kafir. So the tawatur considered in the Quran is its tawatur in its place, and what is considered in takfir is the tawatur of its being Quran. By this, the objection raised about the basmalah is refuted: that if it were mutawatir, denial of it would necessitate takfir, yet they did not excommunicate one another regarding it, and if it is not mutawatir, then it is not Quran. He indicated by his saying 'a verse' that it is in the Quran one verse with which every surah is opened, and according to al-Shafi'i, it is multiple verses in the surahs. The difference is regarding other than the basmalah in Surah al-Naml; as for that, it is part of a verse by consensus. Among the evidence for our madhhab is the hadith: 'I divided the prayer between Me and My servant...' until the end, for he did not mention the basmalah, indicating that it is not part of al-Fatihah. And the hadith counting Surah al-Mulk as thirty verses, and it is thirty without it. The discussion on the basmalah is lengthy among the imams. It is understood from the author's words that it is prohibited to recite it for a junub and a menstruating woman. Al-Muhit and others qualified it with the intention of reciting it as Quran, and the implication of its being Quran is that it is prohibited for a junub unless he intends dhikr or tayammun. In al-Mujtaba: the correct view is that it is a verse regarding its prohibition for a junub, not regarding the validity of prayer with it, for the obligation of recitation is established with certainty, so it is not nullified by something doubtful. And similarly in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage addresses the complex issue of the basmalah's status as a Quranic verse and its implications. The author begins by discussing the concept of shubha (doubt) and its effect on takfir. He explains that denying the basmalah does not make one a kafir because its being a verse of the Quran is not established by tawatur in the sense of being known as Quran through multiple transmissions; rather, it is mutawatir in its occurrence in the mushaf. This distinction prevents takfir. The passage then clarifies the Hanafi position that the basmalah is a single verse that opens each surah, contrasting with al-Shafi'i who considers it multiple verses. Evidence from hadith is presented: the hadith dividing the prayer does not mention the basmalah, indicating it is not part of al-Fatihah; also, the counting of verses in Surah al-Mulk excludes the basmalah. Finally, the ruling on recitation by a person in a state of major ritual impurity (junub) is discussed: it is prohibited if intended as Quran recitation, but allowed if intended as dhikr. There is an intra-Hanafi nuance about the type of shubha affecting the ruling.

Key Terms
البسملة (al-basmalah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'
التواتر (al-tawatur): Multiple transmission that yields certainty
شبهة (shubhah): A doubt or ambiguity that prevents a definitive ruling, such as takfir
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, why is a person who denies the basmalah not considered a kafir?
A) Because the basmalah is not part of the Quran.
B) Because its being a verse of the Quran is not established by tawatur that it is Quran.
C) Because the basmalah is only a part of Surah al-Naml.
D) Because the imams have differing opinions.

Key Takeaway
The basmalah's Qur'anicity is mutawatir in its occurrence in the mushaf, but not in its being an independent verse, creating a shubha that prevents takfir and allows flexibility in its recitation by a junub.

Obligation of Reciting Fatiha and a Surah in Prayer
Ruling on the obligatory recitation of Fatiha and surah in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recitation of al-Fatihah and a surah in prayer and explain the consequences of omitting each.

Core Idea
Both al-Fatihah and surah are wajib; omitting either necessitates repeating the prayer.

This passage addresses the obligation of recitation in prayer for the imam and the one praying alone. The matn states that the worshiper recites al-Fatihah and a surah or three verses. The commentator clarifies that both are wajib due to the Prophet's consistent practice, but al-Fatihah is more emphasized. However, the practical consequence of omitting either is the same: the prayer must be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The recitation of al-Fatihah and a surah (or equivalent) in prayer by the imam or individual. The ruling: both are wajib.
Wajib means obligatory but not fard; the evidence is zanni.
2
Classify the hukm level
Understand that while both are wajib, al-Fatihah is more emphasized because some schools consider it a rukn. However, the Hanafi position is that both are wajib, not fard.
Emphasis (ta'kid) does not change the consequence of omission.
3
Identify the consequence of omission
Omission of either al-Fatihah or the surah results in karahah tahrirniyyah (prohibitive dislike). According to the Hanafi school, any prayer performed with karahah tahrirniyyah must be repeated.
Thus, the prayer must be repeated if either is omitted, contrary to some earlier views.
4
Distinguish between the two karahahs
The passage distinguishes between karahah tahrirniyyah (from omitting wajib) and karahah tanzihiyyah (from omitting sunnah). Reciting only the wajib amount avoids the former but not necessarily the latter.
This nuance is important for understanding the degrees of obligation.
5
Apply the sufficiency condition
The surah can be replaced by three short verses or one long verse. Reciting less than that incurs karahah tahrirniyyah.
The minimum recitation is clearly defined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وقرأ الفاتحة وسورة أو ثلاث آيات أي وقرأ المصلي إذا كان إماماً أو منفرداً على وجه الوجوب ما ذكر وهما واجبتان للمواظبة لكن الفاتحة أوجب حتى يؤمر بالإعادة بتركها دون السورة. كذا ذكره الشارح، وقد تبع فيه الفقيه وفيه نظر ظاهر لأن كلا منهما واجب اتفاقاً وبترك الواجب تثبت كراهة التحريم وقد قالوا كل صلاة أديت مع كراهة التحريم يجب إعادتها، فتعين القول بوجوب الإعادة عند ترك السورة وما يقوم مقامها كترك الفاتحة. الفاتحة أكد في الوجوب من السورة للاختلاف في ركنيتها دون السورة، والأكدية لا تظهر فيما ذكره لأن وجوب الإعادة حكم ترك الواجب مطلقاً لا الواجب المتأكد. وإنما يظهر في الإثم لأنه مقول بالتشكيك كما قدمناه والثلاث آيات القصار تقوم مقام السورة في الإعجاز فكذا هنا وكذا الآية الطويلة تقوم مقامها فإذا نقص عن ثلاث قصار أو آية طويلة فقد ارتكب كراهة التحريم لتركه الواجب، وإذا أتى بها خرج عن كراهة التحريم فإن قرأ القدر المسنون كما سيأتي فقد خرج عن كراهة التنزيه أيضاً وإلا فقد ارتكبها كما صرح به في شرح منية المصلي. فمن قال يخرج عن الكراهة إذا قرأ الواجب أراد التحريمية، ومن قال لا يخرج عنها أراد التنزيهية .
His saying: 'And he recited al-Fatihah and a surah or three verses' means that the worshiper, if he is an imam or praying alone, obligation-wise recites what was mentioned, and both are obligatory due to consistent practice, but al-Fatihah is more obligatory such that he is commanded to repeat [the prayer] by leaving it, unlike the surah. Thus the commentator mentioned, and he followed al-Faqih therein, but there is apparent consideration because each of them is obligatory by agreement, and by leaving an obligation, karahah tahrirniyyah is established, and they said: Every prayer performed with karahah tahrirniyyah must be repeated. So it is determined to say that repetition is obligatory when leaving the surah and what stands in its place just like leaving al-Fatihah. Al-Fatihah is more emphasized in obligation than the surah due to the difference of opinion regarding its being a pillar (rukn), unlike the surah, and the emphasis does not appear in what he mentioned, because the obligation of repetition is the ruling of leaving an obligation absolutely, not the emphasized obligation. Rather it appears in sin because it is said by degrees as we previously stated. And three short verses stand in place of a surah in inimitability, and similarly here, and likewise a long verse stands in its place. So if one recites less than three short verses or one long verse, he has committed karahah tahrirniyyah due to leaving the obligation, and if he recites them, he exits from karahah tahrirniyyah. If he recites the prescribed amount as will come, he exits also from karahah tanzihiyyah, otherwise he has committed it, as explicitly stated in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. So whoever said that one exits from karahah if he recites the wajib, he meant tahrirniyyah, and whoever said he does not exit from it, he meant tanzihiyyah.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage explains the obligation of recitation in prayer for the imam and the one praying alone. The matn states that the worshiper recites al-Fatihah and a surah or three verses. The commentator clarifies that both al-Fatihah and the surah are wajib (obligatory) because of the Prophet's consistent practice (muwazabah). However, al-Fatihah is more emphasized because some scholars consider it a rukn (pillar) of prayer, whereas the surah is not. Despite this, the commentator argues that leaving either of them results in karahah tahrirniyyah (prohibitively disliked), which necessitates repeating the prayer. Thus, the practical outcome is that the prayer must be repeated if either is omitted, even though the surah is less emphasized. The passage also discusses what qualifies as a surah: three short verses or one long verse are sufficient. If the worshiper recites only what is obligatory, he avoids the prohibited dislike but may still incur recommended dislike if he does not recite the sunnah amount. This subtle distinction between two types of karahah is important.

Key Terms
الفاتحة (al-fatihah): The first chapter of the Quran, recited in prayer
السورة (al-surah): A chapter of the Quran or a portion thereof equivalent to three short verses or one long verse
الواجب (al-wajib): An obligation that is not fard; its omission incurs sin and may require compensation
كراهة التحريم (karahah tahrirniyyah): Prohibitive dislike; an act that is closer to haram but not definitively so; its commission requires repentance and may necessitate repeating the prayer
كراهة التنزيه (karahah tanzihiyyah): Light dislike; an act that is better to avoid but not sinful

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of leaving the recitation of a surah (or three verses) in prayer?
A) The prayer is valid but deficient.
B) The prayer must be repeated due to karahah tahrirniyyah.
C) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
D) No consequence because it is only sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Both al-Fatihah and the surah are wajib in Hanafi prayer; omitting either necessitates repetition due to karahah tahrirniyyah.
