Ruling on Tashbihat in Ruku' and Sujud
Explains the Hanafi position on tashbihat and refutes the view of obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers tashbihat in ruku' and sujud to be sunnah muakkadah and not wajib, and apply the concept of sarif to differentiate between obligation and recommendation.

Core Idea
Tashbihat are sunnah muakkadah, not wajib, because the Prophet omitted them when teaching the Bedouin.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the Hanafi ruling on the tashbihat (glorifications) recited during ruku' and sujud. While the hadith commands appear to obligate them, the Hanafi school holds they are a confirmed sunnah. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the key concept of a 'sarif' (diverting factor), and the practical implications for the worshipper.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act under discussion: the tashbihat said in ruku' and sujud. State the Hanafi ruling: sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence: the hadith in Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud where the Prophet commands to say 'Subhana Rabbi al-Adheem' in ruku' and 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' in sujud.
The command 'اجعلوها' is in the imperative form.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the dalil proves obligation. The imperative form apparently indicates wujub in Hanafi usul. But the school interprets it as recommendation.
The apparent meaning is obligation, but a diverting factor (sarif) changes it.
4
Identify the sarif
Identify the sarif: the Prophet did not mention tashbihat when he taught the Bedouin the basics of prayer. If it were obligatory, he would have mentioned it.
This shows the command is for recommendation, not obligation.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that some Hanafis (Abu Muti' al-Balkhi) and other schools (Ahmad) consider it wajib or a pillar. The Hanafi response: the command is on the act of bowing and sujud unconditionally; making tasbih a condition would abrogate the Quran with a khabar wahid, which is impermissible.
The Hanafi position reconciles both proofs by making tasbih sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة
وذلك أدناه، وإذا سجد فليقل سبحان ربي الأعلى ثلاثاً وذلك أدناه»(۱) وفي صحيح مسلم أنه كان يقول في ركوعه سبحان ربي العظيم، وفي سجوده سبحان ربي الأعلى. وفي سنن أبي داود : لما نزلت فسبح باسم ربك العظيم [الواقعة : ٧٤] قال : اجعلوها في ركوعكم . فلما نزلت سبح اسم ربك الأعلى ﴾ [الأعلى : ١] قال : اجعلوها في سجودكم. وظاهر هذا الأمر الوجوب . روي عن أبي مطيع البلخي أن التسبيحات ركن لو تركه لا تجوز صلاته كما في الذخيرة والذي في البدائع عنه أن من نقص من الثلاث في تسبيحات الركوع والسجود لا تجوز صلاته قال : وهذا فاسد لأن الأمر تعلق بفعل الركوع والسجود مطلقاً عن شرط التسبيح فلا يجوز نسخ الكتاب بخبر الواحد، فقلنا بالجاز مع كون التسبيح سنة عملاً بالدليلين بقدر الإمكان اهـ. وقد بحث فيه العلامة ابن أمير حاج الحلبي بأنه لا يتعين العمل بالدليلين في جعل التسبيح سنة بل يكون ذلك أيضاً في جعله واجباً والمواظبة الظاهرة من حاله والأمر به متظافران على الوجوب، فينبغي إذا تركه سهواً أن يجب السجود، وإذا تركه عمداً يؤمر بالإعادة. ونقل ابن هبيرة وغيره أنه مرة واحدة في كل منهما، والتسميع والتحميد وسؤال المغفرة بين السجدتين والتكبيرات واجب في الرواية المشهورة عن أحمد إلا أنه إن ترك شيئاً منها عمداً بطلت صلاته، وسهواً لا ويسجد للسهو .اهـ. وقد يقال : إنما لم يكن واجباً عندنا لوجود الصارف وهو أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام لم يذكره للأعرابي حين علمه ولو كان واجباً لذكره له ، والمواظبة لم تنقل صريحاً وهذا الصارف منع من القول بها ظاهراً فلهذا كان الأمر للاستحباب صرح به غیر واحد من المشايخ. فعلى هذا فالمراد من الكراهة في قولهم لو ترك التسبيحات أصلاً أو نقص عن الثلاث فهو مكروه كراهة التنزيه لأنها في مقابلة المستحب. واختلف في معنى قوله وذلك أدناه فقيل أدنى كمال السنة وقيل أدنى كمال التسبيح، وقيل أدنى القول المسنون والأول أوجه وعلى كل فالزيادة على الثلاث أفضل ويستحب أن يختم على وتر خمس سبع أو تسع لحديث الصحيحين إن الله وتر يحب الوتر » (۲) ولا ينبغي للإمام أن يطيل على وجه يمل القوم لأنه سبب للتنفير وأنه مكروه ولهذا قال الأسبيجابي : ولو كان إماماً يقولها ثلاثاً على قول بعضهم. وقال بعضهم : يقولها أربعاً حتى يتمكن المقتدي من الثلاث، ولو أطال
أقول : هو من علماء الحنابلة . قوله : (وهو) أنه عليه السلام لم يذكره للإعرابي الخ) هذا إنما يتم على تقدير أنه عليه السلام علمه الفرائض والواجبات كلها ولم يترك له شيئاً منها وليس كذلك.
Book of Prayer - Chapter on Description of Prayer. And that is its minimum, and when he prostrates let him say 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' three times and that is its minimum. And in Sahih Muslim that he used to say in his bowing 'Subhana Rabbi al-'Adheem' and in his prostration 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la'. And in Sunan Abi Dawud: When was revealed 'So glorify the name of your Lord, the Most Great' [56:74] he said: 'Place it in your bowing.' When was revealed 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High' [87:1] he said: 'Place it in your prostration.' The apparent [meaning] of this command is obligation. It is narrated from Abu Muti' al-Balkhi that the tashbihat are a pillar; if one abandons them his prayer is not valid, as in al-Dhakhira. And what is in al-Bada'i' from him is that whoever reduces from three in the tashbihat of bowing and prostration, his prayer is not valid. He said: This is corrupt because the command is attached to the act of bowing and prostration absolutely without the condition of tasbih, so it is not permissible to abrogate the Book with a khabar al-wahid. So we said permissibility while the tasbih is sunnah, acting on both proofs as much as possible, end. And 'Allamah Ibn Amir Hajj al-Halabi discussed it, saying: Acting on both proofs is not confined to making tasbih sunnah; rather it could also be making it wajib, and the apparent constancy from his practice and the command are concurrent upon obligation. So if one abandons it forgetfully, sajdah should become obligatory; if deliberately, he should be ordered to repeat. And Ibn Hubayrah and others narrated that it is once in each, and tasmi', tahmid, asking for forgiveness between the two prostrations, and the takbirs are wajib in the well-known narration from Ahmad, except that if one abandons any of them deliberately his prayer is nullified, and forgetfully not, and he does sajdah al-sahw, end. And it may be said: It is not wajib with us because of the diverting factor: that he, peace be upon him, did not mention it to the Bedouin when he taught him; and had it been wajib he would have mentioned it. And constancy was not explicitly transmitted, and this diverting factor prevents saying it apparently. Hence the command is for recommendation, as explicitly stated by more than one of the mashayikh. According to this, what is meant by karahah in their statement that if one abandons the tashbihat entirely or reduces from three, it is makruh tanzihan because it is in opposition to the mustahabb. And they differed on the meaning of 'that is its minimum': it was said the minimum perfection of the sunnah, and it was said the minimum perfection of tasbih, and it was said the minimum of the prescribed saying; the first is more appropriate. In any case, increasing beyond three is better and it is recommended to end on an odd number, five, seven, or nine, due to the hadith of the two Sahihs: 'Indeed Allah is odd and loves oddness.' And it is not appropriate for the imam to prolong in a way that wearies the people because it is a cause of aversion and it is makruh. For this reason al-Asbijabi said: If he is an imam, he should say them three times according to some. And some said: he should say them four times so that the follower can manage three. And if he prolongs... I say: He is of the Hanabila scholars. His statement: (And that is) that he, peace be upon him, did not mention it to the Bedouin etc. This is only valid on the assumption that he taught him all the obligatory acts and duties and did not leave anything out for him, and that is not so.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof on the status of tashbihat (glorifications) in ruku' and sujud. The author begins with the hadith evidence: the Prophet commanded to say 'Subhana Rabbi al-'Adheem' in ruku' and 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' in sujud. The apparent command indicates obligation, but the Hanafi school holds it is sunnah, not wajib. The reasoning: the command is attached to the act of bowing and prostration unconditionally; making tasbih a condition would be like abrogating vague obligation (from the Quran) with a solitary hadith, which is impermissible. Thus both proofs are reconciled by making the tasbih sunnah, preserving the obligation of the act itself. Al-Marghinani then discusses the view of Ibn Amir Hajj al-Halabi who argued that the evidence could also be interpreted as wajib, but the Hanafi position is confirmed by the fact that the Prophet did not mention it to the Bedouin when he taught him the fundamentals—had it been obligatory, he would have. The passage also explains that the minimum of tashbihat is three, and the minimum meaning is debated: whether it is the minimum perfection of the sunnah, of tasbih, or of the prescribed saying. Increasing is better. The imam should not prolong to avoid wearying the congregation. The marginal note clarifies that the argument from the Bedouin hadith is not conclusive because the Prophet might not have mentioned all details.

Key Terms
التسبيحات (al-tashbihat): Glories said in ruku' and sujud, specifically 'Subhana Rabbi al-'Adheem' and 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la'.
أدناه (adnahu): The minimum of the sunnah, or the minimum perfection of tasbih, or the minimum of the prescribed saying.
صارف (sarif): A diverting factor that turns the meaning of a command from obligation to recommendation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the hadith evidence is weak.
B) Because the Prophet did not mention them when teaching the Bedouin the basics of prayer.
C) Because the Quran does not mention them.
D) Because the Sahaba disagreed.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the tashbihat in ruku' and sujud are a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation, based on the principle of acting on both proofs and the Prophet's omission when teaching the Bedouin.

Waiting in Ruku' for a Latecomer: Ruling and Danger of Shirk
Ruling and scholarly discussion on prolonging ruku' for latecomer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on waiting in ruku' for a latecomer and explain why Abu Hanifa feared shirk.

Core Idea
Prolonging ruku' for a latecomer is makruh tahrimi as it risks riya' (minor shirk), but not apostasy.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the commentator discusses the ruling on an imam prolonging his ruku' to allow a latecomer to join the congregation. He presents Abu Hanifa's severe warning about shirk and clarifies that it refers to riya' (showing off), not outright disbelief. This lesson will help you understand the nuanced Hanafi position and distinguish between different scholarly interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'waiting in ruku' for a latecomer' — intentionally prolonging the bowing posture to let someone catch the rak'ah. The ruling given is 'makruh'.
The text states: 'فهو مكروه'
2
Locate the dalil and its meaning
The proof is Abu Hanifa's statement: 'I fear for him a great matter, meaning shirk.' This indicates that the act involves a risk of riya' (showing off), which is a form of minor shirk.
The Quranic verse (18:110) condemns shirk in actions.
3
Trace the misunderstanding and correction
Some scholars misunderstood Abu Hanifa to mean literal kufr. The commentator explains that the Imam meant shirk in intention (riya'), not apostasy, and that this is not certain due to conflicting opinions.
The author of Munyat al-Musalli feared kufr but was corrected.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a spectrum: al-Balkhi said the prayer becomes invalid and leads to kufr; al-Jami' al-Saghir said the person is rewarded; Abu al-Layth made a distinction based on whether the person knows the latecomer or not.
This shows the range of views within the school.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that the act is makruh tahrimi and should be avoided to prevent riya'. It is not kufr nor does it invalidate the prayer.
This is based on Abu Hanifa's cautionary view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمنفرد بالتحميد ثم كبر ووضع ركبتيه ثم يديه ثم وجهه بين كفيه بعكس النهوض
الركوع لإدراك الجائي لا تقر بالله تعالى فهو مكروه. وفي الذخيرة والبدائع وغيرهما قال أبو يوسف : سألت أبا حنيفة عن ذلك فقال : أخشى عليه أمراً عظيماً يعني الشرك. وقد وهم بعضهم في فهم كلام الإمام فاعتقد منه أن يصير المنتظر مشركاً يباح دمه فأفتى بإباحة دمه، وهكذا ظن صاحب منية المصلي فقال : يخشى عليه الكفر، ولا يكفر وكل منهما غلط ولم يرده الإمام رحمه الله تعالى بل أراد أنه يخاف عليه الشرك في عمله الذي هو الرياء وإنما لم يقطع بالرياء في عمله لما أنه غير مقطوع به لوجود الاختلاف فإنه نقل عن الشعبي أنه لا بأس به وهو قول الشافعي في القديم وقد نهى الله عن الإشراك في العمل بقوه تعالى فمن كان . لقاء ربه يرجو [الكهف: ۱۱۰] الآية . وأعجب منه ما نقله في المجتبى عن البلخي أنه تفسد صلاته ويكفر . ثم نقل بعده عن الجامع الأصغر أنه مأجور على ذلك لقوله تعالى وتعاونوا على البر والتقوى [المائدة : ٢] وعن أبي الليث أنه حسن وعنه التفصيل بين أن يعرف الجائي فلا أو لا فنعم .
And the individual suffices with tahmid, then he says takbir and places his knees, then his hands, then his face between his palms, opposite to rising. Waiting in ruku' to catch the latecomer, 'لا تقر بالله تعالى' so it is makruh. And in al-Dhakhira, al-Bada'i' and others: Abu Yusuf said: I asked Abu Hanifa about that, and he said: I fear for him a great matter, meaning shirk. And some mistakenly understood the Imam's statement, thinking that the one waiting becomes a mushrik whose blood is permissible, so they gave fatwa of permissibility of his blood. Similarly, the author of Munyat al-Musalli thought and said: He is feared of kufr, but he does not become kafir. Both are mistakes, and the Imam, may Allah have mercy on him, did not mean that; rather he meant that he fears shirk in his action which is riya', but he did not definitively say it is riya' in his action because it is not certain due to existing difference. For it is narrated from al-Sha'bi that there is no harm in it, and it is the old view of al-Shafi'i, and Allah has forbidden shirk in action by His saying: 'So whoever hopes for the meeting with his Lord' [18:110] the verse. And more astonishing is what is transmitted in al-Mujtaba from al-Balkhi that his prayer becomes invalid and he becomes a kafir. Then after that it is transmitted from al-Jami' al-Saghir that he is rewarded for that due to His saying: 'And cooperate in righteousness and piety' [5:2], and from Abu al-Layth that it is good, and from him the detail: if he can recognize the latecomer or not.
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with scholarly discussion on the issue of waiting in ruku' for a latecomer to join the congregation. The author states that it is makruh. When Abu Yusuf asked Abu Hanifa about it, he responded with a severe warning: 'I fear for him a great matter,' meaning shirk (associating partners with Allah). Some scholars misunderstood this to mean that the person becomes a literal mushrik deserving death, and even some later writers like the author of Munyat al-Musalli thought it could lead to kufr. The commentator clarifies that this is a misunderstanding. Imam Abu Hanifa meant that such waiting can involve riya' (showing off), which is a form of minor shirk in intention. However, he did not definitively declare it as riya' because there is a difference of opinion: al-Sha'bi saw no harm, and it was the old view of Imam al-Shafi'i. The commentator then presents conflicting reports: al-Balkhi in al-Mujtaba says the prayer is invalid and leads to kufr; al-Jami' al-Saghir says the person is rewarded based on the verse on cooperation; and Abu al-Layth finds it good with a detail. The passage shows the range of Hanafi positions on this issue, with the cautionary stance of Abu Hanifa being the most well-known.

Key Terms
الركوع لإدراك الجائي (al-ruku' li-idrak al-ja'i): Prolonging the ruku' (or sujud) intentionally to allow a latecomer to catch that rak'ah.
الرياء (al-riya'): Showing off in worship, considered minor shirk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) That he becomes a disbeliever and his blood is permissible.
B) That his action contains riya' (showing off), which is a form of shirk.
C) That his prayer is valid but he loses reward.
D) That he must repeat his prayer.

Key Takeaway
Prolonging ruku' for a latecomer is makruh tahrimi due to the risk of riya', but it does not constitute apostasy or invalidate the prayer.

The Hanafi Ruling on Tasmi' and Tahmid for Imam and Follower
Inter-madhhab dispute on tasmi' and tahmid after ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tasmi' and tahmid for the imam, follower, and individual, and evaluate the opposing views based on the hadith.

Core Idea
The hadith divides tasmi' and tahmid between imam and follower, and division precludes combination.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common point of confusion in prayer: who says what after rising from ruku'. The Hanafi school draws a clear boundary based on a prophetic instruction, while other scholars allow combination. This lesson examines the evidence and the reasoning behind the Hanafi position, including a note on the individual praying alone.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the imam and follower each say after rising from ruku'. The imam says 'Sami' Allahu liman hamidah' (tasmi') only; the follower says 'Rabbana lakal hamd' (tahmid) only.
This is based on the explicit division in the hadith.
2
Identify the opposing views
Recognize that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that the imam combines both tasmi' and tahmid, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the follower combines both.
Both opposing views rely on the Prophet's action of combining.
3
Follow the opposing proof
The Sahibayn and Shafi'i argue that 'al-qawl muqaddam 'ala al-fi'l' (the statement is given precedence over action). Since the Prophet's action of combining is known, and the hadith is a statement, they give precedence to the action over the statement? Actually, they use the action as evidence that combination is permissible. The passage notes the Sahibayn use the proof that the Prophet used to combine both.
The proof is: the Prophet's practice (fi'l) indicates permissibility of combination.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the hadith explicitly divides (qisma) between imam and follower. Division precludes partnership (shirka). The Prophet's action of combining is overridden by his explicit statement. In Hanafi usul, a clear statement (qawl) takes precedence over action when there is conflict.
Thus the division in the hadith is the primary evidence, and the action is interpreted as specific to the Prophet's own practice, not instructional for the ummah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In the Hanafi school, the imam says only tasmi', the follower only tahmid. In the Shafi'i school, the follower says both. According to the Sahibayn, the imam says both. This affects how a muqtadi and imam perform salah when following a Hanafi imam.
The mufta bihi (relied upon) position is the Hanafi one, supported by the explicit hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ثم رفع رأسه) أي من الركوع، وقد تقدم حكم هذا الرفع في عد الواجبات قوله واكتفى الإمام بالتسميع والمؤتم والمنفرد بالتحميد) الحديث الصحيحين إذا قال الإمام سمع الله لمن حمده فقولوا ربنا لك الحمد» (۱) فقسم بينهما والقسمة تنافي الشركة فكان حجة على أبي يوسف ومحمد القائلين بأن الإمام يجمع بينهما استدلالاً بأنه عليه السلام كان يجمع بينهما لأن القول مقدم على الفعل وحجة على الشافعي في قوله إن المقتدي يجمع بين الذكرين أيضاً، وحكاه الأقطع رواية عن أبي حنيفة وهو غريب فإن صاحب الذخيرة نقل أنه لا يأتي بالتسميع بلا خلاف بين أصحابنا . وأما المنفرد ففيه ثلاثة أقوال : الأول أنه يأتي بالتسميع لا غير وهو رواية المعلى عن أبي يوسف عن أبي حنيفة، وينبغي أن لا يعول عليها ولم أر من صححها. (ولم أر من صححها قال في النهر : قد رأيت ذلك ولله المنة ففي السراج عن شيخ الإسلام أنها الأصح. وقال الرازي: ينبغي على قول الإمام أن يقتصر المنفرد عليه لأنه إما في حق نفسه. قوله: (وصححه في الهداية قال الرملي قال الحلبي وتصحيح الهداية أولى .اهـ. وسيأتي أنه المرجح من (۱) رواه البخاري في كتب الأذان باب ٥٢، ٧٤ ۸۲ ۸۶ مسلم في كتاب الصلاة حديث ٢٥، ٢٨، .. أبو داود في كتاب الصلاة باب ٦٨ الترمذي في كتاب الصلاة باب ۸۲، ۸۳. الموطأ في كتاب النداء حديث ١٦.
His statement (then he raised his head) i.e. from ruku', and the ruling of this raising has preceded in counting the obligatory acts. His statement: and the imam suffices with tasmi', and the follower and the individual with tahmid. The hadith of the two Sahihs: 'When the imam says Sami' Allahu liman hamidah, then say Rabbana lakal hamd.' So he divided between them, and division precludes partnership. So this is an argument against Abu Yusuf and Muhammad who say that the imam combines both, using as evidence that he (peace be upon him) used to combine both, because saying is given precedence over action. And it is an argument against al-Shafi'i in his statement that the follower also combines both remembrances. And al-Aqta' narrated it as a transmission from Abu Hanifa, but it is strange, for the author of al-Dhakhira transmitted that he does not come with tasmi' without any disagreement among our scholars. As for the individual, there are three sayings: The first is that he comes with tasmi' only, and it is a transmission from al-Mu'alla from Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa, and one should not rely on it, and I have not seen anyone who authenticated it. (And I have not seen anyone who authenticated it. He said in al-Nahr: I have seen that, and praise be to Allah, for in al-Siraj from Shaykh al-Islam that it is the most authentic. And al-Razi said: According to the statement of the Imam, the individual should confine himself to it because it is for his own sake. His statement: (And he authenticated it in al-Hidayah. Al-Ramli said, al-Halabi said, and the authentication of al-Hidayah is better, end. And it will come that the preferred (from) ...
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the phrases said after rising from ruku': tasmi' ('Sami' Allahu liman hamidah') and tahmid ('Rabbana lakal hamd'). The author states the Hanafi position: the imam says tasmi' only, the follower says tahmid only, and the individual (munfarid) has a choice. The proof is the hadith from the two Sahihs where the Prophet said: 'When the imam says Sami' Allahu liman hamidah, then say Rabbana lakal hamd.' This division (imam says tasmi', follower says tahmid) precludes combination, so it refutes the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad who thought the imam combines both, and al-Shafi'i who said the follower combines both. The individual (praying alone) has three opinions: (1) he says tasmi' only (a weak transmission from Abu Hanifa), (2) he says tahmid only, (3) he combines both. The preferred view in al-Hidayah is that the individual says tasmi' only, as it is more consistent with the imam's role. The text concludes that this is the preferred view ('al-murajjah').

Key Terms
التسميع (al-tasmi'): Saying 'Sami' Allahu liman hamidah' (Allah hears those who praise Him).
التحميد (al-tahmid): Saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd' (Our Lord, to You is praise).
المنفرد (al-munfarid): A person praying alone (not in congregation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should the imam say after raising from ruku'?
A) 'Sami' Allahu liman hamidah' only.
B) 'Rabbana lakal hamd' only.
C) Both 'Sami' Allahu liman hamidah' and 'Rabbana lakal hamd'.
D) Nothing; it is silent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the imam says tasmi' only and the follower says tahmid only, based on the explicit division in the hadith.

Ruling on Bowing for a Latecomer (al-Ruku' li-Idrak al-Ja'i)
Ruling on bowing for a latecomer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bowing for a latecomer without takbir and explain why it is makruh, not kufr.

Core Idea
Bowing for a latecomer without takbir is makruh due to fear of riya, not kufr.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a controversial issue: what is the ruling if a person already in prayer bows to allow a latecomer to join but forgets or omits the takbir? Some scholars mistakenly thought this makes one a mushrik. The text explains the correct Hanafi position and the reason for the fear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is bowing (ruku') performed by a person already in prayer to allow a latecomer to join the congregation, but without saying 'Allahu Akbar'.
The takbir is normally wajib when moving from one posture to another.
2
State the explicit ruling
The text explicitly rules it as makruh (disliked).
Makruh in Hanafi fiqh means close to haram but not prohibited; avoiding it is rewardable.
3
Analyze the reason given
Abu Hanifa feared 'a great matter' meaning shirk, but the commentator clarifies this refers to shirk in action (riya), not actual disbelief.
Riya is showing off, which is condemned.
4
Distinguish correct understanding from misunderstanding
Some scholars misunderstood and thought the person becomes a mushrik. The text corrects this: it is makruh, and the fear is of riya, not kufr.
Calling someone a kafir has severe consequences; caution is needed.
5
Note differing opinions
The text mentions other views: al-Sha'bi said no harm; al-Shafi'i's old view; al-Balkhi said invalid and kufr; al-Jami' al-Saghir said rewarded; Abu al-Layth said good. The Hanafi mufta bihi is makruh.
Ikhtilaf exists; the mufta bihi is the sound Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة
والمنفرد بالتحميد ثم كبر ووضع ركبتيه ثم يديه ثم وجهه بين كفيه بعكس النهوض
الركوع لإدراك الجائي لا تقر بالله تعالى فهو مكروه. وفي الذخيرة والبدائع وغيرهما قال أبو يوسف : سألت أبا حنيفة عن ذلك فقال : أخشى عليه أمراً عظيماً يعني الشرك. وقد وهم بعضهم في فهم كلام الإمام فاعتقد منه أن يصير المنتظر مشركاً يباح دمه فأفتى بإباحة دمه، وهكذا ظن صاحب منية المصلي فقال : يخشى عليه الكفر، ولا يكفر وكل منهما غلط ولم يرده الإمام رحمه الله تعالى بل أراد أنه يخاف عليه الشرك في عمله الذي هو الرياء وإنما لم يقطع بالرياء في عمله لما أنه غير مقطوع به لوجود الاختلاف فإنه نقل عن الشعبي أنه لا بأس به وهو قول الشافعي في القديم وقد نهى الله عن الإشراك في العمل بقوله تعالى فمن كان . لقاء ربه يرجو [الكهف: ۱۱۰] الآية . وأعجب منه ما نقله في المجتبى عن البلخي أنه تفسد صلاته ويكفر . ثم نقل بعده عن الجامع الأصغر أنه مأجور على ذلك لقوله تعالى وتعاونوا على البر والتقوى [المائدة : ٢] وعن أبي الليث أنه حسن وعنه التفصيل بين أن يعرف الجائي فلا أو لا فنعم . وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لا يأتي في ركوعه وسجوده بغير التسبيحات، وما ورد في السنة من غيرها فمحمول على النوافل تهجداً أو غيره. ولو رفع الإمام رأسه قبل أن يتم المأموم التسبيحات فيه روايتان أصحهما وجوب المتابعة بخلاف ما لو سلم قبل أن يتم المقتدي التشهد فإنه لا يتابعه لأن قراءة التشهد واجبة كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان .
The Book of Prayer - Chapter: Description of Prayer. And the individual (praying alone) says tahmid, then says takbir, and places his knees, then his hands, then his face between his palms, contrary to the manner of rising. Bowing to catch up with the latecomer—if he does not say 'Allahu Akbar'—it is makruh. In al-Dhakhira, al-Bada'i, and others, Abu Yusuf said: I asked Abu Hanifa about that, and he said: I fear for him a great matter, meaning shirk. And some scholars misunderstood the Imam's statement and thought that the one waiting becomes a mushrik whose blood is permissible, so they gave a fatwa permitting his blood. Similarly, the author of Munyat al-Musalli thought that, saying: fear of kufr for him, but he does not become a kafir. Both are mistakes; the Imam (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mean that, but rather he meant that he fears shirk in his action, which is riya (showing off). And he did not definitively say it is riya because it is not definitive due to difference of opinion, for it is narrated from al-Sha'bi that there is no harm in it, and it is the old view of al-Shafi'i. Allah forbade shirk in action by His word: 'So whoever hopes for the meeting with his Lord' [18:110]. And more surprising is what is narrated in al-Mujtaba from al-Balkhi: that his prayer is invalidated and he becomes a kafir. Then after that, it is narrated from al-Jami' al-Saghir that he is rewarded for that due to His word: 'And cooperate in righteousness and piety' [5:2]. And from Abu al-Layth that it is good, and from him a distinction: if he knows the one coming, then no (?) otherwise yes. And the author indicated that he does not recite in his ruku' and sujud other than the tasbihat, and whatever is reported in the Sunnah other than that is taken to apply to supererogatory prayers, whether tahajjud or other. And if the imam raises his head before the follower completes the tasbihat, there are two narrations; the more authentic is the obligation of following, contrary to the case if he says the salam before the follower completes the tashahhud, for he does not follow him because reciting the tashahhud is obligatory. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan.
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering several rulings within the chapter on prayer. First, it discusses the case of a person already in prayer who sees a latecomer and bows to allow him to catch up; if he does not say 'Allahu Akbar' when bowing, it is makruh (disliked). Abu Hanifa feared that this omission could lead to shirk (associating partners with Allah) in terms of riya (showing off), but he did not declare it kufr. Some scholars misunderstood this and wrongly considered the person a mushrik; the commentator clarifies that the fear is of shirk in action (riya), not actual kufr. The text then notes that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq indicates that during ruku' and sujud, one should only recite the prescribed tasbih (subhanallah) and not other verses; any extra recitation from the Sunnah is specific to nafl prayers. Finally, the ruling on following the imam: if the imam raises his head from ruku' before the follower completes the tasbihat, the follower must follow the imam immediately (obligation of mutaba'a). However, if the imam says salam before the follower completes tashahhud, the follower does not follow immediately because tashahhud is individually wajib. These rulings show the nuanced balance between following the imam and completing one's own obligations.

Key Terms
الركوع لإدراك الجائي (al-ruku' li-idrak al-ja'i): Bowing performed by someone already in prayer to allow a latecomer to join the congregation.
الرياء (al-riya): Showing off in worship; doing acts to be seen by others rather than for Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person bows for a latecomer without saying 'Allahu Akbar'?
A) The prayer becomes invalid.
B) It is makruh.
C) It is permissible and rewarded.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Bowing for a latecomer without takbir is makruh due to fear of riya, not kufr.

Ruling on Tasbihat in Ruku' and Sujud
Ruling on recitation in ruku' and sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that in fard prayers, only the prescribed tasbih is recited in ruku' and sujud, and that extra recitations are for nafl prayers.

Core Idea
In fard prayers, ruku' and sujud are only for tasbih; extra Quranic recitation is for nafl.

The text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, as commented upon here, indicates that during ruku' and sujud, the worshipper should only recite the prescribed tasbihat (subhanallah, etc.). Any additional Quranic verses or supplications reported in the Sunnah are specifically for supererogatory prayers, not fard. This ruling maintains the distinct function of each posture in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling's source
The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq indicated that one does not recite in ruku' and sujud other than the tasbihat.
Tasbihat refers to the specific glorifications like 'Subhana Rabbiyal Adheem'.
2
Understand the scope
The ruling applies to fard (obligatory) prayers.
The text says 'what is reported in the Sunnah other than that is taken to apply to supererogatory prayers'.
3
Distinguish between fard and nafl
Extra recitations (e.g., verses from Quran) are allowed in nafl prayers but not in fard.
This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who sometimes recited more in nafl.

Ruling on Following the Imam: Raising Head vs. Tashahhud
Rulings on following the imam in specific actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the obligation to follow the imam in raising the head from ruku' (obligatory) and the non-obligation to follow the imam in ending prayer before completing tashahhud.

Core Idea
The follower must follow the imam in raising the head even if his tasbih is incomplete, but must not follow if the imam says salam before he completes tashahhud.

This passage presents a nuanced ruling in congregational prayer: the obligation of following the imam (mutaba'a) is not absolute. When the imam raises his head from ruku', the follower must follow immediately, even if he hasn't completed his tasbih. However, when the imam says the final salam, the follower must not follow if he has not yet finished his tashahhud. This distinction arises from the different legal weight of the actions: tasbih is sunnah, while tashahhud is wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Scenario 1: Imam raises his head from ruku' before the follower completes tasbih. Scenario 2: Imam says salam before the follower completes tashahhud.
2
State the ruling for each
Scenario 1: According to the more authentic narration, the follower must follow the imam (obligatory). Scenario 2: The follower does not follow the imam; he must complete his tashahhud.
3
Understand the reason for the difference
The tasbih in ruku' is a sunnah; following the imam takes precedence. Tashahhud is wajib (obligatory); hence the follower must complete it before ending the prayer.
Wajib in Hanafi means necessary but not a pillar; its omission is compensated by sajdah sahw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة
والمنفرد بالتحميد ثم كبر ووضع ركبتيه ثم يديه ثم وجهه بين كفيه بعكس النهوض
الركوع لإدراك الجائي لا تقر بالله تعالى فهو مكروه. وفي الذخيرة والبدائع وغيرهما قال أبو يوسف : سألت أبا حنيفة عن ذلك فقال : أخشى عليه أمراً عظيماً يعني الشرك. وقد وهم بعضهم في فهم كلام الإمام فاعتقد منه أن يصير المنتظر مشركاً يباح دمه فأفتى بإباحة دمه، وهكذا ظن صاحب منية المصلي فقال : يخشى عليه الكفر، ولا يكفر وكل منهما غلط ولم يرده الإمام رحمه الله تعالى بل أراد أنه يخاف عليه الشرك في عمله الذي هو الرياء وإنما لم يقطع بالرياء في عمله لما أنه غير مقطوع به لوجود الاختلاف فإنه نقل عن الشعبي أنه لا بأس به وهو قول الشافعي في القديم وقد نهى الله عن الإشراك في العمل بقوله تعالى فمن كان . لقاء ربه يرجو [الكهف: ۱۱۰] الآية . وأعجب منه ما نقله في المجتبى عن البلخي أنه تفسد صلاته ويكفر . ثم نقل بعده عن الجامع الأصغر أنه مأجور على ذلك لقوله تعالى وتعاونوا على البر والتقوى [المائدة : ٢] وعن أبي الليث أنه حسن وعنه التفصيل بين أن يعرف الجائي فلا أو لا فنعم . وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لا يأتي في ركوعه وسجوده بغير التسبيحات، وما ورد في السنة من غيرها فمحمول على النوافل تهجداً أو غيره. ولو رفع الإمام رأسه قبل أن يتم المأموم التسبيحات فيه روايتان أصحهما وجوب المتابعة بخلاف ما لو سلم قبل أن يتم المقتدي التشهد فإنه لا يتابعه لأن قراءة التشهد واجبة كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان .
The Book of Prayer - Chapter: Description of Prayer. And the individual (praying alone) says tahmid, then says takbir, and places his knees, then his hands, then his face between his palms, contrary to the manner of rising. Bowing to catch up with the latecomer—if he does not say 'Allahu Akbar'—it is makruh. In al-Dhakhira, al-Bada'i, and others, Abu Yusuf said: I asked Abu Hanifa about that, and he said: I fear for him a great matter, meaning shirk. And some scholars misunderstood the Imam's statement and thought that the one waiting becomes a mushrik whose blood is permissible, so they gave a fatwa permitting his blood. Similarly, the author of Munyat al-Musalli thought that, saying: fear of kufr for him, but he does not become a kafir. Both are mistakes; the Imam (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mean that, but rather he meant that he fears shirk in his action, which is riya (showing off). And he did not definitively say it is riya because it is not definitive due to difference of opinion, for it is narrated from al-Sha'bi that there is no harm in it, and it is the old view of al-Shafi'i. Allah forbade shirk in action by His word: 'So whoever hopes for the meeting with his Lord' [18:110]. And more surprising is what is narrated in al-Mujtaba from al-Balkhi: that his prayer is invalidated and he becomes a kafir. Then after that, it is narrated from al-Jami' al-Saghir that he is rewarded for that due to His word: 'And cooperate in righteousness and piety' [5:2]. And from Abu al-Layth that it is good, and from him a distinction: if he knows the one coming, then no (?) otherwise yes. And the author indicated that he does not recite in his ruku' and sujud other than the tasbihat, and whatever is reported in the Sunnah other than that is taken to apply to supererogatory prayers, whether tahajjud or other. And if the imam raises his head before the follower completes the tasbihat, there are two narrations; the more authentic is the obligation of following, contrary to the case if he says the salam before the follower completes the tashahhud, for he does not follow him because reciting the tashahhud is obligatory. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan.
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering several rulings within the chapter on prayer. First, it discusses the case of a person already in prayer who sees a latecomer and bows to allow him to catch up; if he does not say 'Allahu Akbar' when bowing, it is makruh (disliked). Abu Hanifa feared that this omission could lead to shirk (associating partners with Allah) in terms of riya (showing off), but he did not declare it kufr. Some scholars misunderstood this and wrongly considered the person a mushrik; the commentator clarifies that the fear is of shirk in action (riya), not actual kufr. The text then notes that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq indicates that during ruku' and sujud, one should only recite the prescribed tasbih (subhanallah) and not other verses; any extra recitation from the Sunnah is specific to nafl prayers. Finally, the ruling on following the imam: if the imam raises his head from ruku' before the follower completes the tasbihat, the follower must follow the imam immediately (obligation of mutaba'a). However, if the imam says salam before the follower completes tashahhud, the follower does not follow immediately because tashahhud is individually wajib. These rulings show the nuanced balance between following the imam and completing one's own obligations.

Key Terms
المتابعة (al-mutaba'a): The follower's action of following the imam promptly.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in the final sitting of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the follower not follow the imam if the imam says salam before the follower completes tashahhud?
A) Because the follower must complete the tasbih first.
B) Because reciting tashahhud is obligatory.
C) Because the follower is allowed to delay the salam.
D) Because the imam's salam may be invalid.

Key Takeaway
The follower must follow the imam in raising the head from ruku' even if tasbih incomplete, but must not follow the imam's salam until tashahhud is completed.

Sunnah Order of Prostration: Knees, Hands, Face
Ruling on the sunnah order of limbs in sujud and its evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah order of placing and lifting limbs during sujud and identify when the order is reversed for a mutakhaffif.

Core Idea
Sunnah order: knees, hands, face; reverse when rising; exception for lightly clothed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the sunnah manner of prostrating in prayer. The Prophet's practice, supported by hadith, establishes a specific order: placing knees first, then hands, then nose, then forehead. When rising, the order is reversed. The ruling is that this order is a confirmed sunnah, not a fard, and a practical exception is made for those wearing light clothing that might expose the body.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling classification
The passage discusses the order of placing and lifting limbs during sujud. Determine whether this order is fard, wajib, or sunnah. The text and evidence indicate it is a sunnah muakkadah.
The fard of sujud is only placing the forehead on the ground; the order is additional.
2
Extract the primary order from the text
From the source: when prostrating, place knees first, then hands, then nose, then forehead. When rising, reverse: forehead, then nose, then hands, then knees.
This is the default sunnah order.
3
Note the hadith evidence
The commentator cites Abu Dawood and al-Tirmidhi that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to do this. This establishes the order as sunnah.
The hadith show the Prophet's constant practice, which in Hanafi usul indicates sunnah.
4
Identify the exception for mutakhaffif
For a person wearing light clothing (mutakhaffif), the order changes: place hands before knees, and the right hand before the left, to avoid exposure.
This exception shows flexibility while maintaining the spirit of the sunnah.
5
Understand the legal distinction
The order is sunnah, not fard. If reversed, the prayer remains valid, but the person misses the reward of following the sunnah. The exception is a recommended adjustment.
This distinction is important: missing a sunnah does not invalidate the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ثم كبر ووضع ركبتيه ثم يديه ثم وجهه بين كفيه بعكس النهوض كما كان يفعله عليه السلام كما رواه أبو داود ولحديث الترمذي : كان عليه السلام إذا سجد وضع وجهه بين كفيه. وأفاد أنه إذا أراد السجود يضع أولاً ما كان أقرب إلى الأرض فيضع ركبتيه أوّلاً ثم يديه ثم أنفه ثم جبهته، وإذا أراد الرفع يرفع أوّلاً جبهته ثم أنفه ثم يديه ثم ركبتيه . وهذا كله عند الإمكان، أما إذا كان متخففاً فإنه يضع اليدين قبل الركبتين ويقدم اليمنى على اليسرى.
His statement: 'Then he says takbir and places his knees, then his hands, then his face between his palms, contrary to the manner of rising' as the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to do, as narrated by Abu Dawood and by the hadith of al-Tirmidhi: 'When the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrated, he placed his face between his palms.' And it indicates that when he intends to prostrate, he first places what is closest to the ground: he places his knees first, then his hands, then his nose, then his forehead; and when he intends to rise, he first raises his forehead, then his nose, then his hands, then his knees. All of this is when possible. As for when he is lightly clothed (mutakhaffif), he places the hands before the knees and gives precedence to the right over the left.
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage explains the sunnah manner of prostrating (sujud) and returning to standing. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that after rising from bowing, the worshiper says takbir and then places his knees, then his hands, then his face between his palms—and when rising, he does the opposite order. The commentator from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq supports this with hadith from Abu Dawood and al-Tirmidhi describing the Prophet's practice. The principle is to place the part of the body that is closest to the ground first: knees, then hands, then nose, then forehead. When rising, the reverse: forehead, nose, hands, knees. This is the recommended (sunnah) order. However, if the person is 'mutakhaffif' (lightly dressed, e.g., wearing a thin garment that might expose the body when bending), then it is recommended to place the hands before the knees to avoid exposure, and to place the right hand before the left. This shows the flexibility of the Hanafi school in considering practical circumstances while preserving the general sunnah.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujud): Prostration, a pillar of prayer; this passage describes the sunnah manner of performing it.
النُهوض (al-nuhud): Rising from prostration; the reverse order is sunnah.
متخفف (mutakhaffif): A person wearing light clothing that may expose the body when bowing or prostrating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the normal case, which limb does a worshiper place on the ground first when going into sajdah?
A) Hands
B) Nose
C) Knees
D) Forehead

Key Takeaway
The sunnah order of sujud is knees then hands then face; when rising, the reverse. For a mutakhaffif, hands come first to avoid exposure.

The Munfarid's Recitation: Tasmi' and Tahmid
Intra-Hanafi dispute on munfarid's tasmi' and tahmid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on what a munfarid recites when rising from ruku' and explain the intra-madhhab dispute's basis and resolution.

Core Idea
The munfarid says only tahmid, not tasmi', per the relied-upon narration.

When you pray alone, should you say both 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and 'Rabbana lakal hamd' when rising from ruku'? Early Hanafi authorities differed, and the preferred position relies on a textual transmission over a stronger evidence. Let's trace why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
From the passage, list the three opinions on what the munfarid says: (1) no tasmi' (first opinion), (2) only tahmid, (3) both tasmi' and tahmid.
The first opinion is 'la yaqul sami'a' – he does not say tasmi' at all.
2
Understand the reasoning for each position
For position (2): tasmi' is to exhort followers to praise; the munfarid has none. For (3): the Prophet combined them in isolation, reconciling hadiths.
Position (2) is argued by al-Halwani and al-Tahawi; (3) by author of al-Hidayah.
3
Recognize the tarjih (preference) mechanism
Though evidence (dalil) supports combining, the madhhab favours the matn’s view (only tahmid) because it is Zahir al-Riwayah – the apparent/transmitted position from the early masters.
Mufta bihi: only tahmid. This is a classic example of authority_weight overriding dalil strength.
4
Apply the ruling
When you pray alone, recite only 'Rabbana lakal hamd' (or its preferred variant) upon standing upright. Do not say 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'.
The same applies if you are a follower; the imam says tasmi' and tahmid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يقول سمع الثاني أنه يأتي بالتحميد لا غير وصححه المصنف في الكافي. وقال في المبسوط : وهو الأصح وعليه أكثر المشايخ. واختاره الحلواني والطحاوي لأن التسميع حث لمن خلفه على التحميد وليس معه أحد ليحثه عليه فلا يأتي بالتسميع . الثالث الجمع بينهما وصححه صاحب الهداية. وقال الصدر الشهيد وعليه الاعتماد واختاره صاحب المجمع لأن قد . من صبح فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه كان يجمع بينهما ولا محمل له سوى حالة الانفراد توفيقاً بينه وبين القول الثابت في الصحيحين في حق الإمام والمأموم. وقيده في غاية البيان بانفراده بصلاة النفل لأنه كان مواظباً على الجماعة في الفرض، وحيث اختلف التصحيح كما رأيت با من الترجيح، فالمرجح من جهة المذهب ما في المتن لأنه ظاهر الرواية كما صرح به قاذ ميخان في شرحه والرجح من جهة الدليل ما صححه في الهداية. وفي القنية : أما المنفرد الله لمن حمده فإذا استوى قائماً قال ربنا لك الحمد في الجواب الظاهر وهو الصحية. اهـ. وفي جامع التمرتاشي : فإن لم يأت بالتسميع حالة الرفع لم يأت به حالة الاستواء، وقد قيل يأتي بهما. والمراد بالتسميع سمع الله لمن حمده ومعناه قبل الله حمد من حمده، وقيل أجاب، وقيل غفر له والهاء في حمده للكناية. كذا في المستصفى. وذكر في الفوائد الحميدية أنها للسكتة والاستراحة. والمراد بالتحميد واحد من أربعة ألفاظ أفضلها اللهم ربنا ولك الحمد كما في المجتبى، ويليه اللهم ربنا لك الحمد، ويليه ربنا ولك الحمد، ويليه المعروف ربنا لك الحمد . فما في المحيط من أفضلية الثاني فمحمول على أفضليته على ما بعده لا على الكل كما لا يخفى لما صرحوا به من أن زيادة الواو توجب الأفضلية واختلفوا فيها، فقيل زائدة، وقيل عاطفة تقديره ربنا حمدناك ولك الحمد واعلم أن المفهوم من المتن أنه لا يكبر حال الارتفاع وهو الموافق لما ذكر في خزانة الفقه أن تكبيرات فرائض اليوم والليلة أربع وتسعون، وإنما يستقيم هذا إذا لم يكن عند الرفع تكبير لكن ذكر في المحيط وروضة الناطفي أنه يكبر حالة الارتفاع لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام وأبا بكر وعمر وعلياً كانوا يكبرون عند كل خفض ورفع كما رواه الطحاوي ويمكن أن يجاب عن الحديث بأن المراد بالتكبير الذكر الذي فه تعظيم الله تعالى توفيقاً. كذا في المجتبى.
He does not say 'Sami'a'. The second [opinion] is that he says only the tahmid, and the author in al-Kafi corrected it. And he said in al-Mabsut: it is the most correct and most of the mashayikh are upon it. And al-Halwani and al-Tahawi chose it because tasmi' is an exhortation for those behind him to praise, and there is no one with him to exhort, so he does not say tasmi'. The third is to combine both, and the author of al-Hidayah corrected it. And al-Sadr al-Shahid said: upon it is the reliance and the author of al-Majma' chose it because [the hadith that he used to combine both] and it has no interpretation other than the case of being alone, to reconcile between it and the established statement in the two Sahihs regarding the imam and the follower. And he restricted it in Ghayat al-Bayan to his being alone in supererogatory prayer because he was steadfast on congregation in obligatory prayer. And since the correction differs as you see with weighting, the preferable from the madhhab's perspective is what is in the matn because it is the apparent transmission as stated by Qadikhan in his commentary, and the preferable from the perspective of evidence is what is corrected in al-Hidayah. And in al-Qunya: As for he who is alone, [he says] 'Allah [accepts] the praise of one who praises Him' then when he stands upright he says 'Our Lord, to You belongs all praise' in the apparent response and it is health. End. And in Jami' al-Timurtashi: If he does not say the tasmi' at the time of raising, he does not say it at the state of standing; and it was said he says both. And the meaning of tasmi' is 'Allah hears whoever praises Him' and its meaning is Allah accepted the praise of one who praised Him, and it was said answered, and it was said forgave him, and the 'ha' in 'hamdihi' is a pronoun. Similarly in al-Mustasfa. And it was mentioned in al-Fawa'id al-Hamidiyyah that it is for silent pause and rest. And the meaning of tahmid is one of four phrases, the most excellent of which is 'Allahumma Rabbana wa laka al-hamd' as in al-Mujtaba, followed by 'Allahumma Rabbana laka al-hamd', followed by 'Rabbana wa laka al-hamd', followed by the known 'Rabbana laka al-hamd'. So what is in al-Muhit of the excellence of the second is understood as its excellence over what comes after it, not over all, as is not hidden because they stated that the addition of 'waw' causes excellence, and they differed about it: some said it is redundant, some said it is conjunctive with the meaning 'Rabbana hamidnaka wa laka al-hamd'. And know that what is understood from the matn is that he does not say takbir at the time of rising, and that is in agreement with what is mentioned in Khizanat al-Fiqh that the takbirs of the obligatory prayers of the day and night are ninety-four, and this is correct only if there is no takbir at the time of rising. But it is mentioned in al-Muhit and Rawdat al-Natifi that he says takbir at the time of rising due to the narration that the Prophet, Abu Bakr, Umar, and Ali used to say takbir at every lowering and raising as narrated by al-Tahawi, and it is possible to respond to the hadith that what is meant by takbir is the dhikr that contains exaltation of Allah Most High by way of reconciliation. Similarly in al-Mujtaba.
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding what a person praying alone (munfarid) should recite during the rising from ruku'. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The text presents three positions: (1) that the munfarid says neither tasmi' nor tahmid? Actually, the default 'la yaqul sami'a' means the munfarid does not say 'Sami'a Allah', which is the first position; (2) that he only says the tahmid (praise); (3) that he combines both tasmi' and tahmid. The second position (only tahmid) is considered Zahir al-Riwayah and thus the relied-upon view in the madhhab, although the evidence (hadith) supports the combination. The author cites various authorities: al-Halwani and al-Tahawi support only tahmid because tasmi' is meant to prompt followers to praise, and the munfarid has no followers. The third position is favored by the author of al-Hidayah, who argues from the Prophet's practice. Ultimately, the matn's position (only tahmid) takes precedence for fatwa, as it is from Zahir al-Riwayah. The passage also elaborates on the meanings of tasmi' and tahmid, and discusses the virtue of different phrasings of the tahmid.

Key Terms
التسميع (al-tasmi'): The phrase 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' said when rising from ruku'; meaning 'Allah hears whoever praises Him'.
التحميد (al-tahmid): The phrase 'Rabbana lakal hamd' or variations; praise to Allah after rising from ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what should a person praying alone (munfarid) say when rising from ruku'?
A) Only 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'
B) Only 'Rabbana lakal hamd'
C) Both 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and 'Rabbana lakal hamd'
D) He should remain silent

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi for the munfarid is to recite only the tahmid upon rising from ruku', omitting the tasmi'.

Sujud: The Dispute over Forehead vs. Nose
Ruling on sujud body parts and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on sujud with only the nose and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Sujud requires the forehead; the nose alone is invalid, per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Prostration is a pillar of prayer, but which parts of the face must touch the ground? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: Abu Hanifa initially allowed sujud with only the nose, but the Sahibayn required the forehead. Later authorities confirm Abu Hanifa's retraction, making the Sahibayn's view the mufta bihi. This lesson analyzes the evidence and the resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
Determine what exactly is in dispute: is sujud valid if only the nose touches the ground (without the forehead)?
The dispute is within the Hanafi school, not between madhahib.
2
State the initial view of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa initially held that sujud with only the nose is valid unconditionally. Identify his evidence: the linguistic and shar'i definition of sujud, and the hadith of seven bones.
His view is based on the hadith mentioning the nose as one of the bones.
3
State the view of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani held that sujud is not valid with only the nose unless there is an excuse on the forehead. Their evidence: the forehead is the default part of the face for sujud, and the hadith is zanni.
This view became the mufta bihi after Abu Hanifa's retraction.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to the hadith
The hadith 'I was commanded to prostrate on seven bones' is zanni in transmission and indication; it does not explicitly prove that the nose alone suffices. The mention of the nose may be an interpretation of the forehead pointing.
The response is based on usul al-fiqh principles: zanni dalil cannot override qat'i definition of sujud.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is the Sahibayn's view. If someone prays with only their nose (no forehead) without an excuse, their sujud is invalid, and the prayer must be repeated.
This is the fatwa, as confirmed by later authorities like al-Hidayah and al-Burhan.

قوله (ثم كبر ووضع ركبتيه ثم يديه ثم وجهه بين كفيه بعكس النهوض كما كان يفعله عليه السلام كما رواه أبو داود ولحديث الترمذي : كان عليه السلام إذا سجد وضع وجهه بين كفيه. وأفاد أنه إذا أراد السجود يضع أولاً ما كان أقرب إلى الأرض فيضع ركبتيه أوّلاً ثم يديه ثم أنفه ثم جبهته، وإذا أراد الرفع يرفع أوّلاً جبهته ثم أنفه ثم يديه ثم ركبتيه . وهذا كله عند الإمكان، أما إذا كان متخففاً فإنه يضع اليدين قبل الركبتين ويقدم اليمنى على اليسرى.
وسجد بأنفه وجبهته) أي سجد عليهما التحصيل الأكمل. والأنف اسم لما صلب وأما مالان منه فلا يجوز الاقتصار عليه باجماعهم كما نقله غير واحد والجبهة اسم لما يصيب الأرض مما فوق الحاجبين إلى قصاص الشعر حالة السجود، وعرفها بعضهم بأنها ما إكتنفه الجبينان. واعلم أن المأمور به في كتاب الله تعالى إنما هو السجود وهو في اللغة يطلق لطأطأه الرأس والانحناء وللخضوع وللتواضع وللميل كسجدت النخلة مالت، وللتحية كالسجود لآدم تكرمة له. كذا في ضياء الحلوم. وفي الشريعة وضع بعض الوجه مما لا سخرية فيه فخرج الخد والذقن والصدغ ومقدم الرأس فلا يجوز السجود عليها، وإن كان من عذر بل معه يجب الإيماء بالرأس. ولعله إنما قال تعالى يخرون للاذقان سجداً أن الذقن ليس محل السجود لأن الساجد أول ما يلقى به الأرض من وجهه الذقن وهو مجتمع اللحيين. ووضع بعض الوجه يتحقق بالأنف كما في الجبهة فيجوز بالجبهة وحدها اتفاقاً على ما عليه الجم الغفير من أهل المذهب. وما في المفيد والمزيد من أنه لا يتأدى الفرض عندهما إلا بوضعهما فخلاف المشهور عنهما، وإنما محل الاختلاف في الاقتصار على الأنف فعنده يجوز مطلقاً، وعندهما لا يجوز إلا من عذر بالجبهة كما صرح به صاحب الهداية، والوجه ظاهر للإمام رحمه الله لأن المأمور به السجود وهو ما قلنا. وأما ما في الصحيحين مرفوعاً «أمرت أن أسجد على سبعة أعظم على الجبهة وأشار بيده إلى أنفه واليدين والركبتين وأطراف القدمين ولا يكف الثياب والشعر (۱) فلا يفيد الافتراض لأن ظني الثبوت قطعاً وظني الدلالة على قوله : (فخرج الخد والذقن الخ) تقدم ما فيه عند ذكر الفرائض . قوله : (فعنده يجوز مطلقاً الخ) قال في الشرنبلالية : هذا قول أبي حنيفة أوّلاً والأصح رجوعه إلى قولهما بعدم جواز الاقتصار في السجود على الأنف بلا عذر في الجبهة كما في البرهان اهـ وفي شرح الشيخ اسمعيل : ثم في الهداية أن قولهما رواية عن أبي حنيفة وفي المجمع وروي عنه قولهما وعليه الفتوى. وفي الحقائق : وروى عنه مثل قولهما قال في العيون وعليه الفتوى وفي دور البحار والفتوى رجوعه إلى قولهما لأنه المتعارف والمتبادر إلى الفهم .اهـ. وفي شرح الملتقى للحصكفي : وعليه الفتوى كما في قال المجمع وشروحه والوقاية وشروحها والجوهرة وصدر الشريعة والعيون قوله : (وأشار بيده إلى أنفه) في فتح القدير : رواية وأشار بيده إلى أنفه غير ضائرة فإن العبرة للفظ الصريح والإشارة إلى الجبهة تقع بتقريب اليد إلى جهة الأنف للتقارب قوله : (لم يوافقه دراية الخ) أما الأول فمسلم، وأما الثاني فلا لما علمت مما مر على أنه قد يمنع الأوّل بناء على ما قدمناه في الفصل السابق بأن يراد
His statement (then he says takbir and places his knees, then his hands, then his face between his palms, opposite of rising) as he (peace be upon him) used to do, as narrated by Abu Dawud and by the hadith of Tirmidhi: He (peace be upon him) when prostrating placed his face between his palms. And it indicates that when he intends to prostrate, he places first what is closest to the ground: he places his knees first, then his hands, then his nose, then his forehead, and when he intends to rise, he raises his forehead first, then his nose, then his hands, then his knees. All this when possible; but if he is lightened, he places his hands before his knees and prefers the right over the left. (And he prostrates with his nose and forehead) i.e., he prostrates with both for the most complete fulfillment. The nose is a name for the hard part; as for its soft part, it is not permissible to suffice with it by consensus as transmitted by more than one. The forehead is a name for what touches the ground from above the eyebrows to the hairline in prostration; some defined it as what is flanked by the temples. Know that what is commanded in the Book of Allah is prostration, and it is in language used for lowering the head and bowing, for humility, for submissiveness, for inclination (like a date palm tilts), and for greeting (like prostration to Adam as honor). Similarly in Diya' al-Huloom. In the Shari'ah, it is placing part of the face that is not disdainful; thus the cheek, chin, temple, and front of the head are excluded, so prostration on them is not permissible, and even if there is an excuse, one must gesture with the head. Perhaps Allah said 'They fall down on their chins prostrating' because the chin is not a place of prostration, since the prostrater first meets the ground with his chin, which is the meeting of the jawbones. Placing part of the face is realized by the nose as with the forehead; so prostration with the forehead alone is permissible by agreement of the vast majority of the school. And what is in al-Mufid and al-Mazid that the obligation is not fulfilled with them (the Sahibayn) except by placing both is contrary to the famous from them. The only point of disagreement is in restricting to the nose: with him (Abu Hanifa) it is permissible absolutely, and with them (the Sahibayn) it is not permissible except with an excuse on the forehead, as stated by the author of al-Hidayah. And the reasoning is apparent for the Imam (may Allah have mercy on him) because what is commanded is prostration, which is what we said. As for the hadith in the Sahihayn raised: 'I was commanded to prostrate on seven bones: on the forehead and he pointed with his hand to his nose, and the hands, knees, and toes, and not to fold up garments and hair' – it does not indicate obligatoriness because [the hadith] is zanni in transmission and zanni in indication on... (text cut off).
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on prostration (sujud) in the commentary of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It first describes the recommended order of placing body parts when prostrating: knees, hands, nose, forehead; and the opposite when rising. Then it focuses on the essential parts of sujud: the nose and forehead. The text defines 'nose' as the hard part, and 'forehead' as the area from eyebrows to hairline. It emphasizes that the obligation in the Quran is 'sujud', which is placing part of the face that is not disdainful (i.e., not the cheek, chin, temple, or front of head). There is consensus that sujud with the forehead alone is valid. The dispute is about sujud with the nose only: Abu Hanifa initially allowed it unconditionally, but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) required the forehead unless there is an excuse. The text then discusses the hadith of the seven bones, arguing that it does not prove obligatoriness due to zanni evidence. Later, it reports that Abu Hanifa's final position (as per many authorities) retracted to the view of the Sahibayn, and that is the fatwa. The mufta bihi is that sujud must include the forehead; the nose alone is insufficient without a forehead excuse.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujud): Placing part of the face that is not disdainful on the ground as an act of worship; in prayer, it is a pillar.
الأنف (al-anf): The nose; specifically the hard part (the bone). The soft part is not sufficient.
الجبهة (al-jabhah): The forehead; the area above the eyebrows to the hairline, between the temples.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, if a person prostrates with only their nose touching the ground (without the forehead) due to no excuse, what is the ruling?
A) The sujud is valid
B) The sujud is invalid and the prayer is nullified
C) The sujud is valid but makruh
D) The sujud is valid if the nose is the hard part

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that sujud requires the forehead; the nose alone is invalid without an excuse.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Prostration on Nose and Forehead: The Hanafi Dispute
Explains the ruling on prostration on nose and forehead and the intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on prostration on the nose and forehead and state the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
Prostration on both forehead and nose is wajib; omitting either without excuse is sinful, but the prayer remains valid.

Prostration (sujud) is a pillar of prayer, but how much of the face must touch the ground? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute about the nose. Imam Abu Hanifa initially ruled that prostrating on the nose alone is permissible, but the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) required both the forehead and nose unless there is an excuse. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the retraction of Abu Hanifa, and the practical ruling that shapes Hanafi prayer today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed element
The act is sujud (prostration) during prayer. The disputed element is whether placing the nose on the ground is obligatory or merely recommended.
Both sides agree that the forehead is obligatory by consensus.
2
State the initial view of Imam Abu Hanifa
He held that it is permissible to limit prostration to the nose alone without any excuse, as sujud linguistically means placing part of the face.
This was his original ijtihad.
3
State the view of the two disciples (Sahibayn)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held that prostration on the nose alone is not permissible except when there is an excuse (such as a wound) on the forehead. They argued that the constant practice (muwazabah) of the Prophet was to place both.
Their position is based on the hadith and the gesture to the nose.
4
Trace the tarjih
Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to have retracted his initial view and agreed with the disciples. Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Haskafi, Ibn al-Humam) confirmed that the fatwa is upon the disciples' view.
The retraction is recorded in multiple sources like al-Burhan and al-Hidayah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if someone prostrates only on the nose without excuse, the prayer is valid but sinful according to the mufta bihi. According to Abu Hanifa's initial view, it would be valid and not sinful.
Some later Hanafis (e.g., author of al-Ikhtiyar) even permit it without dislike, but the relied-upon position is the stricter view.
