كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة
خلاف فيه بناء على أن لفظ (أمرت) مستعمل في الوجوب والندب الذي هو الأعم بمعنى ذلك أو في الندب أو في الوجوب . فقولهما بالافتراض مشكل لأنه يلزمهما الزيادة على الكتاب بخبر الواحد وهما يمنعانه في الأصول كأبي حنيفة، فلذا قال المحقق ابن الهمام: فجعل بعض المتأخرين الفتوى على الرواية الأخرى الموافقة لقولهما لم يوافقه دراية ولا القوي من الرواية. هذا ولو حمل قولهما لا يجوز الاقتصار إلا من عذر على وجوب الجمع كان أحسن إذ يرتفع الخلاف بناء على ما حملنا الكراهة منه عليه من كراهة التحريم ولم يخرجا عن الأصول اهـ. فالحاصل أنه لا خلاف بينهم، فقول الإمام بكراهة الاقتصار على الأنف المراد بها كراهة التحريم وهي في مقابلة ترك الواجب وقولهما بعدم الجواز المراد به عدم الحل وهو كراهة التحريم فالسجود على الجبهة واجب اتفاقاً لأن مقتضى الحديث والمواظبة المروية في سنن الترمذي كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا سجد مكن جبهته وأنفه بالأرض وقال حديث حسن صحيح. وهكذا في صحيح البخاري لكن هذا يقتضي وجوب السجود على الأنف كالجبهة لأن المواضبة المنقولة تعمهما مع أن المنقول في البدائع والتحفة والاختيار عدم الكراهة بترك السجود على الأنف، وظاهر ما في الكتاب يخالفة فإنه قال : وكره أي الاقتصار على أحدهما، سواء كان الجبهة أو الأنف. وهي عند الإطلاق منصرفة إلى كراهة التحريم، وهكذا في المفيد والمزيد. فالقول بعدم الكراهة .ضعيف وخرج أيضاً بقولنا «مما لا سخرية فيه» ما إذا رفع قدميه في السجود فإنه لا يصح لأن السجود مع رفعهما بالتلاعب أشبه منه
بالسجود في الآية السجود الشرعي فيكون مجملاً بينته السنة ومجمل الكتاب إذا بينته السنة يكون المبين ثابتاً بالكتاب، ويؤيده أن السجود اللغوي أيضاً مجمل لتعدد معانيه كما مر فتدبر . قوله : (هذا ولو حمل قولهما لا يجوز الخ) قال الشيخ اسمعيل : فيه نظر لأن كتب المذهب مشحونة بنصب الخلاف في هذه المسألة بينه وبينهما وهو يبعد الحمل على الاتفاق بما ذكر بمراحل كما يظهر للمتتبع، كيف ولفظ المبسوط وإن سجد على الأنف دون الجبهة جاز عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله ويكره، ولم يجز عن أبي يوسف ومحمد رحمه الله وهو رواية ابن عمرو عن أبي حنيفة .اهـ. قوله فالقول بعدم الكراهة ضعيف) أي عدم كراهة ترك السجود على الأنف. قال في النهر : لو حملت الكراهة في رأي من أثبتها على التنزيه ومن نفاها على التحريمية لارتفع التنافي وعبارته في السراج «المستحب أن يضعهما اهـ . لكن قال الشيخ اسمعيل : وفي غرر الأذكار أن الاقتصار على الجبهة يجوز بلا كراهة وإن لم يكن على الأنف عذر اتفاقاً، وكذلك في مجموع المسائل وأنه به يفتي وفي الاختيار : وإن اقتصر على جبهته جاز بالإجماع ولا إساءة بعد أن قال : فإن اقتصر على الأنف جاز وقد أساء. وقالا : لا يجوز إلا من عذر اهـ كلامه فليتأمل ويبعد ما قاله في النهر قول المتن وكره على أحدهما فإنه لا حمله على التنزيهية نظراً إلى ترك السجود على الجبهة لكن سيأتي حمل الكراهة على طلب الكف وضع
يصح
طلباً غير جازم. قوله : ( يخرج أيضاً بقولنا مما لا سخرية فيه ما إذا رفع قدميه الخ) مقتضاه أن
He prostrated with his nose and forehead, and it is disliked to do so with one of them or with the fold of his turban, and he exposed his armpits and kept his belly away from... His statement: 'And he prostrated with his nose and forehead' means he prostrated on both for the most complete fulfillment. The nose is the name for what is hard; as for what is soft from it, it is not permissible to limit oneself to it by consensus as reported by more than one. The forehead is the name for what touches the ground from above the eyebrows to the hairline in the state of prostration. Some defined it as what is flanked by the two temples. Know that what is commanded in the Book of Allah is prostration, and in language it is used for lowering the head and bending, for humility, for submission, for inclination like the date palm bent, and for greeting like prostrating to Adam as an honor. Thus in Diya' al-Hulum. In sacred law it is placing part of the face without mockery, so the cheek, chin, temple, and front of the head are excluded, so prostration on them is not permissible, though if there is an excuse, one must gesture with the head. Perhaps the Most High said 'they fall down on their chins prostrating' because the chin is not a place of prostration, for the prostrator first touches the ground with his face at the chin, which is the meeting of the two jaws. Placing part of the face is realized by the nose as by the forehead, so it is permissible with the forehead alone by agreement according to the great multitude of the school. What is in al-Mufid and al-Mazid that the obligation is not fulfilled for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) except by placing both is contrary to their famous position. The place of difference is only in limiting to the nose: according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is permissible absolutely, while according to them it is not permissible except with an excuse on the forehead, as stated by the author of al-Hidayah. The proof is clear for the Imam (may Allah have mercy on him) because what is commanded is prostration, which is what we said. As for what is in the two Sahihs as marfu': 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: on the forehead – and he pointed with his hand to his nose – and the two hands, the two knees, and the tips of the feet, and not to tuck up the garments or hair' – this does not indicate obligation because it is zanni in transmission and zanni in meaning... His statement: 'So according to him it is permissible absolutely' – said in al-Sharnablaliyya: This was Abu Hanifa's saying initially, and the correct view is that he retracted to their saying of non-permissibility of limiting in prostration to the nose without an excuse on the forehead, as in al-Burhan. In Sharh al-Shaykh Isma'il: Then in al-Hidayah, their saying is a narration from Abu Hanifa, and in al-Majma' it is narrated from him like their saying, and the fatwa is upon it. In al-Haqa'iq: It was narrated from him like their saying. He said in al-Uyun: And upon it is the fatwa, and in Dur al-Bihar: The fatwa is his retraction to their saying because it is customary and immediately understood. In Sharh al-Multaqa lil-Haskafi: And upon it is the fatwa, as in al-Majma' and its commentaries, al-Wiqaya and its commentaries, al-Jawhara, Sadr al-Shari'a, and al-Uyun. His statement: 'And he pointed with his hand to his nose' – in Fath al-Qadir: The narration 'and he pointed with his hand to his nose' is not harmful, for the criterion is the explicit wording, and the pointing to the forehead occurs by bringing the hand near the direction of the nose due to proximity. His statement: 'It did not agree with knowledge...' – As for the first, it is admitted, but as for the second, no, because of what you have learned from what has passed, though it may be that the first is prevented based on what we presented in the previous chapter: that by 'I have been commanded' is meant... (Footnote: Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Ahmad) ... Disagreement exists based on that the word 'I have been commanded' is used for obligation and recommendation, which is the more general meaning, or for recommendation, or for obligation. Their statement of obligation is problematic because it would require adding to the Book by a solitary hadith, while they prevent that in principles like Abu Hanifa. Therefore, the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam said: Some later scholars made the fatwa on the other narration agreeing with them, but it did not agree with knowledge nor the strong of narration. This, if their saying 'it is not permissible except with an excuse' were interpreted as requiring the combination, it would be better, for the disagreement would be removed based on our interpreting the dislikedness from him as karahah tahrimi, and they would not have left the principles. So the conclusion is that there is no disagreement between them, for the Imam's saying of dislike for limiting to the nose means karahah tahrimi, which is equivalent to leaving an obligation, and their saying of non-permissibility means not permissible, which is karahah tahrimi. Thus, prostration on the forehead is obligatory by agreement, because the implication of the hadith and the constant practice reported in Sunan al-Tirmidhi that the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he prostrated placed his forehead and nose on the ground, and he said it is a hasan sahih hadith. Similarly in Sahih al-Bukhari, but this would entail obligation of prostration on the nose like the forehead, because the transmitted constancy includes both, though what is transmitted in al-Bada'i', al-Tuhfa, and al-Ikhtiyar is that there is no dislike in leaving prostration on the nose. What is apparent in the book contradicts it, for it said: 'And it is disliked' i.e., limiting to one of them, whether the forehead or the nose. And when used absolutely, it refers to karahah tahrimi, and similarly in al-Mufid and al-Mazid. So the saying of no dislike is weak. Also by our saying 'without mockery' is excluded the case of raising his feet in prostration, for it is not valid because prostration with raising them is more like playing than prostration... in the verse. The prostration in the verse is legal prostration, so it is mujmal, and the Sunnah clarifies it, and a mujmal of the Book when clarified by the Sunnah becomes established by the Book. This is supported by the fact that linguistic prostration is also mujmal due to its multiple meanings, so reflect. His statement: 'This, if their saying 'it is not permissible' is interpreted...' – Shaykh Isma'il said: There is consideration in this, for the books of the school are filled with establishing disagreement in this issue between him and them, and it is far from agreement by what was mentioned as stages, as appears to one who follows. How so, and the wording of al-Mabsut: 'If he prostrates on the nose without the forehead, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but disliked, and it is not permissible according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and it is a narration from Ibn Amr from Abu Hanifa.' His statement: 'So the saying of no dislike is weak' i.e., no dislike for leaving prostration on the nose. He said in al-Nahr: If the dislike in the view of those who affirm it is interpreted as tanzihi, and those who deny it as tahrimi, the contradiction would be removed. His expression in al-Siraj: 'It is mustahabb to place them both.' But Shaykh Isma'il said: In Ghurar al-Adhkar, limiting to the forehead is permissible without dislike even if there is no excuse on the nose, by agreement, and similarly in Majmu' al-Masa'il, and that it is what one gives fatwa on. And in al-Ikhtiyar: 'If he limits to his forehead, it is permissible by consensus and there is no offense' after saying: 'If he limits to his nose, it is permissible and he has done wrong. And they said: It is not permissible except with an excuse.' So his speech is to be considered, and what he said in al-Nahr is far from the text's saying 'And it is disliked on one of them', for it cannot be interpreted as tanzihi considering leaving prostration on the forehead, but later the interpretation of dislike as requesting to refrain without insistence. His statement: 'Also by our saying 'without mockery' is excluded the case of raising his feet...' its implication is that
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling of prostration during prayer, specifically whether one must prostrate on both the forehead and the nose, or whether it is sufficient to prostrate on only one. The author, al-Marghinani, begins by defining the key terms: the nose refers to its hard part, and the forehead is the area above the eyebrows to the hairline. Prostration in sacred law is placing part of the face on the ground without mockery. There is a consensus that prostration is valid with the forehead alone. However, the dispute arises regarding the nose: Imam Abu Hanifa initially held that it is permissible to limit prostration to the nose without any excuse, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) maintained that it is not permissible except when there is an excuse (such as a wound) on the forehead. The text then discusses the evidence: the hadith 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones...' is used by the disciples to argue obligation, but the author points out that the hadith is zanni in transmission (ahad) and zanni in meaning (it can indicate recommendation). He also notes that Abu Hanifa later retracted his position and is reported to have agreed with the disciples. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that prostrating on the forehead is obligatory, and prostrating on the nose is also obligatory in the sense that omission without excuse is sinful. However, some later scholars, such as those cited in al-Ikhtiyar, state that limiting to the forehead is permissible without dislike. The text reconciles the positions by interpreting Abu Hanifa's 'dislike' as karahah tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), which is equivalent to his students' 'not permissible' – meaning it is a sin to omit the nose without reason. Thus, the practical ruling is that one should prostrate on both forehead and nose; if one prostrates only on the forehead, the prayer is valid but it is disliked (tahriman) unless there is an excuse. The passage also discusses the point that raising both feet off the ground during prostration invalidates the prayer, as it resembles playing. The overall conclusion is that there is no real conflict once the terminology is understood.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujud): In sacred law, placing part of the face on the ground without mockery, specifically the forehead and nose.
الجبهة (al-jabhah): The area between the eyebrows (top of forehead) to the hairline, excluding the temples.
الأنف (al-anf): The hard, bony part of the nose (the bridge), not the soft part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the ruling if a person prostrates only on the nose without any excuse on the forehead?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but the person has committed a sin (karahah tahrimi).
C) The prayer is valid and there is no sin because the nose suffices.
D) The prayer is invalid only if the person intended to omit the forehead.

Key Takeaway
Prostration on both forehead and nose is wajib in the Hanafi school; omitting the nose without an excuse is sinful, but the prayer remains valid.

Obligatory Limbs in Sujud: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on obligatory limbs in sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on placing feet, hands, and knees in sujud, identify the mufta bihi view, and explain the evidence and practical consequences of the ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Placing feet in sujud is wajib (not fard), while hands and knees are neither fard nor wajib in the Hanafi school.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq reveals a rich intra-Hanafi debate on what must be placed on the ground during sujud. While the nose and forehead are undisputed, the feet, hands, and knees have been subject to varying views among Hanafi jurists. We will trace the arguments, identify the preferred position, and understand why the ruling matters in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Limbs
List the body parts discussed: feet (toes), hands, and knees. Note the range of rulings attributed to each.
The passage mainly focuses on feet, but also addresses hands and knees briefly.
2
Map the Hanafi Positions
For feet, note the spectrum: fard (Quduri, weak), wajib (Fath al-Qadir), sunna (Shaykh al-Islam, al-Hidayah). For hands and knees: fard (Abu al-Layth, weak), not fard (fatwa view).
The text calls Quduri's fard position 'weak' and Abu al-Layth's view unsupported.
3
Analyze the Evidence
Identify the decisive (qat'i) evidence: it only requires part of the face on the ground. Speculative (zanni) evidence and constant practice (muwazabah) support wujub for feet, but not for hands/knees.
The key distinction: fard requires qat'i dalil; wajib can be established by zanni + practice.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
If one omits placing feet: if fard, prayer invalid; if wajib, prayer valid but sinful (requires compensation such as sajdah al-sahw?); if sunna, valid with no sin.
The mufta bihi is wajib, so omission without excuse incurs karahah tahrimiyyah.
5
Apply the Mufta Bihi
Conclude that placing the toes on the ground is wajib; leaving it intentionally without excuse is makruh tahrimi. Hands and knees are not fard; they are sunna or merely recommended.
This matches the fatwa position cited from al-Tanjis and al-Khulasa.

Source Text

بالتعظيم والإجلال ويكفيه وضع أصبع واحدة فلو لم يضع الأصابع أصلاً ووضع ظهر القدم فإنه لا يجوز لأن وضع القدم بوضع الأصبع. وإذا وضع قدماً ورفع آخر جاز مع الكراهة من غير عذر كما أفاده قاضيخان وذهب شيخ الإسلام إلى أن وضعهما سنة فتكون الكراهة تنزيهية والأوجه على منوال ما سبق هو الوجوب فتكون الكراهة تحريمية لما سبق من الحديث. وذكر القدوري أن وضعهما فرض وهو ضعيف. وأما اليدان والركبتان فظاهر الرواية عدم افتراض وضعهما . قال في التنجيس والخلاصة وعليه فتوى مشايخنا. وفي منية المصلي : ليس بواجب عندنا واختار الفقيه أبو الليث الافتراض وصححه في العيون ولا دليل عليه لأن القطعي إنما أفاد وضع بعض الوجه على الأرض دون اليدين والركبتين، والظني المتقدم لا يفيده لكن مقتضاه ومقتضى المواظبة الوجوب، وقد اختاره المحقق في فتح القدير وهو إن شاء الله تعالى أعدل الأقوال لموافقته الأصول وإن صرح كثير من مشايخنا بالسنية ومنهم صاحب الهداية. وفي المجتبى : سجد على طرف من أطراف جبهته يجوز اهـ . وظاهر ما في التنجيس يخالفه فإنه قال : إذا وضع من الجبهة مقدار الأنف لا يجوز عند أبي حنيفة لأن الأنف عضو كامل، وهذا المقدار من الجبهة ليس بعضو كامل ولا بأكثر منها اهـ . إلا أن يحمل الطرف على الأكثر كما لا يخفى.
With reverence and exaltation, and placing one finger suffices. If he did not place the fingers at all and placed the back of the foot, it is not permissible because the placing of the foot is by placing the finger. If he placed one foot and raised the other, it is permissible with dislike without an excuse, as Qadi Khan stated. And Shaykh al-Islam held that placing both feet is sunna, so the dislike is tanzih. But the more correct view according to what preceded is obligation, so the dislike is tahrimi due to the hadith mentioned earlier. Al-Quduri mentioned that placing them is fard, which is weak. As for the hands and knees, the apparent narration is that their placement is not fard. It is stated in al-Tanjis and al-Khulasa: and upon this is the fatwa of our scholars. In Munyat al-Musalli: it is not obligatory according to us. Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi chose fard and verified it in al-Uyun, but there is no evidence for it because the decisive (qat'i) only indicates placing part of the face on the ground, not the hands and knees. The speculative (zanni) mentioned earlier does not indicate it, but its requirement and the requirement of constancy indicate obligation. The muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir chose this, and it is, Allah willing, the most balanced opinion because it agrees with principles, even though many of our scholars explicitly stated it is sunna, among them the author of al-Hidaya. In al-Mujtaba: he prostrated on a side of his forehead – it is permissible. The apparent meaning of what is in al-Tanjis contradicts this, for it says: if he places from the forehead the amount of the nose, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa because the nose is a complete limb, and this amount of forehead is not a complete limb nor more than it. Unless one interprets 'side' to mean the majority.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of placing the feet, hands, and knees during sujud. The text begins by stating that placing even one finger suffices for the feet. If the back of the foot is placed instead of the toes, it is invalid because the intended placement is the toes. Placing one foot and raising the other is permissible but disliked (makruh) without an excuse. Qadi Khan holds the dislike as tanzih (avoiding the better) while others, citing a hadith, deem it tahrimi (closer to haram). Al-Quduri's view that placing both feet is fard is deemed weak. For hands and knees, the relied-upon view is that they are not fard; this is the position of the fatwa according to al-Tanjis and al-Khulasa. However, Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi considered them fard, but the commentator notes lack of clear evidence. The more balanced opinion, per Fath al-Qadir, is that placing the feet is obligatory (wajib) due to constant practice, not fard. Many Hanafi scholars, including the author of al-Hidayah, consider it sunna. The text also discusses a transmission from al-Mujtaba allowing prostration on a side of the forehead, which seems to contradict al-Tanjis that requires more than the nose's area. The commentator reconciles by interpreting 'side' as the majority.

Key Terms
وضع القدمين (wad' al-qadamayn): Placing the feet during sujud, specifically the toes facing the qibla.
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): A prohibition-like dislike, close to haram, requiring avoidance.
القطع (al-qat'): Decisive evidence that is certain in transmission and meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is al-Quduri's view that placing the feet is fard considered weak?
A) Because it contradicts the Quran
B) Because it is based on a weak hadith (mursal)
C) Because it lacks decisive evidence (qat'i)
D) Because the Sahibayn disagreed with it

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of placing feet in sujud is wajib (proven by zanni evidence and constant practice), while hands and knees are not fard, based on the absence of decisive proof.

Sujud on the Turban Coil (al-Koor)
Ruling on sujud on turban coil with proof from hadith and condition about forehead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sujud on the turban coil and explain the condition regarding the forehead.

Core Idea
Sujud on the turban coil is valid but disliked tanzih, provided the coil covers the forehead.

Sujud requires placing the forehead on the ground. But what if one wears a turban with a coil? The Hanafi school addresses this with a nuanced ruling: it is permissible but better avoided, unless there is a need. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning, including the proof from hadith and the critical condition that the coil must be on the forehead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Prostrating (sujud) while having a coiled part of the turban (al-koor) on the forehead. The ruling is: it is valid but disliked (makruh tanzih).
Dislike is tanzih, not tahrimi.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The text cites hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim: the companions prostrated on their garments in extreme heat. Also, al-Hasan reported that they prostrated on turbans. This indicates permissibility.
The hadith is sahih and used to show validity.
3
Understand the condition about forehead
Ibn Amir Hajj notes that the ruling applies only when the coil is on the forehead or part of it. If the coil is only on the head and the forehead touches nothing, sujud is invalid.
Many common people are lax about this.
4
Classify the dislike (karahah)
The text clarifies that the dislike is tanzih (non-prohibitive) because the Prophet himself prostrated on his turban sometimes. It becomes tahrimi only if one limits himself to something less (e.g., always avoiding the ground out of arrogance).
The author's wording caused confusion; the commentator resolves it.
5
Extend to attached barriers
The commentator extends the same ruling to any barrier attached to the body, like extra cloth or sleeve, as long as it is on a pure place.
This bridges to the next lesson on sleeves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His saying: (And it is disliked with one of them, or he coils his turban) i.e., it is disliked to prostrate upon it, and it is its coiling. It is said: kaar al-‘imamah wa kawwara: he coiled it on his head. This turban has ten coils and twenty coils. Likewise in al-Mughrib. It is with a fatha on the kaf as Ibn Amir Hajj recorded due to the hadith of the two Sahihs: we used to pray with the Prophet (peace be upon him) in severe heat, and when one of us could not place his forehead on the ground, he would spread his garment and prostrate on it. Al-Bukhari mentioned in his Sahih: al-Hasan said: the people used to prostrate on the turban and the cap. So that indicates validity; it is only disliked because it omits the ultimate reverence. What is in al-Tanjis regarding the reason of leaving reverence refers back to it, and abandoning reverence entirely invalidates the prayer. The scholar Ibn Amir Hajj gave a good note here: the validity of sujud on a coil is when the coil is on the forehead or part of it; but if it is only on the head and he prostrates on it without his forehead or nose touching the ground (according to the view requiring nose), then the prayer is invalid for not prostrating on the proper place. Many common people are lax about this and think it permissible. It is apparent that the dislike is tanzih due to the transmission of his action and his companions prostrating on the turban teaching permissibility, so it was not tahrimi. Abu Dawood narrated from Salih bin Haywan that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saw a man prostrating with his forehead covered by his turban, so he uncovered his forehead, indicating what is better and more complete. It is clear that the place of dislike is when there is no excuse; with an excuse, it is not disliked. In the author's words there is confusion, for he made the dislike for limiting to one of them and for prostrating on the coil the same, while we have verified that it is tahrimi in the first and tanzih in the second. So the intended meaning of dislike is a request to refrain, a non-emphatic request, whether or not there is sin. He indicated by 'coil' that any barrier between him and the ground that is attached to him has the same ruling, i.e., validity, as if he prostrated on the extra part of his garment or his sleeve on a pure place. As for dislike, in al-Dhakhira and al-Muhit: if he spreads his sleeve and prostrates on it, if he spreads it to protect his face from dust, it is disliked because it is a kind of arrogance; if he spreads it to protect his turban and clothes, it is not disliked. Qadi Khan stated that there is no harm in it and did not mention dislike. In al-Zad: if he prostrates on his sleeve, if there is dust or pebbles, it is not disliked because he repels harm from himself; if there is not, it is permissible but disliked. Reconciliation: what is in al-Dhakhira is when he fears no harm and intends elevation, so it is disliked tahriman; what Qadi Khan mentioned is when there is no elevation and he fears no harm, so it is disliked tanzihan, which goes back to contrary to better. The phrase 'no harm' often refers to something better left. What is in al-Zad is when there is no elevation and he fears harm, so it is permissible. We restricted it to the place being pure because if he spreads his sleeve on impurity, the correct view is impermissibility. His words indicate that if he prostrates on a barrier between him and the ground that is separate from him, it is valid a fortiori, like a prayer mat or mat. Al-Akmal stated in his report that it is better for the imam... and similarly in Mukhtar al-Sihah and other language books. So if 'side' (taraf) is interpreted as the aforementioned meaning, then the interpretation is valid and reconciliation is possible without difficulty, as similar instances occur frequently in their speech.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of prostration while wearing a coiled turban (koor) or using a garment as a barrier. The text begins by defining 'koor' as the coiled part of the turban on the head. It then cites hadith from Bukhari and Muslim where the companions prostrated on their garments in extreme heat, and from al-Hasan that they prostrated on turbans and caps, indicating validity. The dislike is due to leaving the ultimate reverence, but it is tanzih (better avoided) because the Prophet himself allowed it. However, if the turban is only on the head and the forehead does not touch the ground, the prayer is invalid. The commentator clarifies the distinction: prostrating on the coil when it is on the forehead is valid but disliked; if it is only on the head, invalid. Then the text delves into rulings on prostrating on sleeves or garments as barriers. The key is intention: if one spreads his sleeve to protect his face due to dust or heat, it is permissible (not disliked if harm is feared). If done out of arrogant avoidance of the ground, it is disliked tahriman. Qadi Khan sees no problem at all, while others differentiate. The reconciliation: if no harm and intended as elevation, tahrimi; if no harm and no elevation, tanzihi; if fear of harm, mubah. The barrier must be pure. The final lines address the earlier issue of 'side' (taraf) from the previous lesson, noting that linguistic interpretation supports the reconciliation.

Key Terms
الكور (al-koor): A coiled part of the turban on the head, upon which one might prostrate.
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyyah): A non-prohibitive dislike, better to avoid but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when is sujud on a turban coil considered invalid?
A) When the coil is on the forehead
B) When the coil is only on the head and the forehead does not touch anything
C) When there is an excuse like extreme heat
D) When the person intends to avoid the ground

Key Takeaway
Sujud on the turban coil is valid but better avoided when not needed, and it is crucial that the coil sits on the forehead.

Sujud on Sleeves and Attached Barriers
Ruling on sujud on sleeve with reconciliation of conflicting Hanafi texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three rulings for sujud on a sleeve based on intention and reconcile the different Hanafi texts.

Core Idea
Prostrating on a sleeve is disliked only if done arrogantly; it is permissible when needed to repel harm.

Beyond the turban, the scholars also discuss prostrating on one's sleeve. The ruling hinges on the intention: is one avoiding the ground out of arrogance or protecting oneself? This lesson explores the textual sources from al-Dhakhira, al-Muhit, Qadi Khan, and al-Zad, and shows how the commentator reconciles seemingly conflicting statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the key variable
The act is sujud on one's sleeve (or garment) while it is attached to the body. The key variable is intention and the presence of harm.
The ruling changes based on these factors.
2
Examine the three scenarios
The text presents three scenarios: (1) spreading sleeve to protect face from dust due to harm → not disliked; (2) spreading sleeve when no harm and no aim to elevate → disliked tanzih; (3) spreading sleeve to avoid ground out of arrogance → disliked tahrimi.
Also a fourth: when no harm and no elevation, Qadi Khan says no problem.
3
Analyze the reconciliation
The commentator reconciles the sources: al-Dhakhira's tahrimi applies when intention is arrogant and no harm; Qadi Khan's 'no harm' applies when no arrogance and no harm (tanzih); al-Zad's permissibility applies when there is fear of harm.
Thus, there is no real contradiction.
4
Apply the condition of purity
The sleeve must be on a pure place. If spread on impurity, sujud is invalid.
This is a general condition for all attached barriers.
5
Contrast with separate barriers
The text notes that a separate barrier (like a mat) is always valid and not disliked, a fortiori.
This is because it is not attached to the body.

Source Text

His saying: (And it is disliked with one of them, or he coils his turban) i.e., it is disliked to prostrate upon it, and it is its coiling. Prostration on the Turban: Validity and Dislike
Explains ruling of prostrating on the turban with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prostration on the turban and identify when it is valid or invalid based on the position of the coil.

Core Idea
Prostration on the turban is valid but disliked unless the coil is on the forehead.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common practice in prayer: prostrating on a turban. It clarifies that while the act is valid based on prophetic practice, it is disliked because it reduces humility. However, a critical condition is that the turban's coil must lie on the forehead; otherwise, the prostration is invalid. The text also distinguishes between two types of dislike, warning against common negligence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and initial ruling
The act is prostrating on the turban during prayer. The text first establishes that the prayer is valid based on hadith where companions prostrated on their garments in extreme heat.
The hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari is the primary evidence.
2
Understand the condition for validity
Validity depends on the coil of the turban being on the forehead or part of it. If the coil is only on the head and the forehead does not touch the ground, the prostration is invalid because the obligatory limb (forehead) has not met its place.
Ibn Amir Hajj emphasizes this condition, warning against common carelessness.
3
Differentiate the level of dislike
The text states the dislike is tanzihi (light) based on prophetic permission, not tahrimi (prohibited). The Prophet's action of uncovering a man's forehead indicated the better practice, not a ban.
Dislike applies only when there is no excuse (e.g., heat).
4
Resolve the apparent confusion in the matn
The author of the matn combined two cases under one dislike ruling. The commentary clarifies: restricting to one garment (tahrimi) vs. prostrating on the coil (tanzihi). This distinction is crucial for correct application.
The term 'karahah' in the matn required unpacking.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
In daily prayer, if one must prostrate on a turban due to heat or need, ensure the coil sits on the forehead. If not possible, it is better to uncover the forehead. The act remains valid but less preferred.
Modern headgear like caps or hoods may have analogous rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو العمامة وكورها دارها على رأسه، وهذه العمامة عشرة أكوار وعشرون كوراً. كذا في المغرب. وهو بفتح الكاف كما ضبطه ابن أمير حاج لحديث الصحيحين كنا نصلي مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في شدة الحر فإذا لم يستطع أحدنا أن يمكن جبهته من الأرض بسط ثوبه فسجد عليه وذكر البخاري في صحيحه قال الحسن: كان القوم يسجدون على العمامة والقلنسوة فدل ذلك على الصحة، وإنما كره لما فيه من ترك نهاية التعظيم. وما في التنجيس من التعليل بترك التعظيم راجع إليه والافتراك التعظيم أصلاً مبطل للصلاة، وقد نبه العلامة ابن أمير حاج هنا تنبيهاً حسناً وهو أن صحة السجود على الكور إذا كان الكور على الجبهة أو بعضها، أما إذا كان على الرأس فقط وسجد عليه ولم تصب جبهته والأرض على القول بتعيينها ولا أنفه على القول بعدم تعيينها، فإن الصلاة لا تصح لعدم السجود على محله، وكثير من العوام يتساهل في ذلك ويظن الجواز. وظاهر أن الكراهة تنزيهية لنقل فعله وأصحابه من السجود على العمامة تعليماً للجواز فلم تكن تحريمية، وقد أخرج أبو داود عن صالح بن حيوان أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى رجلاً يسجد وقد اعتم على جبهته فحسر عن جبهته إرشاداً لما الأفضل والأكمل. ولا يخفى أن محل الكراهة عند عدم العذر، أما معه فلا . وفي كلام المصنف اشتباه فإنه جعل الكراهة في الاقتصار على أحدهما وفي السجود على الكور واحدة، وقد حققنا أنها تحريمية في الأول تنزيهية في الثاني فيراد بالكراهة طلب الكف عن فعلها طلباً غير جازم، سواء كان في الفعل إثم أو لا
It is the turban and its coil, he wrapped it on his head. This turban has ten coils and twenty coils. So in al-Mughrib. It is with fatha on the kaf as Ibn Amir Hajj recorded it, due to the hadith in the two Sahihs: 'We used to pray with the Prophet (peace be upon him) in severe heat, and if one of us could not place his forehead on the ground, he would spread his garment and prostrate on it.' And al-Bukhari mentioned in his Sahih: al-Hasan said: 'The people used to prostrate on the turban and the cap.' So that indicates validity. It is only disliked because it involves abandoning the ultimate humility. And the explanation in al-Tanjis about abandoning humility refers to that, and abandoning humility entirely invalidates the prayer. The scholar Ibn Amir Hajj noted a good point here: that the validity of prostration on the coil is when the coil is on the forehead or part of it. But if it is only on the head and he prostrates on it, and his forehead does not touch the ground (according to the view that specifies the forehead) nor his nose (according to the view that does not specify), then the prayer is not valid due to the lack of prostration on its place. Many common people are careless about this and think it is permissible. It is apparent that the dislike is tanzihi because of the transmission of his action and his companions prostrating on the turban as a teaching of permissibility, so it is not tahrimi. It is not hidden that the place of dislike is when there is no excuse; as for with an excuse, then no. And in the author's words there is confusion, for he made the dislike the same for restricting to one of them and for prostrating on the coil. We have verified that it is tahrimi in the first and tanzihi in the second. By dislike is meant the request to refrain from doing it without firmness, whether there is sin in the action or not.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It explains the ruling of prostrating on the turban (عمامة) and its coils (كور). The text begins by describing the turban and its coils, then cites hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari to prove that prostration on the turban is valid: the companions would prostrate on their garments in extreme heat. The hadith of al-Hasan states that people prostrated on the turban and cap. So the prayer is valid. However, it is disliked (makruh) because it involves omitting the ultimate humility (تعظيم). The text clarifies that the dislike is tanzihi (lightly disliked) and not tahrimi (prohibited), based on the prophetic practice of allowing it. Then it gives an important condition: the coil must be on the forehead or part of it. If the coil is only on the head and the forehead does not touch the ground, the prostration is invalid because the obligated limb (forehead) has not met the ground. The text warns that common people are negligent about this. It then cites another hadith from Abu Dawud where the Prophet uncovered his forehead, showing the better practice. The dislike applies only when there is no excuse; with an excuse (e.g., extreme heat), there is no dislike. The author then resolves an apparent confusion: the author of the matn combined two cases into one ruling, but the commentary clarifies that one case is tahrimi and the other tanzihi.

Key Terms
عمامة (ʿimāmah): A turban worn on the head.
كور (kūr): A coil or fold of the turban.
كراهة تنزيهية (karāhah tanzīhiyyah): Light dislike; the act is permissible but better avoided without sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is prostration on the turban considered invalid?
A) When the coil is on the forehead
B) When the coil is only on the head and the forehead does not touch the ground
C) When the turban has more than ten coils
D) When the person has an excuse like extreme heat

Key Takeaway
Prostration on a turban is only valid if the coil is on the forehead; otherwise the prayer is invalid, and even when valid, it is lightly disliked without excuse.

The Ruling of Prostration on Connected Barriers (Sleeve, Garment)
Examines ruling of prostrating on connected barriers and reconciles opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling of prostration on a connected barrier based on the person's intention and circumstances, and apply the reconciled Hanafi position to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Prostration on a connected barrier is valid, but its dislike depends on intention and necessity.

In the previous lesson, we learned that prostrating on the coiled part of the turban is valid. The author now extends that ruling to any barrier connected to the body, such as the sleeve or excess garment. However, the text reveals a nuanced debate among Hanafi authorities about whether such an act is disliked, and if so, to what degree. This lesson unpacks the three main opinions and the reconciliation that yields the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
Recognize that the passage first affirms the validity (sahih) of prostration on any connected barrier, by analogy to the turban coil.
The principle of extension is qiyas: the sleeve is like the turban coil in being a connected barrier.
2
Recognize the Disagreement on Dislike
Note that three views are reported: al-Dhakhira/al-Muhit, Qadikhan, and al-Zad. Each has a different position on whether the act is disliked and why.
The disagreement is over the degree of karahah, not the validity.
3
Understand the Basis of Each View
For each opinion, identify the key factors: intention (arrogance vs. necessity) and the presence of harm (e.g., dust, heat).
Qadikhan's 'no harm' is interpreted as tanzihi, not absolute permissibility.
4
Follow the Reconciliation Method
Observe how the text reconciles the three views by assigning each to a specific factual scenario: (1) intending arrogance, no fear of harm → tahrimi; (2) no arrogance, no fear of harm → tanzihi; (3) no arrogance, fear of harm → mubah.
The reconciliation preserves the core ruling of validity while grading dislike.
5
Apply the Reconciled Position
Given a new scenario, identify the intention and the presence of harm, then determine the ruling (tahrimi, tanzihi, or mubah).
The condition that the ground under the barrier be pure is also essential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار بالكور إلى أن كل حائل بينه وبين الأرض متصل به فإن حكمه كذلك يعني الصحة كما لو سجد على فاضل ثوبه أو كمه على مكان طاهر. وأما الكراهة ففي الذخيرة والمحيط : إذا بسط كمه وسجد عليه إن بسط ليقي التراب عن وجهه كره ذلك لأن هذا نوع تكبر، وإن بسط ليقي التراب على عمامته و ثيابه لا يكره لعدمه. ونص قاضيخان على أن لا بأس به ولم يذكر كراهة. وفي الزاد: ولو سجد على كمه إن كان ثمة تراب أو حصاة لا يكره لأنه يدفع الأذى عن نفسه، وإن لم يكن جاز ويكره. والتوفيق بينهما بحمل ما في الذخيرة على ما إذا لم يخف ضرراً وقصد الترفع فيكره تحريماً، ويحمل ما ذكره قاضيخان على ما إذا لم يكن ترفعاً ولم يخف أذى فيكره تنزيهاً وهي ترجع إلى خلاف الأولى، وكلمة لا بأس غالباً فيما تركه أولى ويحمل ما في الزاد على ما إذا لم يكن ترفعاً وخاف الأذى فيكون مباحاً وقيدنا بكون ما تحته طاهراً لأنه لو بسط كمه على نجاسة فالأصح عدم الجواز ودل كلامه على أنه لو سجد على حائل بينه وبين الأرض منفصل عنه فإنه يصح بالأولى كالسجادة والحصير.
And he indicated by 'the coil' that every barrier between him and the ground that is connected to him has the same ruling, meaning validity, as if he prostrated on the excess of his garment or his sleeve on a pure place. As for the dislike: in al-Dhakhira and al-Muhit: if he spreads his sleeve and prostrates on it, if he spreads it to protect his face from dust, it is disliked because this is a type of arrogance; and if he spreads it to protect his turban and clothes from dust, it is not disliked because of the absence of arrogance. Qadikhan ruled that there is no harm in it and did not mention dislike. In al-Zad: if he prostrates on his sleeve, if there is dust or pebbles, it is not disliked because he repels harm from himself; if there is not, it is permissible and disliked. The reconciliation between them is by carrying what is in al-Dhakhira to the case where he does not fear harm and intends elevation, so it is disliked tahriman; and what Qadikhan mentioned is carried to where there is no elevation and he does not fear harm, so it is disliked tanzihan, which returns to khilaf al-awla; and the phrase 'no harm' is mostly used for what is better to leave. And what is in al-Zad is carried to where there is no elevation and he fears harm, so it is permissible. And we conditioned that what is under it be pure, because if he spreads his sleeve on impurity, the correct view is non-permissibility. And his speech indicates that if he prostrates on a barrier between him and the ground that is separate from him, it is valid a fortiori, like a prayer mat or a reed mat.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with multiple opinions. It begins by extending the principle from the turban coil to any barrier connected to the person (like the excess of a garment or the sleeve). Prostration on such a barrier is valid, but the dislike depends on the intention. The text reports three views: (1) from al-Dhakhira and al-Muhit: if one spreads the sleeve to protect the face, it is disliked (tahrimi) due to arrogance; if to protect the turban/clothes, not disliked. (2) Qadikhan says there is no harm (no dislike). (3) al-Zad distinguishes: if there is dust/harm, no dislike; if no harm, permissible but disliked. The reconcilation: the first case (intending elevation/arrogance) is tahrimi; Qadikhan's case (no arrogance, no fear of harm) is tanzihi (khilaf al-awla); al-Zad's case (fear of harm, no arrogance) is mubah (permissible). The text also adds the condition that the place under the sleeve must be pure (tahir). Finally, it states that a disconnected barrier (like a mat) is valid a fortiori (بالأولى).

Key Terms
حائل (ḥāʾil): A barrier between the forehead and the ground.
كراهة تحريمية (karāhah taḥrīmiyyah): Prohibited dislike; sinful to do.
كراهة تنزيهية (karāhah tanzīhiyyah): Disliked but not sinful; better to avoid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciliation in the text, when is prostration on the sleeve considered mubah (permissible)?
A) When the person intends arrogance
B) When there is no fear of harm and no arrogance
C) When there is fear of harm and no arrogance
D) When the sleeve is spread on impure ground

Key Takeaway
Prostration on a connected barrier is valid; the degree of dislike (tahrimi, tanzihi, mubah) depends on the person's intention and the presence of harm.

The Imam's Prayer Mat: A Ruling That Changes with Time
Discusses whether the imam should use a prayer mat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's use of a prayer mat and explain how the preferred practice shifted due to social context.

Core Idea
The imam's prayer mat ruling adapts to the community's care for purity.

The use of a prayer mat (sajjadah) by the imam seems like a minor detail, but it reveals a deeper Hanafi principle: rulings can change based on the condition of the people. This lesson traces how the preferred practice moved from leaving the mat to using it, as people became lax about cleanliness. You will learn not only the ruling but also the reasoning behind its evolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original preferred practice
Find the statement from al-Akmal: the first (i.e., preferred) for the imam was to leave the prayer mat (i.e., pray directly on the ground). Understand that this was to avoid causing hardship on common people who might think a mat is required.
This was the earlier view in a time when purity was generally maintained.
2
Understand the rationale behind the original view
The imam (and those followed like a mufti) should avoid actions that might burden others. If the imam uses a mat, common people might feel compelled to use one even if it is difficult or unnecessary.
The principle is to facilitate, not to cause hardship (haraj).
3
See the change in preference over time
Al-Bazzazi applied that ruling to his own time. But the commentator notes that in his later time, people have become negligent about purity (tahara), so it is better for the imam to use a mat to ensure cleanliness.
The same principle of preventing hardship now leads to the opposite recommendation.
4
Recognize the governing principle
The underlying principle is that prostration is valid on clean ground or anything similar that the forehead can press into. The mat is permissible as long as it is pure. The change is about what is advisable (first), not what is obligatory.
This is a clear example of how social conditions affect preferred practice (adab) while the hukm (mubah) remains constant.
5
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider an imam in a mosque with clean carpet. Should he use a prayer mat? In a community where people are careful about purity, leaving the mat may be preferred. But if people are careless, using the mat is better. The imam should assess the need.
The modern application requires observing the actual condition of the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الأكمل في تقريره أن الأولى للإمام الشيء. ومثله في مختار الصحاح وغيرهما من كتب اللغة. فإذا كان الطرف بالمعنى المذكور فالحمل حجة لا بعد فيه إذ مثله وقع كثيراً في كلامهم . الخلوة ومن يقتدي به كالمفتي ترك السجادة حتى لا يحمل العوام على ما فيه حرج عليهم بخلافه في يقتدي به وحمله البزازي على زمانهم أما في زماننا فالأولى الصلاة عليها لما أن الناس تهاونوا في أمر الطهارة، والأصل كما أنه يجوز السجود على الأرض يجوز على ما هو بمعنى الأرض مما تجد جبهته حجمه وتستقر عليه .
And al-Akmal mentioned in his report that the preferred practice for the imam is to leave the prayer mat. Similar is in Mukhtar al-Sihah and other language books. So if 'al-taraf' is in the mentioned meaning, then the burden is a proof, no difficulty in it, for similar occurs often in their speech. (New line) The imam and one who is followed like the mufti should leave the prayer mat so that he does not cause the common people to fall into hardship, contrary to the one who is followed. And al-Bazzazi carried it to their time; but in our time, it is better to pray on it because people have become negligent about purity. The principle is: just as it is permissible to prostrate on the ground, it is permissible on what is similar to the ground from that which the forehead finds its hardness and rests upon.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about the imam's use of a prayer mat (سجادة). It cites al-Akmal that the preferred practice for the imam is to leave the prayer mat (i.e., pray directly on the ground) to avoid causing hardship on common people who may think it is required. However, al-Bazzazi relates this to their time. In the commentator's own time (likely later), people have become careless about purity (طهارة), so it is better for the imam to use a prayer mat for cleanliness. The principle is: prostration on the ground is permissible, and similarly on anything that the forehead can press into and settle on, as long as it is pure. The section ends with the definition of 'finding hardness' (حجم) which will be detailed next.

Key Terms
إمام (imām): The leader of congregational prayer.
سجادة (sajjādah): A prayer mat or rug used for prostration.
حرج (ḥaraj): Hardship, difficulty, or constraint; in legal context, a burden that should be avoided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is it better in the commentator's time for the imam to use a prayer mat?
A) To follow the Sunnah
B) Because people have become careless about purity
C) To avoid arrogance
D) Because the ground is usually impure

Key Takeaway
The imam's use of a prayer mat is permissible, and the preferred practice depends on the community's care for purity, adapting to avoid hardship.

The Condition of 'Finding Hardness' for Valid Prostration
Defines the condition of 'finding hardness' and lists various surfaces for valid prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of 'finding hardness' (wijdān al-ḥajm) for prostration and apply it to determine the validity of prostration on various surfaces.

Core Idea
Prostration is valid only when the forehead finds firmness on a surface that does not allow further sinking.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi ruling on the required firmness of the prostration place. The text from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq expands on the condition of 'finding hardness' and applies it to numerous surfaces, from carpets and grains to snow and human backs. Understanding this condition is essential for ensuring the validity of salah in various situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Condition
Understand the definition of 'finding hardness' (wijdān al-ḥajm): when the forehead exerts force, it does not sink further into the surface.
This is the key test for surfaces that are not natural earth.
2
List the Surfaces and Their Base
Go through the passage and list each surface mentioned (carpet, mat, wheat, barley, bed, cart, animal back, human back, dead body, rice, millet, maize, snow, grass, straw, cotton, turban coil, cap edge, small stone). Note whether the surface is on the ground or mobile.
The base matters: if on the ground, it's generally valid; if on an animal or person, extra conditions apply.
3
Apply the Hardness Condition
For each surface, determine whether the forehead can find firmness. For example, grains in a sack compress and provide hardness; loose grains do not. Snow must be packed; soft cotton does not provide firmness.
Exceptions arise when the surface itself is solid (like a packed mattress) or when a barrier prevents sinking.
4
Examine Special Cases
Study the rulings for prostration on a person's back (requires necessity, same prayer, and the person must be prostrating on the ground) and on a dead body (invalid if hardness of body felt). Note the four conditions.
These cases show how the condition interacts with additional requirements.
5
Summarize the General Rule
Conclude that validity hinges on the forehead finding a firm, stable surface. The height difference between the place of prostration and feet must not exceed two upright bricks (quarter cubit each).
This rule unifies many scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتفسير وجدان الحجم أن الساجد لو بالغ لا يتسفل رأسه أبلغ من ذلك فيصح السجود على الطنفسة والحصير والحنطة والشعير والسرير والعجلة إن كانت على الأرض لأنه يجد الأرض بخلاف ما إذا كانت على ظهر الحيوان لأن قرارها حينئذ على الحيوان كالبساط الأشجار. ولو سجد على ظهر رجل إن كان للضرورة بأن لم يجد موضعاً . الأرض يسحد عليه والمسجود على ظهره في الصلاة جاز، وإن لم يكن في الصلاة أو فرجه لا يجوز لعدمها. وقيد في الواقعات أن تكون صلاتهما متحدة حتى لو سجد على ظهر من يصلي صلاة أخرى لا يجوز لعدمها وعليه مشى في الخلاصة وفتح القدير : وشرط في المجتبى شرطاً آخر وهو أن يكون المسجود على ظهره ساجداً على الأرض، فلو سجد على ظهر مصل ساجد على ظهر مصل لا يجوز فالشروط أربعة . وفي المحيط : ولو سجد على ظهر الميت وعليه لبد، إن وجد حجم الميت لم يجز لأنه سجد على الميت وإن لم يكن يجد حجمه جاز لأنه سجد على اللبد ولو سجد على الأرز أو الجاورس أو الذرة لا يجوز لعدم استقرار الجبهة عليها حتى لو كان الأرز في الجوالق فإنه يجوز لأنه يجد الحجم بواسطة انكباسه كما ذكره في منية المصلي. وإن سجد على الثلج إن لم يلبده وكأن يغيب وجهه ولا يجد حجمه يجز وإن لبد جاز. وكذا إذا ألقي الحشيش فسجد عليه إن وجد حجمه جاز وإلا فلا، وكذا التبن والقطن. ومن هنا يعلم جواز أداء الصلاة على الطراحة القطن فإن وجد الحجم جاز وإلا فلا. وهذا القيد لا بد منه في السجود على كور العمامة وطرف القلنسوة كما صرح به في المجتبى. وفي منية المصلي ولو أن موضع السجود ارفع من موضع القدمين مقدار لبنتين منصوبتين جاز وإن كان أكثر لا يجوز أراد لبنة بخارى وهو ربع ذراع اهـ. وفي التنجيس : ولو سجد على حجر صغير إن كان أكثر الجبهة على الأرض يجوز وإلا فلا. وهكذا في كثير من الكتب معزياً إلى نصير وفيه بحث، لأن اسم السجود يصدق بوضع شيء من الجبهة على
And the explanation of 'finding hardness' is that if the one prostrating exerts force, his head does not sink further than that. So prostration is valid on a carpet, a reed mat, wheat, barley, a bed, and a cart if they are on the ground, because he finds the ground, unlike if they are on the back of an animal, because then their base is on the animal like a rug on trees. And if he prostrates on the back of a person, if out of necessity because he does not find a place on the ground to prostrate on, and the one prostrated on is in prayer, it is valid; if not in prayer or if it is a private part, it is not valid due to the absence of necessity. It is conditioned in al-Waqi'at that their prayers be the same (i.e., both in the same prayer), so if he prostrates on the back of one praying a different prayer, it is not allowed due to the absence of unity. This is followed in al-Khulasa and Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Mujtaba another condition is added: that the one prostrated on is prostrating on the ground; if he prostrates on the back of a person who is prostrating on the back of another, it is not valid. So there are four conditions. In al-Muhit: if he prostrates on the back of a dead body on which there is felt, if he finds the hardness of the dead body, it is not valid because he prostrated on the dead body; if he does not find its hardness, it is valid because he prostrated on the felt. And if he prostrates on rice, millet, or maize, it is not valid due to the lack of stability of the forehead on them, unless the rice is in a sack, then it is valid because he finds hardness through its compression, as mentioned in Munyat al-Musalli. And if he prostrates on snow, if he does not pack it and his face sinks and he does not find hardness, it is not valid; if he packs it, it is valid. Similarly, if grass is spread and he prostrates on it: if he finds hardness, it is valid; otherwise no. Similarly, straw and cotton. From this, it is known that it is permissible to perform prayer on a cotton mattress: if he finds hardness, it is valid; otherwise no. This condition is necessary in prostration on the coil of the turban and the edge of the cap, as stated in al-Mujtaba. In Munyat al-Musalli: if the place of prostration is higher than the place of the feet by the amount of two upright bricks, it is valid; if more, it is not valid. He meant a brick of Bukhara, which is a quarter of a cubit. In al-Tanjis: if he prostrates on a small stone, if most of the forehead is on the ground, it is valid; otherwise no. This is mentioned in many books attributed to Nasir, but there is discussion, because the name 'prostration' applies by placing part of the forehead on...
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings defining the condition of 'finding hardness' (وجدان الحجم) for the place of prostration. It explains that the forehead must press into a surface that does not allow the head to sink further. Valid surfaces include carpets, mats, grains like wheat and barley if stable, a bed, and a cart provided they are on the ground (i.e., the base is on earth). If on an animal's back, invalid because the base moves. Prostration on a living person's back is valid only out of necessity with several conditions: the prosterner cannot find ground, the back-person must be in the same prayer, and that person must be prostrating on the ground (not on another's back). These amount to four conditions. Prostration on a dead body is invalid if the hardness of the body is felt; if a barrier like felt prevents it, it is valid. Grains like rice are invalid unless contained in a sack where they compress and provide firmness. Snow is valid if packed to provide hardness. Grass, straw, and cotton require finding hardness; a cotton mattress is valid only if it gives firm support. The same condition applies to the turban coil and cap edge. The text also gives a rule: the place of prostration must not be more than two 'bricks' (cube-shaped bricks, quarter cubit each) higher than the feet. Prostration on a small stone is valid if most of the forehead is on the ground (not the stone). The passage ends with a note that there is discussion about this last point because prostration requires placing part of the forehead on the ground.

Key Terms
وجدان الحجم (wijdān al-ḥajm): The forehead pressing into a surface that does not allow further sinking; the surface provides firmness.
جوالق (jawāliq): A large sack or bag, e.g., containing rice.
لبنة بخارى (labanat bukhārā): A brick of Bukhara, used as a measurement equal to a quarter of a cubit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum permissible height difference between the place of prostration and the feet?
A) One handspan
B) Two upright bricks (quarter cubit each)
C) One brick
D) No difference allowed

Key Takeaway
The forehead must find firmness (wijdān al-ḥajm) on a stable surface for prostration to be valid, with specific rules for unusual surfaces like backs and snow.

Prostration on the Back of a Person in Prayer: Conditions for Validity
Ruling on prostration on a person's back with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi conditions for the validity of prostration on a person's back during prayer and apply them to hypothetical scenarios.

Core Idea
Prostration on another person is permissible only under four precise conditions, all rooted in necessity and shared worship.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the Hanafi ruling on prostration upon the back of another person is presented not as an absolute prohibition but as a permitted act under restricted conditions. The author gathers conditions from al-Waqi'at and al-Mujtaba, resulting in four requirements. Understanding these conditions is essential for distinguishing valid exceptional cases from invalid ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The ruling is that prostration on another person's back is permissible (ja'iz) under conditions.
The default ruling is not permissible without meeting all conditions.
2
List the four conditions
Condition 1: Necessity (darurah) – no space on the ground. Condition 2: The one prostrated on is in prayer. Condition 3: Both prayers are the same (identical prayer unit). Condition 4: The one prostrated on is prostrating directly on the ground.
Conditions 1-3 are from al-Waqi'at; condition 4 is from al-Mujtaba.
3
Understand the source of each condition
The text explicitly cites al-Waqi'at for the first three and al-Mujtaba for the fourth, showing the process of gathering conditions from different works.
This demonstrates how later Hanafi scholars compile and harmonize rulings.
4
Apply the conditions to examples
Consider a scenario where the mosque floor is completely covered and no space exists. If the person prostrates on the back of someone praying the same prayer and who is themselves prostrating on the ground, it is valid. If any condition is missing, e.g., the person prostrated on is not praying, it is invalid.
The key is to check each condition sequentially.
5
Note the consequence of missing a condition
If any condition is absent, prostration on the back is not permissible (la yajuz). This could affect the validity of the prayer if done intentionally or require sajdah sahwu if done inadvertently.
In severe crowding, many scholars advise avoiding this practice altogether.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سجد على ظهر رجل إن كان للضرورة بأن لم يجد موضعاً على الأرض يسجد عليه والمسجود على ظهره في الصلاة جاز، وإن لم يكن في الصلاة أو فرج [؟] لا يجوز لعدمها. وقيد في الواقعات أن تكون صلاتهما متحدة حتى لو سجد على ظهر من يصلي صلاة أخرى لا يجوز لعدمها وعليه مشى في الخلاصة وفتح القدير : وشرط في المجتبى شرطاً آخر وهو أن يكون المسجود على ظهره ساجداً على الأرض، فلو سجد على ظهر مصل ساجد على ظهر مصل لا يجوز فالشروط أربعة.
If he prostrates on the back of a man, if out of necessity such that he does not find a place on the ground to prostrate on, and the one prostrated on is in prayer, it is permissible. But if he is not in prayer, or on his thigh [?], it is not permissible due to lack of necessity. It is conditioned in al-Waqi'at that their prayers be united, so that if he prostrates on the back of someone praying a different prayer, it is not permissible. Al-Mujtaba added another condition: that the one prostrated on be prostrating on the ground, so if he prostrates on the back of a person prostrating on the back of another, it is not permissible. Thus the conditions are four.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with conditions regarding prostration on the back of another person during prayer. The ruling is that such prostration is permissible only under four conditions. First, it must be out of necessity, meaning the person cannot find any suitable spot on the ground to prostrate. Second, the person being prostrated upon must also be engaged in prayer. Third, both prayers must be the same (i.e., they are performing the same obligatory prayer, likely in congregation). Fourth, the one being prostrated upon must be prostrating directly on the ground, not on another person. These conditions are gathered from two sources: al-Waqi'at provides the first three, and al-Mujtaba adds the fourth. The Hanafi position is that if any condition is missing, the prostration is invalid.

Key Terms
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity: the condition that the person cannot find any other place to prostrate on the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many conditions are required for the validity of prostration on the back of a person in Salah according to this passage?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Prostration on the back of another person in prayer is valid in the Hanafi school only when all four conditions of necessity, shared prayer, unified intent, and direct ground prostration are met.

Valid Surfaces for Prostration: The Condition of Hajm
Expansion of conditions for valid prostration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid prostration surface according to the Hanafi school, including the requirement of hajm, the height limit, the majority of forehead rule, and the ruling on body parts.

Core Idea
Prostration is valid only when the forehead finds firmness (hajm) and settles.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the Hanafi conditions for the place of prostration (sajdah). The central requirement is that the forehead must find volume (hajm) — a firm surface that prevents further sinking. The author lists numerous examples and clarifies edge cases, including height differences, loose substances, and prostration on parts of one's own body.

Guided Path
1
Understand the core principle of hajm
Identify the definition: the forehead must find a volume (hajm) when pressing, meaning the surface is firm enough that the head does not sink further.
This is the key criterion throughout.
2
Analyze the examples to see how hajm applies
Work through the examples: valid on ground, rug, mat, wheat, barley, bed, cart; invalid on animal back, loose rice without sack, unpacked snow. Note that loose substances become valid if compressed.
Focus on the reasoning for each.
3
Note the height limit and majority of forehead rule
The place of prostration cannot be more than two standing bricks (quarter cubit) higher than the feet. When prostrating on a small stone, the majority of the forehead must be on the ground; placing only a part is insufficient.
The author critiques Nasir's view that any part suffices.
4
Distinguish rulings for palm, thigh, and knee
Prostration on one's own palm is valid on the strongest view; on the thigh only with an excuse; on the knee is never valid, though an excuse may suffice in necessity.
This is because the knee does not provide enough surface area.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل كما أنه يجوز السجود على الأرض يجوز على ما هو بمعنى الأرض مما تجد جبهته حجمه وتستقر عليه . وتفسير وجدان الحجم أن الساجد لو بالغ لا يتسفل رأسه أبلغ من ذلك فيصح السجود على الطنفسة والحصير والحنطة والشعير والسرير والعجلة إن كانت على الأرض لأنه يجد الأرض بخلاف ما إذا كانت على ظهر الحيوان لأن قرارها حينئذ على الحيوان كالبساط الأشجار. ولو سجد على الأرز أو الجاورس أو الذرة لا يجوز لعدم استقرار الجبهة عليها حتى لو كان الأرز في الجوالق فإنه يجوز لأنه يجد الحجم بواسطة انكباسه كما ذكره في منية المصلي. وإن سجد على الثلج إن لم يلبده وكأن يغيب وجهه ولا يجد حجمه يجز وإن لبد جاز. وكذا إذا ألقي الحشيش فسجد عليه إن وجد حجمه جاز وإلا فلا، وكذا التبن والقطن. ومن هنا يعلم جواز أداء الصلاة على الطراحة القطن فإن وجد الحجم جاز وإلا فلا. وهذا القيد لا بد منه في السجود على كور العمامة وطرف القلنسوة كما صرح به في المجتبى. وفي منية المصلي ولو أن موضع السجود ارفع من موضع القدمين مقدار لبنتين منصوبتين جاز وإن كان أكثر لا يجوز أراد لبنة بخارى وهو ربع ذراع. وفي التنجيس : ولو سجد على حجر صغير إن كان أكثر الجبهة على الأرض يجوز وإلا فلا. وهكذا في كثير من الكتب معزياً إلى نصير وفيه بحث، لأن اسم السجود يصدق بوضع شيء من الجبهة على الأرض ولا دليل على اشتراط أكثرها كما قالوا يكفي في القدمين وضع أصبع واحدة، ولهذا قال في المجتبى : سجد على طرف من أطراف جبهته جاز. ثم نقل كلام نصير تضعيفه. نعم وضع أكثرها واجب للمواظبة على تمكين الجبهة من الأرض، وعلى تسليم الأكثر شرط فيجب أنه إذا كان ما أصاب الحجر والأرض يبلغ أكثرها يجوز لا أنه لا يعتد بما أصاب الحجر أصلاً كما ظاهر كلامهم والله الموفق للصواب. وقيد بكون الحائل تبعاً لأن الحائل لو كان بعضه، فإن كان كفه يجوز على الأصح، وإن كان فخذه يجوز بعذر لا بغيره على الصحيح، وإن كان ركبته لا يجوز مطلقاً من غير خلاف يعلم لكن إن كان بعذر كفاه باعتبار ما في ضمنه من الإيمان وكان عدم الخلاف فيه لكون السجود يقع على حرف الركبة لا يأخذ قدر الواجب من الجبهة على ما قدمناه عن التنجيس وفي فتح القدير، والذي ينبغي ترجيح الفساد على الكف والفخذ.
The principle is that just as prostration on the ground is permissible, it is permissible on what is akin to the ground, such that the forehead finds its volume (hajm) and settles on it. The interpretation of finding volume is that if the one prostrating tries to press further, his head does not go lower than that. Thus prostration is valid on a rug, a mat, wheat, barley, a bed, and a cart if they are on the ground because he finds the ground; contrary to if they are on an animal's back, because their stability is then on the animal like a rug on trees. If he prostrates on rice, millet, or maize, it is not valid due to the lack of stability of the forehead, unless the rice is in a sack, then it is valid because he finds volume through its compression. If he prostrates on snow, if he does not pack it and his face sinks and he does not find volume, it is not valid; if he packs it, it is valid. Similarly, if grass is thrown and he prostrates on it, if he finds volume it is valid, otherwise not; likewise straw and cotton. From here it is known that praying on a cotton mattress is permissible if he finds volume, otherwise not. This condition is necessary for prostration on the coiled part of the turban and the edge of the cap. In Munyat al-Musalli: if the place of prostration is higher than the place of the feet by the amount of two standing bricks, it is valid; if more, not valid; he intended a brick of Bukhara, which is a quarter cubit. In al-Tanqih: if he prostrates on a small stone, if the majority of the forehead is on the ground, it is valid; otherwise not. And so in many books, attributed to Nasir, but there is discussion, because the term prostration applies by placing any part of the forehead on the ground, and there is no evidence for requiring the majority; they said a single finger suffices for the feet. Hence in al-Mujtaba: if he prostrates on a part of his forehead, it is valid. Then he transmitted Nasir's statement as weak. Indeed, placing the majority is recommended (wajib) for regularity of pressing the forehead on the ground, and accepting the majority as a condition means that if that which touches the stone and ground reaches the majority, it is valid; it is not as if what touches the stone is not counted at all, as their words apparently imply. And it is conditioned that the barrier (ha'il) be subordinate, because if the barrier is part of him: if it is his palm, it is valid on the strongest view; if his thigh, it is valid with an excuse but not otherwise on the correct view; if his knee, it is absolutely not valid with no known disagreement, but if there is an excuse, it may suffice considering the faith within him, and the lack of disagreement is because prostration falls on the edge of the knee, not taking the required amount of the forehead. In Fath al-Qadir, the correct view is to favor invalidity for palm and thigh.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage lays out the fundamental principle that valid prostration requires the forehead to find a firm surface (hajm) that prevents further descent. The author then provides numerous examples. Prostration is valid on surfaces that are fixed directly on the ground like rugs, mats, grain, beds, and carts, because the forehead can press and settle. It is not valid if the surface is on an animal's back. For loose substances like rice, millet, or maize, it is not valid unless they are in a container that compresses to provide a firm surface. Snow requires packing, grass and cotton require the forehead to find firmness. The height difference between the prostration place and feet is limited to two standing bricks (about a quarter cubit). For a small stone, the ruling depends on whether most of the forehead is on the ground; the author notes a discussion with Nasir's view that any part suffices, but the relied-upon view is that most forehead must be on the ground as a condition for validity, though placing most is wajib. Finally, if one prostrates on a part of his own body (palm, thigh, knee), the ruling varies: palm is valid on the strongest view, thigh only with excuse, knee never valid per known view, but may be excused in necessity.

Key Terms
حجم (hajm): The firmness or volume of the surface such that when the forehead presses, it does not sink further and remains stable.
حائل (ha'il): A barrier between the forehead and the ground, which may be part of the body or something else.
لبنة بخارى (labnat Bukhara): A brick standard used in Bukhara, approximately a quarter cubit (about 23 cm).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the minimum amount of forehead that must be on the ground when prostrating on a small stone?
A) Any part
B) The majority
C) The whole forehead
D) At least one square inch

Key Takeaway
For prostration to be valid, the forehead must find a firm surface (hajm), the place must not be too high, and if on a small stone, the majority of the forehead must be on the ground.
